The Prophet Muhammad as Seal and Universal Messenger
Commentary on two lines about Muhammad being seal and universal messenger.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet Muhammad is the final prophet and how his mission extends to all beings, addressing the apparent challenge of Jesus' descent.

Core Idea
Muhammad is the seal and universal prophet; Jesus follows his law.

This passage from Tuhfat al-Mureed explains two key characteristics of Prophet Muhammad: his being the seal of the prophets and the universality of his mission. The commentator addresses a common objection about Jesus descending at the end of time, clarifying that Jesus acts within Muhammad's sharia. Understanding these points strengthens faith in the finality and universality of his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the commentator parses each line of the poem.
The text uses classical Arabic grammatical analysis.
2
Identify the two main characteristics
Find where the commentator explains 'seal of the prophets' and 'universality of mission'. Note the use of the restriction (qasr) with the implied ba'.
This is a key linguistic tool in kalam.
3
Understand the objection and answer about Jesus
Read the part about Jesus's descent. Understand why it does not contradict sealing prophethood.
The answer depends on Jesus being a follower, not a new prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تحفة المريد على جوهرة التوحيد سيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم خاتم الأنبياء] ٦٩ - وَخُصَّ خَيْرُ الخَلْقِ أَنْ قَدْ تَمَّمَا بِهِ الجَميعَ رَبُّنا وعَمَّمَا قوله : (وَخُصَّ خَيْرُ الخَلْقِ) ببناء الفعل للمفعول، و(خير الخلق): نائب فاعل الذي هو الله ، والأصل: وخصّ الله خير الخلق ؛ أي: أفضلهم وهو نبينا محمد ، و (خيرُ) أفعل تفضيل أصله (أخير ) كـ ( أكرم)، حذفت منه الهمزة لكثرة الاستعمال. وقوله : (أَنْ) قَدْ نَمَّمَا بِهِ الجَميعَ رَبُّنا أي: بأن ختم ربنا به صلى الله عليه وسلم جميع الأنبياء، فالباء مقدرة وهي داخلة على المقصور، فتتميم جميع الأنبياء مقصور عليه صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يتعداه إلى غيره، قال تعالى: ﴿وَخَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّ ) [الأحزاب: (٤٠] ، ويلزم منه ختم المرسلين؛ لأنه يلزم من ختم الأعم ختم الأخص من غير عكس، ولا يُشكل ذلك بنزول سيدنا عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام في آخر الزمان؛ لأنه إنما ينزل حاكماً بشريعة نبينا ومُتَّبعاً له، ولا يُنافي ذلك أنه حين نزوله يحكم برفع الجزية عن أهل الكتاب، ولا يقبل منهم إلا الإسلام أو السيف؛ لأن نبينا أخبرنا بأنها مُغيَّاة إلى نزول عيسى، فحكمه بذلك إنما هو بشريعة نبينا . وخصائصه لا تنحصر حدا ولا عدا ولكن المهم منها ما ذكره المصنف. ، عموم بعثه واتباعُ عيسى له بعد نزولِهِ] قوله : (وَعَمَّمَا) بِعْتَتَهُ) أي : وخُصَّ أيضاً بأن عمَّم ربُّنا بعثته، فالباء مقدرة وهي داخلة على المقصور كما في الذي قبله، فتعميم البعثة مقصور عليه صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يتعداه إلى غيره فأرسله الله إلى جميع المكلفين من الثقلين إرسال تكليف اتفاقاً . وأما الملائكة فقد تقدَّم فيهم الخلافُ، والأصح (۱) أنه مُرسَلٌ إليهم إرسال
Tuhfat al-Mureed Ala Jawharat al-Tawhid. Our master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, is the Seal of the Prophets. 69 - 'And the best of creation was singled out that our Lord completed all through him and made universal.' His saying 'and the best of creation was singled out' with the verb built for the object, and 'the best of creation' is the agent of the verb which is God. The original is: 'And God singled out the best of creation', i.e. the most excellent of them, and he is our Prophet Muhammad. 'Khayru' is an elative, originally 'akhyar' like 'akram', its hamza deleted due to frequent use. His saying 'an qad tammama bihi al-jami'a rabbuna' means that our Lord sealed all the prophets through him, may God bless him and grant him peace. The letter ba' is implied and enters upon the one restricted. So the completion of all prophets is restricted to him, may God bless him and grant him peace, not extending beyond him. God said: 'and seal of the prophets' [Q. 33:40], and from this follows the sealing of messengers, because sealing the general entails sealing the specific without the reverse. This is not problematic because of the descent of our master Jesus, peace be upon him, at the end of time, because he only descends as a judge ruling by our Prophet's law and a follower of him. It does not contradict that at his descent he will rule to lift the jizya from the People of the Book and accept from them only Islam or the sword, because our Prophet informed us that it is limited until Jesus' descent, so his ruling in that is only by our Prophet's law. His special characteristics are not limited in number or count, but the important ones are what the author mentioned. Universality of his mission and Jesus' following him after his descent. His saying 'wa 'ammama bi'thatihi' means: he was also singled out in that our Lord made his mission universal. So the letter ba' is implied and enters upon the one restricted as in the previous instance. So the universality of the mission is restricted to him, may God bless him and grant him peace, not extending to others. God sent him to all morally responsible beings from the two heavy kinds (jinn and humans) as a mission of obligation by consensus. As for angels, there is previous disagreement about them, and the most correct is that he was sent to them as a mission
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on two lines from the Jawharat al-Tawhid concerning the special characteristics of Prophet Muhammad: his being the seal of the prophets and the universality of his mission. The commentator begins by parsing the first line: 'Wa khussa khayru al-khalqi' (And the best of creation was singled out). The verb is passive, and 'khayru al-khalqi' is the agent (na'ib fa'il). The original active would be 'God singled out the best of creation'. 'Khayr' is an elative form with the hamza deleted for frequency. The phrase 'an qad tammama bihi al-jami'a rabbuna' means that God completed/ sealed all prophets through him. The letter 'ba' in 'bihi' is implied and restricts the completion to him alone. This is supported by Q. 33:40. The sealing implies that of messengers as well, as the general encompasses the specific. Then an objection is raised: how does Jesus's descent at the end of time not contradict this? The answer is that Jesus descends as a follower of Muhammad's law, not as a new prophet. He will rule according to that law, including lifting the jizya, as foretold by Muhammad—so he acts within Muhammad's sharia. The commentator notes that the Prophet's special characteristics are countless, but only important ones are mentioned. Next, the second line 'wa 'ammama' is explained: he was also singled out by the universality of his mission. Again, the implied 'ba' restricts it to him. He was sent to all morally responsible beings (jinn and humans) by obligation. There is disagreement about angels: some say he was sent to them too, and the most correct view is that he was sent to them as well (the text ends mid-sentence).

خاتم النبيين
تمم
عمم
نزول عيسى
بعثة
ثقلين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Jesus descending as a judge at the end of time contradicts the finality of Muhammad's prophethood.
Correction: The commentator clarifies that Jesus will descend not as a new prophet but as a follower of Muhammad's law, ruling by it. Thus, it does not violate the seal.

Checkpoint
How does the commentator resolve the apparent problem of Jesus descending at the end of time with Muhammad being the seal of prophets?
A) Jesus will be a prophet independently
B) Jesus will judge by his own gospel
C) Jesus will follow Muhammad's sharia and rule by it
D) Jesus will not descend at all

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad is the final prophet and was sent to all creation, and the descent of Jesus only confirms that as he rules by Muhammad's law.

The Seal of the Prophets and the Descent of Isa
Commentary proving Muhammad is seal of prophets and answering objection about Isa's descent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the belief that Muhammad is the seal of the prophets is consistent with the prophesied descent of Isa at the end of time.

Core Idea
Muhammad is the final prophet; Isa returns as a follower, not a new prophet.

The Qur'an explicitly calls Muhammad the 'Seal of the Prophets' (Q. 33:40). Yet some wonder about the descent of Prophet Isa, who is also a prophet. This passage from a classical commentary resolves the tension by explaining that Isa will descend not as a prophet bringing a new law, but as a ruler following Muhammad's sharia. Let's examine the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the original Arabic and its translation. Notice the grammatical points about the verb and the superlative.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage states that Muhammad is the seal of all prophets, meaning no prophet after him brings a new message.
3
Understand the objection
The descent of Isa seems to pose a problem. What is the objection? Why would someone think this contradicts the seal?
4
Follow the answer
The commentary explains that Isa descends as a follower of Muhammad's sharia, not as a prophet with new legislation. Therefore, the seal remains intact.
Also note the specific point about jizya being lifted until Isa's descent.
5
Reflect on the logic
The argument uses the principle that sealing the broader category (prophets) necessarily seals the narrower (messengers). Reflect on how this reasoning strengthens the doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ر تحفة المريد على جوهرة التوحيد سيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم خاتم الأنبياء] ٦٩ - وَخُصَّ خَيْرُ الخَلْقِ أَنْ قَدْ تَمَّمَا بِهِ الجَميعَ رَبُّنا وَعَمَّمَا قوله : (وَخُصَّ خَيْرُ الخَلْقِ) ببناء الفعل للمفعول، و(خير الخلق): نائب فاعل الذي هو الله ، والأصل: وخصّ الله خير الخلق ؛ أي: أفضلهم وهو نبينا محمد ، و (خيرُ) أفعل تفضيل أصله (أخير ) كـ ( أكرم)، حذفت منه الهمزة لكثرة الاستعمال. وقوله : (أَنْ) قَدْ نَمَّمَا بِهِ الجَميعَ رَبُّنا أي: بأن ختم ربنا به صلى الله عليه وسلم جميع الأنبياء، فالباء مقدرة وهي داخلة على المقصور، فتتميم جميع الأنبياء مقصور عليه صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يتعداه إلى غيره، قال تعالى: ﴿وَخَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّ ) [الأحزاب: (٤٠] ، ويلزم منه ختم المرسلين؛ لأنه يلزم من ختم الأعم ختم الأخص من غير عكس، ولا يُشكل ذلك بنزول سيدنا عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام في آخر الزمان؛ لأنه إنما ينزل حاكماً بشريعة نبينا ومُتَّبعاً له، ولا يُنافي ذلك أنه حين نزوله يحكم برفع الجزية عن أهل الكتاب، ولا يقبل منهم إلا الإسلام أو السيف؛ لأن نبينا أخبرنا بأنها مُغيَّاة إلى نزول عيسى، فحكمه بذلك إنما هو بشريعة نبينا . وخصائصه لا تنحصر حدا ولا عدا ولكن المهم منها ما ذكره المصنف.
Tuhfat al-Murid on Jawharat al-Tawhid. Our master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, the seal of the prophets. 69 - And the best of creation was distinguished in that our Lord completed and generalized all through him. His saying: 'And the best of creation was distinguished' with the verb built for the passive, and 'best of creation' is the substitute subject, which is God, and the original is: And God distinguished the best of creation, i.e., the most virtuous of them, and he is our prophet Muhammad. And 'best' is a superlative, originally 'akhyar' like 'akram', the hamza deleted due to frequent use. His saying: 'that' meaning that our Lord sealed with him, peace be upon him, all the prophets. So the preposition 'bi' is implied and enters the restricted object. Thus the completion of all prophets is restricted to him, peace be upon him, not extending to others. He said: 'And seal of the prophets' [al-Ahzab: 40]. And from this follows the seal of the messengers because sealing the general entails sealing the specific without converse. And this is not problematic due to the descent of our master Isa, peace and prayer be upon him, at the end of time, because he descends only as a ruler by the law of our prophet and a follower of him. And it does not contradict that at his descent he rules to lift the jizya from the People of the Book and accepts from them only Islam or the sword, because our prophet informed us that it is limited until the descent of Isa. So his ruling by that is only by the law of our prophet. And his special characteristics cannot be limited by limit or count, but the important among them is what the author mentioned.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the line 'And the best of creation was distinguished in that our Lord completed and generalized all through him' from the poem. It first explains the grammar and meaning: 'And the best of creation was distinguished' is passive, with 'best of creation' as the subject, i.e., God distinguished him. 'Best' is a superlative originally 'akhyar' with hamza dropped for frequent use. Then it explains 'that our Lord completed all through him': God sealed all prophets with him. The preposition 'bi' is implied and enters the restricted object, meaning that the completion (i.e., sealing) of all prophets is restricted to him and no one else. The verse from al-Ahzab is cited. It follows logically that he is the seal of messengers because sealing the broader category (prophets) entails sealing the narrower (messengers). A potential objection is raised: What about the descent of Jesus at the end of time? The answer is that Jesus descends as a follower of Muhammad's law, not as a prophet with a new law. He will rule according to Muhammad's sharia, such as abolishing jizya. This does not break the seal because Jesus is not bringing a new message. The passage concludes by noting that the Prophet's special characteristics cannot be enumerated, but the important ones are those mentioned by the author.

خاتم النبيين

شريعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The descent of Isa means he will be a prophet after Muhammad, breaking the seal.
Correction: The commentary clarifies that Isa descends as a follower of Muhammad's sharia, not as a prophet with a new message, so the seal is not broken.

Checkpoint
Why does the descent of Prophet Isa at the end of time not contradict Muhammad being the seal of the prophets?
A) Because Isa will bring a new sharia.
B) Because Isa will descend as a ruler by Muhammad's sharia and a follower of him.
C) Because the seal only applies to prophets before Muhammad.
D) Because Isa will not descend at the end of time.

Key Takeaway
Muhammad is the final prophet; any future coming of a prophet (like Isa) will be under his law, not as a new prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Muhammad is the final prophet, why do you still look to other figures or ideologies for ultimate guidance? How does this reality demand a total reorientation of your trust and loyalty?
?
The text explains that Isa will descend as a follower of Muhammad's law. Does your heart truly accept that no new revelation or guidance can supersede what the Prophet brought, or are you secretly waiting for something 'new' that feels more relevant?
?
Your belief in the seal of prophethood is not just a theological fact—it is a test of your submission. Where in your life do you still act as if you need a new prophet to tell you what to do, instead of fully committing to the guidance already given?

The Universal Nature of Muhammad's Mission
Explanation of the universal scope of Muhammad's mission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the comprehensive scope of Prophet Muhammad's mission, including its extension to jinn, angels, Gog and Magog, and the spiritual world, and why this universality is unique to him.

Core Idea
Muhammad's mission is universal by essence, extending to all creation from Adam to the end of time.

The second special characteristic of the Prophet is the universality of his mission. This lesson unpacks what that means: he was sent to all morally responsible beings—humans, jinn, even angels in some interpretations—and his mission reaches earlier prophets and nations in the spiritual realm. Understanding this helps us appreciate why denying it is a serious error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on universality
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning up to the verse 'Saba: 28'. Notice how the author defines the generalization of the mission and its scope.
Focus on the terms 'obligatory sending' vs 'sending of honor'.
2
Identify the different recipients
List the groups mentioned: humans, jinn, angels, Gog and Magog, earlier prophets and nations. Note how each group is included differently.
For angels, there is a disagreement; the more correct view is 'sending of honor'.
3
Understand the spiritual dimension
The text says he is sent to all prophets and nations in the 'world of spirits' because his spirit was created first. This is a key point about the timeless reach of his mission.
This explains how he can be sent to people before his physical birth.
4
Connect to the Quran and hadith
Notice the proof texts: 'I was sent to all people' and Quran 34:28. These establish the universality as a revealed truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عموم بعثه واتباعُ عيسى له بعد نزولِهِ] قوله : (وَعَمَّمَا) بِعْتَتَهُ) أي : وخُصَّ أيضاً بأن عمَّم ربُّنا بعثته، فالباء مقدرة وهي داخلة على المقصور كما في الذي قبله، فتعميم البعثة مقصور عليه صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يتعداه إلى غيره فأرسله الله إلى جميع المكلفين من الثقلين إرسال تكليف اتفاقاً . وأما الملائكة فقد تقدَّم فيهم الخلافُ، والأصح (۱) أنه مُرسَلٌ إليهم إرسال تشريف، وبعضهم اعتمد أنه مرسل إليهم إرسال تكليف بما يليق بهم، فإن منهم الراكع والساجد إلى يوم القيامة. وما كُلّف به الإنس تفصيلاً وإجمالاً، فقد كُلّف به الجن كذلك، وشمل ذلك يأجوج ومأجوج - بالهمز وتركه ـ وهم أولاد يافث بن نوح، وقيل: جيل من الترك، وقيل : غير ذلك . والتحقيق أنه مرسل لجميع الأنبياء والأمم السابقة، لكن باعتبار عالم الأرواح، فإن روحه خُلقت قبل الأرواح وأرسلها الله لهم فبلغت الجميع، والأنبياء نُوَّابه في عالم الأجسام (۱) ، فهو مُرسَلٌ لجميع الناس من لدن آدم إلى يوم القيامة حتى إلى نفسه؛ لدخول الجميع تحت قوله : بعثت إلى الناس كافة (٢)، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَكَ إِلَّا كَافَةً لِلنَّاسِ (س: ۲۸] . حكم من نفى بعثة النبي ] فمن نفى عموم بعثته فقد كفر، وفي ذلك رد على العيسوية؛ وهم فرقة من اليهود زعموا تخصيص رسالته بالعرب. لا يُقال: تعميم البعثة ليس خاصا بنبينا ، بل مثله نوح فإنه كان مبعوثاً لجميع من في الأرض بعد الطوفان؛ لأنَّا نقول: تعميم بعثة نوح ليس من أصل البعثة، بل أمر اتفاقي؛ ؛ لأنه لم يَسْلَم من الهلاك إلا من كان معه في السفينة. وأما تعميم بعثة نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فهو من أصل البعثة، ومقتضى ما ذكر (۳) أن بعثة نوح لم تكن عامة قبل الطوفان فيكون بعض المغرقين لم يرسل إليهم، فيقال: إذ لم يُرسل إليهم فما مُوْجِبُ غرقهم؟ وقد قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا كُنَّا مُعَذِّبِينَ حَتَّى نَبْعَثَ رَسُولًا [الإسراء: (١٥، ولذلك قيل : إنها عامة قبل الطوفان ولعل الأول تمسك بقوله تعالى : ( وَاتَّقُوا فِتْنَةً لَّا تُصِيبَنَّ الَّذِينَ ظَلَمُوا مِنكُمْ خَاصَةُ )) (الأنفال: ٢٥)، وعلى القول بعموم
[The universality of his mission and the following of Jesus to him after his descent] His saying: 'And he generalized his mission' means: And he was distinguished also by our Lord generalizing his mission, so the preposition 'bi' is implied and enters the restricted object as in the previous one. So the generalization of the mission is restricted to him, peace be upon him, not extending to others. So God sent him to all morally responsible beings among the two heavy ones (humans and jinn) by an obligatory sending, unanimously. As for angels, the disagreement already preceded, and the more correct is that he is sent to them by a sending of honor, and some affirmed that he is sent to them by an obligatory sending befitting them, for among them are those who bow and prostrate until the Day of Resurrection. And what humans are obliged with, in detail and in summary, the jinn are obliged with likewise, and that includes Gog and Magog—with hamza and without it—and they are the sons of Japheth son of Noah, and it is said: a generation of Turks, and it is said: other than that. And the verification is that he is sent to all prophets and previous nations, but with regard to the world of spirits. For his spirit was created before spirits, and God sent it to them, and it reached all of them, and the prophets are his deputies in the world of bodies. So he is sent to all people from Adam until the Day of Resurrection, even to himself, because all are included under his saying: 'I was sent to all people' and His saying: 'And We have not sent you except comprehensively to mankind' [Saba: 28]. [Section: The ruling on whoever denies the Prophet's mission] So whoever denies the universality of his mission has disbelieved, and in that is a refutation of the 'Isawiyya, who are a sect of the Jews who claimed that his message is restricted to the Arabs. It may not be said: The generalization of the mission is not specific to our Prophet, but rather like him is Noah, for he was sent to everyone on earth after the flood. For we say: The generalization of Noah's mission is not from the origin of the mission, but rather an accidental matter, because only those who were with him in the ark survived. As for the generalization of the mission of our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, it is from the origin of the mission. And the implication of what was mentioned is that Noah's mission was not general before the flood, so some of the drowned were not sent to them. So it is said: If they were not sent to them, then what is the cause of their drowning? And He said: 'And We were not punishers until We send a messenger' [al-Isra: 15]. Therefore, it is said: It was general before the flood, and perhaps the first one holds to His saying: 'And fear a trial that will not strike exclusively those who have wronged among you' [al-Anfal: 25]. And on the view of generality...
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage explains the second special characteristic of the Prophet: the universality of his mission. It begins by interpreting 'And he generalized his mission' in the poem, emphasizing that this generalization is restricted to the Prophet and no other. God sent him to all morally responsible beings (mukallaf) among humans and jinn by an obligatory sending (irsal taklif). Regarding angels, there is a disagreement: the more correct view is that he is sent to them by a sending of honor (tashrif), not obligation, but some say he is sent to them by obligation appropriate to their nature (e.g., prayer). The obligation of humans and jinn includes details and summaries, covering even Gog and Magog. The verification (tahqiq) is that he is sent to all earlier prophets and nations in the world of spirits, because his spirit was created before theirs and reached them; the prophets are his deputies in the material world. Thus, he is sent to all people from Adam to the Day of Resurrection, even to himself, based on hadith and Quran (Saba: 28). The next section, 'The ruling on whoever denies the Prophet's mission,' states that denying the universality of his mission is disbelief (kufr), and this refutes the Jewish sect al-'Isawiyya who limited his mission to Arabs. An objection is raised: Was not Noah's mission universal after the flood? The answer distinguishes between essential (asli) and accidental (ittifaqi) universality. Noah's universality was accidental because it occurred only after the flood when no others remained; before the flood, it was not universal, otherwise the drowned would have been sent a messenger before punishment, but God does not punish without sending a messenger. This leads to an alternative view that Noah's mission was also universal before the flood. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the argument is clear: Muhammad's universality is essential and unique.

Defending the Universality Against Objections
Ruling on denial of universality and refutation of objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying the universality of Muhammad's mission constitutes disbelief, and how the objection regarding Noah's mission is refuted by distinguishing essential from accidental universality.

Core Idea
Denying the universality of Muhammad's mission is disbelief; Noah's universal mission was accidental, not essential.

Having established the universal scope of the Prophet's mission, the text now defends it against objections. It declares that anyone who denies this universality has disbelieved, refuting the Jewish sect al-'Isawiyya. Then it addresses a potential objection: was Noah's mission also universal? The distinction between essential and accidental universality resolves the issue.

Guided Path
1
Read the ruling and refutation
Read the section from 'فمن نفى عموم بعثته فقد كفر' to the end. Note the immediate ruling and the refutation of al-'Isawiyya.
Al-'Isawiyya limited the mission to Arabs.
2
Analyze the Noah objection
The objection claims Noah's mission was also universal. Identify how the author distinguishes it from Muhammad's universality.
The key term is 'from the origin of the mission' vs 'accidental matter'.
3
Understand the reasoning about punishment
The text uses Quran 17:15 to argue that if Noah's mission was not universal before the flood, the drowned could not have been punished. This strengthens the uniqueness of Muhammad's universality.
There is a debate; some hold Noah's mission was universal before the flood too.
4
Reflect on the significance of uniqueness
This distinction shows that Muhammad's universality is a special characteristic that no other prophet shares in the same essential way.

[The universality of his mission and the following of Jesus to him after his descent] His saying: 'And he generalized his mission' means: And he was distinguished also by our Lord generalizing his mission, so the preposition 'bi' is implied and enters the restricted object as in the previous one. So the generalization of the mission is restricted to him, peace be upon him, not extending to others. So God sent him to all morally responsible beings among the two heavy ones (humans and jinn) by an obligatory sending, unanimously. As for angels, the disagreement already preceded, and the more correct is that he is sent to them by a sending of honor, and some affirmed that he is sent to them by an obligatory sending befitting them, for among them are those who bow and prostrate until the Day of Resurrection. And what humans are obliged with, in detail and in summary, the jinn are obliged with likewise, and that includes Gog and Magog—with hamza and without it—and they are the sons of Japheth son of Noah, and it is said: a generation of Turks, and it is said: other than that. And the verification is that he is sent to all prophets and previous nations, but with regard to the world of spirits. For his spirit was created before spirits, and God sent it to them, and it reached all of them, and the prophets are his deputies in the world of bodies. So he is sent to all people from Adam until the Day of Resurrection, even to himself, because all are included under his saying: 'I was sent to all people' and His saying: 'And We have not sent you except comprehensively to mankind' [Saba: 28]. [Section: The ruling on whoever denies the Prophet's mission] So whoever denies the universality of his mission has disbelieved, and in that is a refutation of the 'Isawiyya, who are a sect of the Jews who claimed that his message is restricted to the Arabs. It may not be said: The generalization of the mission is not specific to our Prophet, but rather like him is Noah, for he was sent to everyone on earth after the flood. For we say: The generalization of Noah's mission is not from the origin of the mission, but rather an accidental matter, because only those who were with him in the ark survived. As for the generalization of the mission of our Prophet Muhammad, peace be upon him, it is from the origin of the mission. And the implication of what was mentioned is that Noah's mission was not general before the flood, so some of the drowned were not sent to them. So it is said: If they were not sent to them, then what is the cause of their drowning? And He said: 'And We were not punishers until We send a messenger' [al-Isra: 15]. Therefore, it is said: It was general before the flood, and perhaps the first one holds to His saying: 'And fear a trial that will not strike exclusively those who have wronged among you' [al-Anfal: 25]. And on the view of generality...
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage explains the second special characteristic of the Prophet: the universality of his mission. It begins by interpreting 'And he generalized his mission' in the poem, emphasizing that this generalization is restricted to the Prophet and no other. God sent him to all morally responsible beings (mukallaf) among humans and jinn by an obligatory sending (irsal taklif). Regarding angels, there is a disagreement: the more correct view is that he is sent to them by a sending of honor (tashrif), not obligation, but some say he is sent to them by obligation appropriate to their nature (e.g., prayer). The obligation of humans and jinn includes details and summaries, covering even Gog and Magog. The verification (tahqiq) is that he is sent to all earlier prophets and nations in the world of spirits, because his spirit was created before theirs and reached them; the prophets are his deputies in the material world. Thus, he is sent to all people from Adam to the Day of Resurrection, even to himself, based on hadith and Quran (Saba: 28). The next section, 'The ruling on whoever denies the Prophet's mission,' states that denying the universality of his mission is disbelief (kufr), and this refutes the Jewish sect al-'Isawiyya who limited his mission to Arabs. An objection is raised: Was not Noah's mission universal after the flood? The answer distinguishes between essential (asli) and accidental (ittifaqi) universality. Noah's universality was accidental because it occurred only after the flood when no others remained; before the flood, it was not universal, otherwise the drowned would have been sent a messenger before punishment, but God does not punish without sending a messenger. This leads to an alternative view that Noah's mission was also universal before the flood. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the argument is clear: Muhammad's universality is essential and unique.

Universality of Muhammad's Prophethood Compared to Noah's
Comparison of Noah's limited prophethood to Muhammad's universal one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Muhammad's prophethood is uniquely universal compared to Noah's, covering all times and both humans and jinn.

Core Idea
Muhammad's mission is universal; Noah's was limited to his time and people.

This passage presents a powerful comparison between the scope of Noah's prophethood and that of Muhammad. It clarifies that Noah's mission was restricted to his era before the Flood, while Muhammad's message encompasses all times and all beings, including the jinn. Understanding this distinction deepens our appreciation of the finality and universality of Islam.

This underscores the unique universality of Muhammad's prophethood.

The Abrogation of Previous Sharias by Muhammad's Sharia
Explanation of verse 71: abrogation of all previous sharias by Muhammad's sharia is obligatory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the abrogation of all previous divine laws by Muhammad's sharia is a necessary doctrine, supported by Quran, hadith, and consensus, and how it refutes Jewish and Christian objections.

Core Idea
Muhammad's sharia abrogates all previous sharias, as affirmed by Quran, consensus, and sound reason.

In this lesson, we examine a key doctrine of Islamic belief: that the sharia of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) abrogates all previous divine laws. This teaching is not merely a historical claim but a matter of theological necessity. The author presents evidence from the Quran, the consensus of Muslims, and a rational refutation of the objections raised by Jews and Christians.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the main claim and the structure of the argument.
The passage begins with the verse line, then expands into explanation and proof.
2
Identify the main claim and evidence
The main claim is that Muhammad's sharia abrogates all previous sharias necessarily. Look for the evidence: Quran verse 3:85, hadith reaching tawatur, and Muslim consensus.
Contrast with the position of Jews and Christians who deny it.
3
Understand the objection and its refutation
Jews/Christians argue that abrogation would imply a hidden benefit from Allah. The refutation is that benefits (masalih) differ according to time, so each era's sharia is appropriate.
This refutes the notion of any change in divine knowledge.
4
Reflect on the significance
This doctrine establishes the finality of Muhammad's prophethood and the obligation to follow his sharia. The passage ends with a prayer against those who deny it.
Consider how this impacts interfaith discussions.

النبوات
۷۱ - وَنَسْخُهُ لِشَرْعِ غَيْرِهِ وَقَعْ حَتْماً أَذَلَّ اللهُ مَنْ لَهُ مَنَعْ
قوله : (وَنَسْخُهُ لِشَرْعِ غَيْرِهِ وَقَعْ حَتْماً) أي: ونسخ شرع نبينا محمد لشرع كل غيره، وقع وحصل حال كونه متحتماً ، فـ (حتماً) بمعنى متحتماً حال من فاعل (وقع)، ويدل لذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَبْتَغِ غَيْرَ الْإِسْلَامِ دِينًا ﴾ [آل عمران: ٨٥] الآية، والأحاديث في ذلك كثيرة بلغت جملتها مبلغ التواتر، فنسخ مشرعه الشرع غيره واقع سماعاً بإجماع المسلمين خلافاً لليهود والنصارى، حيث زعموا أن شرع نبينا لم ينسخ شرع أحدٍ من الأنبياء توسلاً للقول بنفي نبوته، واحتجوا على ذلك بأنه يلزم على القول بالنسخ ظهور مصلحةٍ كانت خفية على الله تعالى ورُدَّ بأن المصلحة تختلف الأزمنة، فالمصلحة في زمن الأمم السابقة اقتضت تكليفهم بشرائعهم، والمصلحة في زماننا اقتضت تكليفنا بشريعتنا وقوله : (أَذَلَّ اللهُ مَنْ لَهُ مَنَعْ) أي : ألحق الذلَّ بمن منع نسخ شرع نبينا لغيره، وهذه جملة دعائية على اليهود والنصارى فإنهم المانعون لذلك .
Prophethoods. 71 - And his abrogation of the sharia of other than him occurred necessarily; Allah humiliated those who prevented it. His statement: (And his abrogation of the sharia of other than him occurred necessarily) i.e., the abrogation of the sharia of our Prophet Muhammad of every sharia other than his occurred and took place while it was necessary; so 'necessarily' (ḥatman) is in the sense of 'necessary' as a circumstantial accusative from the subject of 'occurred'. That is indicated by His statement (Whoever seeks other than Islam as a religion) [Āl ʿImrān 85] and the hadiths on that are numerous, reaching the level of tawātur. So the abrogation of his sharia of the sharia of other than him is established by hearsay by the consensus of the Muslims, contrary to the Jews and Christians, for they claimed that the sharia of our Prophet did not abrogate the sharia of any of the prophets, seeking thereby to deny his prophethood. They argued that abrogation would entail the emergence of a benefit that was hidden from Allah. The reply was that benefits differ according to times, so the benefit in the time of previous nations necessitated their obligation to their sharias, and the benefit in our time necessitated our obligation to our sharia. And his statement: (Allah humiliated those who prevented it) i.e., He inflicted humiliation on those who prevented the abrogation of our Prophet's sharia over other than his; this is a prayer against the Jews and Christians, for they are the preventers of that.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage defines and proves the abrogation of all previous sharias by the sharia of Prophet Muhammad. It is a response to Jews and Christians who deny this. The author explains the verse line and provides proof from Quran and hadith, and refutes their objection by showing that benefits change over time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abrogation implies a change in God's knowledge or purpose, as if He discovered a new benefit.
Correction: The benefit (maslahah) differs according to time; what was suitable for earlier nations is replaced by what is suitable for us. This does not entail any deficiency in divine knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The abrogation of previous sharias by Muhammad's sharia is a necessary doctrine proven by Quran, hadith reaching tawatur, and Muslim consensus, and it does not imply any deficiency in God.

Abrogation: Permissibility, Occurrence, and the Nature of Good and Evil
Commentary on verse 72: permissibility and occurrence of abrogation, response to rational good/evil objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the permissibility and actual occurrence of abrogation of parts of the Sharia, and why the rational determination of good and evil does not prevent abrogation.

Core Idea
Good and evil are defined by revelation, not reason, so abrogation is possible in principle.

This passage from the commentary on verse 72 addresses a key doctrine: that abrogation of some parts of Muhammad's Sharia by others is both permissible and occurred. It tackles an objection that certain obligations and prohibitions cannot be abrogated because they are rationally good or evil, and explains that good and evil are determined by the Lawgiver. It then summarizes the discussion by distinguishing between the levels of possibility and actual occurrence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the grammatical structure and the two key terms: جواز (permissibility) and وقوع (occurrence).
2
Identify the objection and response
Find the objection about rational good/evil and the author's response that good is defined by revelation.
3
Understand the summary of the two stations
Note the distinction between permissibility (anything is possible) and actual occurrence (only partial abrogation happened).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَنَسْخَ بَعْضِ شَرْعِهِ بِالبَعْضِ أَجِزْ ) لا يخفى أن (نسخ) بالنصب مفعول مقدَّمٌ لـ ( أجز) الواقع بعده؛ أي: اعتقد جواز نسخ بعض شرعه بالبعض الآخر جوازاً وقوعيّا؛ لأن ذلك وقع بالفعل نعم وجوب معرفته تعالى وتحريم الكفر نسخه غير واقع، وإن كان جائزاً كما هو مذهب أهل الحق خلافاً لمن قال : (إن المعرفة حَسَنٌ عقلي، والكفر قبيح عقلي، فوجوب المعرفة وتحريم الكفر لا يجوز نسخهما)، ونحن نقول : الحسن ما حسَّنه الشرع والقبيح ما قبَّحه الشرع، فلو جعل المعرفة من القبيح، والكفر من الحسن فلا حرج عليه .
وشمل البعض المنسوخ البعض القرآني خلافاً لمن منعه كأبي [مسلم]) الأصفهاني مُحتجا بقوله تعالى: لَا يَأْتِيهِ الْبَطِلُ مِنْ بَيْنِ يَدَيْهِ وَلَا مِنْ خَلْفِهِ ) [فصلت: ٤٢] فلو نسخ بعضه لتطرق إليه البطلان . وأجاب الأولون بأن الضمير لمجموع القرآن وهو لا ينسخ اتفاقاً، وخرج بتقييد المصنف بالبعض نسخ الجميع، فهو وإن كان جائزاً لكنه غير واقع
فالحاصل أن الكلام في مقامين :
مقام جواز ومقام وقوع، فمن حيث الجواز يجوز نسخ الشريعة كلا أو بعضاً، وأما من حيث الوقوع فلا يجوز نسخ الجميع جوازاً وقوعيا .
وقوله : (وما فِي ذَا لَهُ مِنْ غَضَ) أي : وما في هذا الحكم، وهو تجويز نسخ بعض شرعه بالبعض الآخر من نقص يقتضي امتناعه
His statement: (And I permit the abrogation of part of his sharia by another part). It is not hidden that (abrogation) is in the accusative as a fronted object of (I permit) that occurs after it; i.e., believe in the permissibility of abrogating some of his sharia by another part as a permissibility of occurrence, because that indeed occurred. Yes, the obligation of knowledge of Him and the prohibition of disbelief – their abrogation is not actual, though it is permissible, as is the doctrine of the people of truth, contrary to those who said: (Knowledge is rationally good, and disbelief is rationally evil, so the obligation of knowledge and the prohibition of disbelief cannot be abrogated). And we say: Good is what the Law declares good, and evil is what the Law declares evil. So if He were to make knowledge evil and disbelief good, there would be no objection to Him.
And the abrogated part includes Quranic part, contrary to those who prevented it, like Abu [Muslim] al-Isfahani, arguing by His statement: (Falsehood cannot approach it from before it or behind it) [Fussilat 42]; so if some of it were abrogated, falsehood would reach it. And the earlier scholars replied that the pronoun refers to the whole Quran, which is not abrogated unanimously. And by the author's restriction to 'part', the abrogation of the whole is excluded, so it is permissible but not actual.
In summary, the discussion is in two stations: a station of permissibility and a station of occurrence. From the perspective of permissibility, it is permissible to abrogate the sharia entirely or partially. As for occurrence, it is not permissible to abrogate the whole as an actual occurrence.
And his statement: (And there is no deficiency in this for him) i.e., there is no deficiency in this ruling, which is permitting the abrogation of some of his sharia by another part, that would necessitate its impossibility.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the second part of verse 72. It first explains the grammatical structure, then discusses the permissibility and occurrence of abrogation of some parts of the sharia by others. It addresses the objection that knowledge of God and prohibition of disbelief cannot be abrogated because they are intrinsically good/evil. The author responds by stating that good and evil are defined by revelation, not reason. Then it addresses an objection from Abu Muslim al-Isfahani that abrogation of Quranic verses is impossible due to the verse about protection from falsehood. The answer is that the verse refers to the entire Quran, which is never abrogated as a whole. The passage concludes with a summary distinguishing between possibility (جواز) and actual occurrence (وقوع): abrogation of the entire sharia is possible but did not occur; abrogation of some parts is possible and did occur. Finally, it explains the phrase 'وما في ذا له من غض' meaning there is no deficiency in this ruling.

Key Terms
نسخ
جواز
وقوع
حسن
قبيح
معرفة
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The obligation to know God and the prohibition of disbelief cannot be abrogated because they are rationally good and evil.
Correction: Good and evil are determined by revelation, so God could abrogate them in principle, though He has not.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what determines whether something is good or evil?
A) Human reason
B) Revelation (Sharia)
C) Consensus of scholars
D) Intrinsic nature of the act

Key Takeaway
Abrogation of parts of the Sharia is both permissible and occurred, but the obligation to know God and prohibition of disbelief have not been abrogated, and good and evil are defined by revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that what Allah commands is good even when it contradicts your own sense of justice or reason? Think of a specific ruling you find difficult—will you submit your intellect to revelation in that matter starting today?
?
Have you ever hesitated to obey a divine command because it seemed harsh or outdated? This lesson teaches that good and evil are defined only by Allah. Will you commit to seeking His decree as the sole measure of right and wrong, even when it costs you comfort?
?
The passage says the obligation to know God has not been abrogated, but it could have been. Imagine if Allah had declared ignorance of Him good and knowledge evil. Would you still worship Him on that basis? Let that question expose where your loyalty truly lies—with your own reason or with the Revealer.

Abrogation of Quranic Verses: The Objection of Abu Muslim al-Isfahani
Refutation of the objection that Quranic verses cannot be abrogated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection to abrogation of Quranic verses based on the verse of protection from falsehood, and the response that it refers to the entire Quran.

Core Idea
The Quran's protection from falsehood applies to the whole, not to every part, so partial abrogation is possible.

This passage addresses a specific objection from Abu Muslim al-Isfahani against the possibility of abrogating any Quranic verse. Citing the verse 'Falsehood cannot approach it from before it or behind it', he argued that abrogation would imply falsehood. The commentary provides the response: the pronoun refers to the entire Quran, which is never abrogated as a whole, but parts can be abrogated.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Understand Abu Muslim's argument using the Quranic verse.
2
Identify the response
Note that the pronoun refers to the whole Quran, so abrogation of parts is not a contradiction.
3
Relate to the author's restriction
The author's phrase 'part' excludes abrogation of the whole, which is permissible but not actual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

?
Reflect on your daily relationship with the Quran: do you approach each verse as part of a coherent whole that is divinely preserved, or do you treat them as isolated fragments? What change will you make in your recitation or study to honor the Quran as a unified book, not a collection of parts?

Abrogation of Book by Book and Sunna by Sunna
First two types of abrogation: Book by Book and Sunna by Sunna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first two types of abrogation (Book by Book and Sunna by Sunna) and their scriptural examples.

Core Idea
Later revelation supersedes earlier, even within the same type.

This lesson dives into the first two categories of abrogation outlined by Sanusi. We will see how a Qur'anic verse can abrogate another Qur'anic verse, and how a prophetic hadith can abrogate an earlier hadith. The examples clarify the principle that timing of revelation matters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation carefully. Focus on the two examples given.
Notice the phrase 'لتأخره نزولاً' – it explains the criterion.
2
Identify the abrogating and abrogated
For each example, identify which text is abrogated and which abrogates. Note the basis: later revelation.
3
Reflect on the principle
Consider why revelation chronology matters. This is foundational for understanding legal development in Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشمل ما ذكر نسخ الكتاب بالكتاب كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَجًا وَصِيَّةً لِأَزْوَاجِهِم مَّتَلَعًا إِلَى الْحَوْلِ غَيْرَ إخراج [البقرة: ٢٤٠] فإنه نُسخ بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَجًا يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْراً) [البقرة: ٢٣٤) لتأخره نزولاً، وإن تقدَّم تلاوة.
ونسخ السنة بالسنة كما في حديث: كنت نهيتكم عن زيارة القبور فزوروها » (١) ، فإنه نسخ النهي الذي وقع منه أولاً بالأمر في هذا الحديث.
ونسخ السنة بالكتاب كما في استقبال بيت المقدس الثابت بالسنة(٢)، فإنه نسخ باستقبال الكعبة الثابت بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَوَلِ وَجْهَكَ شَطْرَ الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٤٤]. ونسخ الكتاب بالسنة كما في قوله تعالى : كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمْ إِذَا حَضَرَ أَحَدَكُمُ الْمَوْتُ إِن ترك خيرًا الْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْوَالِدَيْنِ وَالأَقْرَبِينَ ﴾ [البقرة: ۱۸۰] ، فإنه نسخ بـحـديـث: «لا وصية.
And what was mentioned includes the abrogation of the Book by the Book, as in His statement: (And those who are taken in death among you and leave wives, a bequest for their wives: maintenance for one year without expulsion) [Al-Baqarah 240], for it was abrogated by His statement: (And those who are taken in death among you and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves for four months and ten days) [Al-Baqarah 234], because it was later in revelation, even if earlier in recitation. And the abrogation of the Sunna by the Sunna, as in the hadith: 'I had forbidden you from visiting graves, but now visit them,' for it abrogated the prohibition that occurred from him first by the command in this hadith. And the abrogation of the Sunna by the Book, as in facing Jerusalem established by the Sunna, for it was abrogated by facing the Kaaba established by His statement: (So turn your face toward the Sacred Mosque) [Al-Baqarah 144]. And the abrogation of the Book by the Sunna, as in His statement: (Prescribed for you, when death approaches one of you, if he leaves wealth, a bequest for parents and relatives) [Al-Baqarah 180], for it was abrogated by the hadith: 'No bequest'.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage classifies and provides examples of four types of abrogation in Islamic law. It covers abrogation of Quran by Quran (e.g., the verse about bequest for a year abrogated by the verse about four months and ten days), abrogation of sunna by sunna (e.g., the prohibition of visiting graves abrogated by a later hadith permitting it), abrogation of sunna by Quran (e.g., facing Jerusalem abrogated by facing the Kaaba), and abrogation of Quran by sunna (e.g., the verse about bequest for parents and relatives abrogated by the hadith 'no bequest for an heir'). Each example is briefly explained, emphasizing the principle of later revelation superseding earlier.

Key Terms
نسخ
كتاب
سنة
نزول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think abrogation only occurs when the later text explicitly states it abrogates the earlier.
Correction: Abrogation is determined by the chronological order of revelation, not by explicit mention. The examples show that even without saying 'this abrogates that', the later ruling takes effect.

Checkpoint
Which verse abrogated the bequest for a year (2:240)?
A) The verse of inheritance (4:11)
B) The verse of waiting period (2:234)
C) The verse of divorce (2:228)
D) The verse of guardianship (4:34)

Key Takeaway
The first two types of abrogation show that a later revelation from the same source (Quran or Sunna) can override an earlier one.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held onto a religious practice or interpretation simply because it was the first you learned, even after discovering later evidence that supersedes it? What might be holding you back from accepting the newer guidance? Ask yourself: am I following the latest command or just my habit?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) initially forbade visiting graves, then later allowed it. Does your heart resist change in religious matters? Reflect on an area where you might be clinging to an earlier ruling out of comfort rather than submission. Will you actively seek the most current and authentic guidance?
?
Abrogation shows that Allah's wisdom might delay some commands. Are you patient with divine timing, or do you demand all answers immediately? Consider a situation where you are waiting for clarity in your faith—will you trust that guidance comes at the right time, even if it supersedes what you thought before?

Abrogation of Sunna by Book and Book by Sunna
Last two types: Sunna by Book and Book by Sunna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the last two types of abrogation: Sunna abrogated by Quran, and Quran abrogated by Sunna.

Core Idea
Abrogation can cross between Quran and Sunna in both directions.

We now examine the cross-type abrogation examples: a sunna practice (facing Jerusalem) abrogated by a Qur'anic command, and a Qur'anic verse (about bequests) abrogated by a prophetic hadith. These illustrate the flexibility of Islamic legal development.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the two examples.
Observe how the examples are structured similarly to the previous lesson.
2
Compare the directions
One example abrogates sunna with Quran, the other abrogates Quran with sunna. Understand that both are valid.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider what this means for the authority of Quran vs. Sunna. Both can abrogate each other when later in time.

Source Text

It covers abrogation of Quran by Quran (e.g., the verse about bequest for a year abrogated by the verse about four months and ten days), abrogation of sunna by sunna (e.g., the prohibition of visiting graves abrogated by a later hadith permitting it), abrogation of sunna by Quran (e.g., facing Jerusalem abrogated by facing the Kaaba), and abrogation of Quran by sunna (e.g., the verse about bequest for parents and relatives abrogated by the hadith 'no bequest for an heir'). Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the Quran cannot be abrogated by the Sunna because the Quran is of higher authority.
Correction: Although the Quran is the primary source, a later sunna can abrogate an earlier Qur'anic ruling, as in the bequest example. Authority is not the issue; chronology is.

Checkpoint
Which example does the passage give for abrogation of the Book by the Sunna?
A) Facing Jerusalem abrogated by facing Kaaba
B) The prohibition of visiting graves abrogated by permission
C) The bequest verse abrogated by hadith
D) The verse of waiting period abrogating bequest

Key Takeaway
Cross-type abrogation shows that later revelation, whether Quran or Sunna, can overrule earlier rulings of the other type.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a command from Allah that contradicts your long-held practice, do you instantly obey like the companions changed qibla, or do you resist? What holds you back from immediate submission?
?
The Quranic verse on bequest for parents was abrogated by a single hadith. Does this shake your assumption that the Quran is always the final authority? How do you reconcile the need for both Quran and Sunna in your daily life?
?
If later revelation can change earlier rulings, what does that teach you about the nature of Allah's guidance as a gradual, merciful process? Are you willing to let go of a comfortable practice if a stronger evidence from Quran or Sunna requires it?

The Abundance and Clarity of the Prophet's Miracles
The author introduces the abundance and clarity of the Prophet's miracles and defines 'ghurar'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's miracles are described as 'many and distinguished' and the precise meaning of the term 'ghurar' in this context.

Core Idea
The Prophet's miracles are countless and unmistakably clear, each a sign of his prophethood.

In this lesson, we explore a key passage that highlights the extraordinary number and clarity of the Prophet's miracles. The commentator explains that the term 'ghurar' denotes miracles that are not only abundant but also well-known and undeniable, and he clarifies a subtle point about whether miracles require a challenge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get an overall sense of the content.
Notice the poetic line and the commentary that follows.
2
Understand the definition of miracles
Pay attention to the commentator's explanation that miracles are extraordinary events that may or may not include a challenge.
This corrects a common misunderstanding.
3
Grasp the meaning of 'ghurar'
Learn how the term evolved from a horse's blaze to mean 'clear and famous' in customary usage.
The commentator explicitly states the intended meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقديم مَنَائِ مَنْ مَعْجِزَاتِ سَيِّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ صلى الله عليه وسلم
٧٣ - ومُعْجِرَاتُهُ كَثِيرَةٌ غُرَرٌ مِنْها كَلامُ اللهِ مُعْجِزُ البَشَرُ
قوله : ( ومُعْجِرَاتُهُ كَثِيرَةٌ غُرَرُ ) لمَّا ذكر فيما تقدَّم تأييد الله تعالى للأنبياء بالمعجزات. . نبَّه هنا على كثرتها ووضوحها لنبينا دون غيره ؛ فالغرض الآن التنبيه على كثرة معجزاته ووضوحها، لكن المراد من معجزاته الأمور الخارقة للعادة الظاهرة على يده ؛ سواء كانت مقرونة بالتحدي أم لا فهو من استعمال اللفظ في حقيقته ومجازه، أو من عموم المجاز، وإنما وصفها بالكثرة المطلقة إيماء للعجز عن الإحاطة بها والغُرر جمع غُرَّة، وهي في الأصل: بياض في جبهة الفرس فوق الدرهم، وتطلق على خيار الشيء، ثم استعملت في كلّ واضح معروف على وجه الحقيقة العرفية، وهو المراد هنا، في (غرر) بمعنى واضحات مشهورات .
Introduction of a portion of the miracles of our master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace.
73 - And his miracles are many, distinguished, among them is the speech of Allah, the miracle that challenges human beings.
His statement (And his miracles are many, distinguished) – when he previously mentioned Allah's support of the prophets with miracles, he pointed here to their abundance and clarity for our Prophet uniquely; so the purpose now is to draw attention to the abundance of his miracles and their clarity. But what is meant by his miracles are the extraordinary matters that appear at his hand, whether they are accompanied by a challenge or not; this is using the term in its literal and metaphorical sense, or from the general metaphorical usage. And he described them with absolute abundance as a hint at the inability to encompass them. And (al-ghurar) is the plural of ghurra, which originally is a white spot on the forehead of a horse above a dirham, and it is used for the best of a thing, then it was used for everything clear and known according to customary reality, and that is what is meant here: in (ghurar) meaning clear and famous things.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is an introductory explanation of the poetic line '_Wa-muʽjizātuhu kathīratun ghurarun_' (And his miracles are many, distinguished). The author first notes that the poet, after previously discussing divine support for prophets through miracles, now highlights the abundance and clarity of miracles specific to our Prophet Muhammad (PBUH). The term 'miracles' (muʽjizāt) here refers to supernatural events (al-umūr al-khāriqah li-l-ʽādah) manifested at his hand, whether or not they are accompanied by a challenge (taḥaddī). The author then explains the word 'ghurar' (plural of ghurra): originally meaning a white mark on a horse's forehead, it came to denote the best part of a thing, and then by customary usage, anything clear and well-known. Thus, the miracles are described as 'clear and famous' (wāḍiḥāt mashhūrāt). The description of 'absolute abundance' (al-kathrat al-muṭlaqah) indicates that one cannot fully enumerate them.

Key Terms
معجزات
غرر
خارق للعادة
تحدي
مجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles always require a challenge (tahaddi).
Correction: The author states that miracles are extraordinary events that may or may not be accompanied by a challenge; the term is used in both literal and metaphorical senses.

Checkpoint
What does the term 'ghurar' (غرر) mean in the context of this passage?
A) White spots on a horse
B) Many and diverse
C) Clear and famous
D) The best part of something

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's miracles are both abundant and clear, with 'ghurar' meaning well-known and manifest signs.

Classification of Miracles by Certainty and Consequence
Sanusi enumerates three categories of miracles with their rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of miracles according to Sanusi and the corresponding rulings for denying them.

Core Idea
Not all miracles are equal: the punishment for denial depends on the strength of transmission.

Sanusi provides a concise but crucial classification of the Prophet's miracles. He links the level of certainty of a miracle's transmission to the religious consequence of denying it. This helps clarify why denying the Qur'an is far more severe than denying a less-known miracle, even if both are authentic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic original and its translation. Notice that Sanusi uses a conditional structure: 'if it is mutawatir... then kufr', 'if it is famous... then fisq', 'if it is not famous... then ta'zir'.
The passage uses the conjunction 'و' (and) to connect the three cases.
2
Identify the three levels of transmission
The three levels are: (1) tawatur (mass transmission), (2) shuhra (fame but not mutawatir), and (3) sahih or hasan chain (authentic but not famous). Understand how each level affects certainty.
Tawatur gives certainty; shuhra gives strong probability; sahih/hasan gives authenticity without fame.
3
Link each level to its ruling
For each level, note the corresponding punishment: denial of mutawatir is kufr (disbelief), denial of famous is fisq (sin), denial of authentic but non-famous is ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
This shows that not all denials are equal in severity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن ما كان منها معلوماً بالقطع منقولاً بالتواتر كالقرآن .. فلا شك في كفر منكره، وما لم يكن منها كذلك، فإن اشتهر كنبع الماء من بين أصابعه .. فسق منكره، وإن لم يشتهر وثبت بطريق صحيح أو حسن .. عُزّر منكره.
And know that whatever among them is known with certainty, transmitted by mass transmission (tawatur) like the Qur’an – there is no doubt in the disbelief (kufr) of its denier. And whatever among them is not like that, if it is famous like the flowing of water from between his fingers – then the denier is a sinner (fasiq). And if it is not famous and is established by a sound (sahih) or good (hasan) chain – then the denier is subjected to discretionary punishment (ta'zir).
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage provides a classification of the Prophet's miracles based on the level of certainty of their transmission and the corresponding punishment for denial. The author states three categories: (1) Miracles known with certainty through mass transmission (tawatur), such as the Qur’an – denying them is kufr (disbelief). (2) Miracles that are famous (ishtahara) but not mutawatir, like the flowing of water from between the Prophet's fingers – denying them makes one a fasiq (sinner), not a disbeliever. (3) Miracles that are not famous but are authentically established through sound (sahih) or good (hasan) chains – denying them incurs ta'zir (discretionary punishment). This classification shows the different weight of evidence: tawatur leads to certainty and heresy; widespread fame leads to sin; individual authentic reports lead to less severe punishment.

Key Terms
قطع
تواتر
شهرة
فسق
تعزير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that denying any authentic miracle is kufr (disbelief).
Correction: The passage clarifies that only denial of mutawatir miracles results in kufr; denial of less authenticated miracles has lesser rulings (fisq or ta'zir).

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on denying a miracle that is famous but not mutawatir?
A) Kufr
B) Fisq
C) Ta'zir
D) No sin

Key Takeaway
The punishment for denying a miracle depends on the level of certainty in its transmission: mutawatir miracles lead to disbelief, famous ones lead to sin, and authentic but less-known ones lead to discretionary punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a hadith about a miracle that is sahih but unfamiliar, does your internal reaction lean toward acceptance or skepticism? How does this classification help you discipline your response?
?
Think of a mutawatir miracle like the Qur'an. Do you truly feel the weight of certainty in your heart, or have you become desensitized? What would it take for you to live with the same conviction as the Companions?
?
If denying a famous miracle makes one a fasiq, does your indifference or careless talk about well-known Prophetic miracles reflect a lack of reverence? What concrete change can you make today to honor these signs of Allah?

The Qur'an as the Greatest Miracle and the Meaning of 'Kalam Allah'
The author distinguishes 'Kalam Allah' and explains the Qur'an's superiority as a miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two meanings of 'Kalam Allah' and why the Qur'an is the greatest and most enduring miracle of the Prophet.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is the greatest miracle because it remains until the Day of Resurrection.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies a crucial distinction: the term 'Kalam Allah' refers both to God's eternal attribute of speech and to the revealed words of the Qur'an. He then explains why the Qur'an, as the revealed wording, is the most excellent of the Prophet's miracles, surpassing all others in duration and comprehensiveness. Let's explore how this terminology shapes our understanding of the Qur'an's miraculous nature.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two meanings of 'Kalam Allah'
Read the opening sentences where 'Kalam Allah' is defined as both the eternal attribute and the revealed wording. Note how the same term is used for two different realities.
This distinction is fundamental in Islamic theology (kalam).
2
Identify which meaning the author intends
The passage states that in common usage, 'Kalam Allah' refers to the eternal attribute, and 'Qur'an' to the originated wording. However, the author (al-Laqani) here intends the wording. Notice the shift from general to specific.
3
Learn why the Qur'an is the best miracle
The commentator gives two reasons: (1) it is the most enduring, remaining until the Day of Resurrection, and (2) it encompasses all other miracles, either explicitly or implicitly via general verses.
Reflect on the verse citations: {Indeed Allah over all things is competent} and {We have not neglected in the Book anything}.
4
Consider how the Qur'an includes all miracles
The passage explains that even miracles not explicitly mentioned in the Qur'an are included in its general statements. This underscores the Qur'an's comprehensiveness.
Think about why this makes the Qur'an uniquely miraculous compared to other miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (مِنْها كَلامُ اللهِ) قد تقدَّم أن كلام الله يُطلق على الصفة القديمة وعلى اللفظ المنزل على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، المتعبد بتلاوته المتحدى بأقصر سورة منه كما يُطلق عليهما القرآن، لكن قد غلب كلام الله في الصفة القديمة والقرآن في اللفظ الحادث، والمصنف أراد هنا بكلام الله اللفظ، وإنما نصَّ عليه بخصوصه؛ لأنه أفضل معجزاته وأدومها لبقائه إلى يوم القيامة، ولا يخرج عنه شيء من معجزاته غالباً، وإلا فبعضها لم يذكر فيه بطريق الصراحة، وإن كان داخلاً في عموم قوله تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّ اللَّهَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ﴾ [الطلاق: ١٢]، ﴿وَمَا فَرَّطْنَا فِي الكِتابِ مِن شَيْءٍ﴾ [الأنعام: ٣٨] .
His statement (among them is the speech of Allah) – It has previously been mentioned that 'speech of Allah' (kalam Allah) is applied to the eternal attribute and to the wording sent down upon the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, which is used for worship in recitation and is challenged with the shortest surah thereof, just as 'Qur'an' is applied to both. But the usage of 'kalam Allah' has become predominant for the eternal attribute, and 'Qur'an' for the originated wording. The author intended here by 'kalam Allah' the wording. And he specifically mentioned it because it is the best of his miracles and the most lasting, remaining until the Day of Resurrection. And no miracle of his generally falls outside it, otherwise some of them are not mentioned in it explicitly, though they are included in the generality of His statement {Indeed Allah over all things is competent} [65:12] and {We have not neglected in the Book anything} [6:38].
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage explains the phrase '_minhā kalāmu llāh_' (among them is the speech of Allah) from the poem. The author clarifies that 'kalam Allah' can refer to two things: (1) the eternal attribute of speech (al-ṣifah al-qadīmah), and (2) the created wording (al-lafẓ al-munzal) revealed to the Prophet, which is recited in worship and challenged with the shortest surah. Although the term 'Qur'an' is applied to both, in common usage 'kalam Allah' predominantly denotes the eternal attribute, while 'Qur'an' denotes the originated wording. The author (al-Laqani) intended here the latter (the wording). He singled out the Qur'an because it is the best and most enduring of the Prophet's miracles—remaining until the Day of Judgment. Moreover, almost all miracles are either explicitly or implicitly mentioned in the Qur'an. Those not explicitly stated fall under general verses like 'Allah over all things is competent' or 'We have not neglected in the Book anything,' thus the Qur'an encompasses all miracles.

Key Terms
كلام الله
صفة قديمة
لفظ حادث
القرآن
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'Kalam Allah' always means the eternal attribute and the Qur'an is identical with that eternal speech.
Correction: The passage clarifies that 'Kalam Allah' can also refer to the created wording, and the author intends this meaning here. The Qur'an as a miracle is the temporal revelation, not the eternal attribute.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does 'kalam Allah' mean in the phrase 'among them is the speech of Allah'?
A) The eternal attribute
B) The created wording
C) Both equally
D) It is ambiguous

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an, as the created wording of God, is the greatest and most enduring miracle, encompassing all others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says the Qur'an encompasses all other miracles through verses like 'Indeed Allah over all things is competent'. Do you live as if that verse is enough to cover every difficulty you face, or do you still look for 'miracles' in your life to confirm God's power? What area of your life do you need to entrust to that verse right now?
?
You have the very words that remain until the Day of Resurrection. How can you, starting today, treat the recitation of these words as not just a ritual but as your direct encounter with the greatest miracle? What one practical change would make this real for you?

Examples of Miracles: Splitting of the Moon and Greeting of Trees
The author cites the moon splitting and trees greeting the Prophet as miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two specific miracles of the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ) that are established by hadith and the reasoning behind their acceptance.

Core Idea
The moon split and trees greeted the Prophet—miracles witnessed by many and affirmed by the Qur’an's principles.

This passage from the commentary provides concrete examples of miracles that support the Prophet's prophethood. The author cites the well-known miracle of the moon splitting, as narrated by Ibn Mas'ud, and begins to mention the greeting of trees and stones. These miracles are not explicitly detailed in the Qur'an but are authenticated by reliable hadith and general Qur'anic statements about Allah's power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation to get the full narrative of the moon splitting miracle. Notice the details: the two halves, the mountain, the command to witness.
The passage is incomplete at the end; the tree greeting is only introduced.
2
Understand the Quraysh's response
Observe how the disbelievers first accuse the Prophet of magic, then send to other lands to verify, and finally claim it is 'continuous magic'.
Their shifting argument shows they were confounded.
3
Note the second example
The author begins to mention the greeting of stones and trees to the Prophet, but the text cuts off. Understand that this is another category of miracles not mentioned in the Qur'an.
The full hadith is known from other sources.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why the author includes these examples: they are concrete manifestations of Allah's power supporting prophethood, consistent with Qur'anic principles like 'Allah is over all things competent'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذلك كانشقاق القمر، فعن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه أنه قال: بينما نحن مع رسول الله إذ انشق القمرُ فَلقتين، فكانت فَلقةٌ وراء الجبل وفَلقةٌ دونه، فقال لنا رسول الله اشهدوا ) ، وقال كفار قريش هذا سِحْرٌ فابعثوا إلى أهل الآفاق : حتى تنظروا أرأوا مثل هذا أم لا؟ فأخبر أهل الآفاق بأنهم رأوهُ مُنشقًا ، فقال كفار قريش هذا سِحْرٌ مُستمر، فقد انشقّ نصفين وهو في السماء، وإن كان قد يسبق إلى الوهم أنه نزل منها إلى الجبل. وكتسليم الحجر والشجر عليه ، فعن علي رضي الله تعالى عنه أنه قال: «كنت
And that is like the splitting of the moon; from Ibn Masʽud, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: While we were with the Messenger of Allah, the moon split into two halves, so one half was behind the mountain and the other half before it. The Messenger of Allah said to us, 'Bear witness.' The disbelievers of Quraysh said, 'This is magic. Send to the distant lands so that you may see if they saw the like of this or not.' So the people of the distant lands informed them that they had seen it split. The Quraysh disbelievers said, 'This is continuous magic.' For it split into two halves while it was in the sky, although it might occur to the imagination that it descended from it to the mountain. And like the greeting of the stone and tree to him; from ʽAli, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: 'I was...'
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage provides two specific examples of the Prophet's miracles that are not explicitly mentioned in the Qur'an but are known through hadith. The first is the splitting of the moon (inshiqāq al-qamar), narrated by Ibn Masʽud: the moon split into two pieces, one on each side of a mountain, witnessed by the Prophet's companions. The Quraysh disbelievers initially called it magic and sent travelers to other regions to verify; those regions confirmed they had seen it split. The Quraysh then claimed it was 'continuous magic' (siḥrun mustamirr), arguing that the moon remained split even while in the sky, though one might imagine it descended. The second example, cut short, is the greeting of stones and trees to the Prophet, as narrated by ʽAli. The passage illustrates that such miracles are included in the Qur'an's general statements, like 'Allah is over all things competent' (65:12) and 'We have not neglected in the Book anything' (6:38), even if not explicitly detailed.

الشجر
معجزة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The miracles of the moon splitting and trees greeting are not authentic because they are not mentioned in the Qur'an.
Correction: The passage shows these miracles are established by authentic hadith and are consistent with general Qur'anic principles, such as Allah's power over all things and the comprehensiveness of the Book.
