The Miracle of Qatada's Eye Healing
Narrates the miracle of Qatada's eye being healed by the Prophet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophetic miracle of Qatada's eye healing and the lesson it teaches about faith, priorities, and divine intervention through the Prophet.

Core Idea
Qatada's eye was miraculously healed as a reward for his self-sacrifice for the Prophet.

This story from the Battle of Uhud illustrates a profound miracle performed through the Prophet. It also reveals Qatada's unique concern and the Prophet's compassion. As you read, notice the choices presented to Qatada and his surprising request.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once slowly, then read the full translation. Let the narrative unfold.
Pay attention to the emotional tone—the Prophet's tears and Qatada's concern.
2
Identify the miracle
Notice that the eye was returned to its place and became the best of his eyes. This is the clear miraculous element.
The miracle is not just healing, but restoration of function and superiority.
3
Reflect on Qatada's choice
Qatada chose to have the eye returned and asked for Paradise, fearing women's rejection. What does this tell about his priorities?
He valued both worldly and religious concerns, but ultimately trusted the Prophet's intercession.
4
Understand the Prophet's prayer
The Prophet prayed: 'Protect Qatada as You protected the face of Your Prophet.' This connects Qatada's sacrifice to the Prophet's own protection.
The prayer was answered fully.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر قتادة وكرد عين حين سالت على خده، وذلك أنه كان يتقي بوجهه السهام عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في غزوة أحد، فأصاب عينه سهم فسالت على خده، فأخذها بيده وسعى بها إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فلما رآها في كفه دمعت عيناه، وقال: إن شئت صبرت ولك الجنة، وإن شئت رددتها ودعوت الله لك فلم تفقد منها شيئا، فقال: يا رسول الله، إن الجنة لجزاء جميل وعطاء جليل، ولكني رجل مبتلى بحب النساء، وأخاف أن يقلن: أعور فلا يردنني، ولكن تردها وتسأل الله لي الجنة، فردها في موضعها، وقال: اللهم قه قتادة كما وقيت وجه نبيك فاجعلها أحسن عينيه وأحدهما نظرا، وكان كذلك، وكانت لا ترمد إذا رمدت الأخرى.
And he mentioned Qatada and the crushing of his eye when it flowed on his cheek, because he was shielding his face from arrows for the Messenger of God ﷺ in the Battle of Uhud. An arrow struck his eye and it flowed onto his cheek. He took it in his hand and went with it to the Messenger of God ﷺ. When the Prophet saw it in his palm, his eyes teared, and he said: 'If you wish, you can bear patiently and you will have Paradise, and if you wish, I will return it and supplicate God for you and you will not miss anything from it.' He said: 'O Messenger of God, Paradise is a fine reward and a great gift, but I am a man afflicted with love of women, and I fear that they will say 'one-eyed' and will not want me. Rather, return it and ask God for Paradise for me.' So he returned it to its place and said: 'O God, protect Qatada as You protected the face of Your Prophet, and make it the best of his eyes and the sharpest in sight.' And it was so, and it never became inflamed when the other did.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage recounts a specific prophetic miracle: the healing of Qatada's eye during the Battle of Uhud. The story begins by describing how Qatada was using his face to shield the Prophet from arrows, and an arrow struck his eye causing it to fall onto his cheek. He carried it to the Prophet. When the Prophet saw it, his eyes teared and he gave Qatada a choice: either bear it patiently and receive Paradise, or have the eye returned and pray for it not to lose anything. Qatada chose to have it returned but asked the Prophet to pray for him to have Paradise, fearing that women would reject him if he were one-eyed. The Prophet returned the eye to its place and prayed for Qatada, making that eye the better of his two eyes. The passage ends by noting that the eye remained such that it never became inflamed when the other did.

Key Terms
قتادة
معجزة
شفاء العين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the Prophet had independent control over nature and could heal at will without divine permission.
Correction: The miracle occurred because God answered the Prophet's prayer, as the Prophet said: 'I will return it and supplicate God for you.' It was a divine act, not the Prophet's own power.

Checkpoint
What two options did the Prophet give Qatada regarding his injured eye?
A) Bear patiently and receive Paradise, or have the eye returned and healed.
B) Bear patiently and receive Paradise, or have the eye removed.
C) Have the eye returned without any condition.
D) Bear patiently and receive wealth.

Key Takeaway
The miracle of Qatada's eye healing shows that divine power works through the Prophet's supplication, and that even in seeking worldly concerns, faith in the Prophet's intercession can bring both worldly and spiritual benefit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Qatada risked his sight by shielding the Prophet with his face, ask yourself: What is the most valuable thing you possess that you would be willing to sacrifice for the sake of Allah and His Messenger? Will you actually do it when the moment comes?
?
Qatada chose to have his eye healed because he feared women would reject him as one-eyed. What fears or desires in your life make you reluctant to embrace a trial that could bring you Paradise? Are you willing to be honest with yourself about what you are truly seeking?
?
The Prophet's eyes teared when he saw Qatada's eye in his hand. Do you feel that same compassion when you witness the struggles of your fellow believers? Or has your heart become hardened? What practical step will you take this week to show genuine care for someone suffering for the sake of Allah?

The Miracle of the Lizard Testifying to Prophethood
Narrates the miracle of a lizard speaking to confirm prophethood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the miraculous speaking of a lizard served as a compelling proof of the Prophet Muhammad's prophethood, as narrated in the account of a Bedouin's conversion.

Core Idea
Even a lizard recognized the Prophet as true.

This lesson presents a remarkable miracle where a lizard spoke in clear Arabic to confirm the Prophet's message. The story shows how a Bedouin's skepticism was overcome when the creature itself testified to prophethood. It demonstrates that all of creation can be used by Allah to affirm the truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the story carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the narrative flow. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the dialogue and the lizard's response.
The story is a single continuous narrative.
2
Identify the miracle
Notice that a lizard speaking is not normal; this is a miracle (mu'jiza). It defies the natural order as a sign from Allah.
Miracles are given to prophets as proofs.
3
Understand the Bedouin's test
The Bedouin sets a condition: he will only believe if the lizard believes. Observe how the Prophet handles the challenge.
4
Reflect on the lizard's testimony
The lizard gives a detailed description of Allah and acknowledges Muhammad as the Seal of the Prophets. Consider the theological content revealed by the lizard.
This shows that even animals possess knowledge of God's attributes in this miraculous context.
5
Note the outcome
The Bedouin converts. This illustrates how miracles can bring about faith in those who witness them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكشهادة الضب بنبوته: روي أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان في محفل من أصحابه إذ جاءه أعرابي وقد صاد ضبا، فقال الأعرابي: من هذا؟ قالوا: نبي الله، فقال: واللات والعزى لا آمنت به إلا أن يؤمن هذا الضب وطرحه بين يديه، فقال: يا ضب، فأجابه بلسان مبين يسمعه القوم جميعا: لبيك وسعديك يا زين من وافي القيامة، قال: من تعبد؟ قال: الذي في السماء عرشه، وفي الأرض سلطانه، وفي البحر سبيله، وفي الجنة رحمته، وفي النار عقابه، قال: فمن أنا؟ قال: رسول رب العالمين، وخاتم النبيين، وقد أفلح من صدقك، وخاب من كذبك، فأسلم الأعرابي.
And [among the miracles is] the testimony of the lizard (al-dabb) to his prophethood: It is narrated that the Messenger of God ﷺ was in a gathering of his Companions when a Bedouin came to him having caught a lizard. The Bedouin said: 'Who is this?' They said: 'The Prophet of God.' He said: 'By al-Lat and al-Uzza, I will not believe in him unless this lizard believes.' He placed it before him. He said: 'O lizard!' It answered in a clear tongue which the people all heard: 'At your service, O ornament of those who will come on the Day of Resurrection.' He said: 'Whom do you worship?' It said: 'He whose throne is in the heaven, whose authority is on earth, whose path is in the sea, whose mercy is in Paradise, whose punishment is in the Fire.' He said: 'Then who am I?' It said: 'The Messenger of the Lord of the worlds, and the Seal of the Prophets. Successful is he who believes you, and failed is he who denies you.' So the Bedouin became Muslim.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage presents another miracle affirming prophethood: the testimony of a lizard. The story describes a Bedouin who captured a lizard and, to test the Prophet, demanded that the lizard believe. The Prophet called the lizard, and it spoke in a clear language heard by all present, acknowledging the Prophet as the Messenger of God and the Seal of the Prophets. The lizard's speech included a description of God's attributes and His dominion over all realms. Upon hearing this, the Bedouin embraced Islam. This miracle demonstrates that even animals recognize the truth of the Prophet's message, and it serves as a proof for those who witnessed it.

Key Terms
ضب
شهادة
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This story implies that all lizards are rational beings capable of speech.
Correction: This was a specific miraculous event (mu'jiza) granted to the Prophet; it does not mean lizards normally have intellect or speech.

Checkpoint

A) The Bedouin is misguided.
B) The Bedouin will be successful if he believes.
C) The Bedouin is a true seeker.
D) The lizard refused to comment.

Key Takeaway
This miracle demonstrates that even animals can be used by Allah to affirm the truth of prophethood, and such events can lead to faith in those who witness them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The lizard recognized the Prophet immediately. You have no such excuse. What is holding you back from fully submitting to him today?
?
The Bedouin demanded a miracle before believing. Have you been waiting for a sign to change a specific aspect of your life? What would be enough for you?
?
The lizard declared success for those who believe and failure for those who deny. Where do you stand? What concrete step will you take this week to live by that declaration?

The Fabricated Hadith of the Deer
States that the deer story is fabricated and has no authentic basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the story of the deer is a fabricated hadith and why authenticity matters in prophetic miracle narratives.

Core Idea
Not every dramatic miracle story is authentic—some are fabricated.

This lesson examines a well-known but inauthentic story about a speaking deer. The passage firmly declares it a fabrication. By studying this, you will learn how scholars identify and reject forged reports, even when they contain seemingly miraculous elements.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the author's verdict and the quoted story.
Notice that the author begins with a clear judgment.
2
Identify the author's verdict
Find the exact phrase where the author declares the hadith fabricated. Understand that this is a definitive ruling, not a suggestion.
The word 'موضوع' (mawdu') is key.
3
Examine the story's details
Read the quoted wording of the deer story. Note its elements: the deer speaks, asks for release, nurses fawns, returns, and declares faith.
The story is dramatic but the author rejects it.
4
Reflect on the lesson for authenticity
Consider why scholars would label such a story fabricated. This highlights the importance of rigorous verification in Islamic tradition.
Even miraculous-sounding reports must have a valid chain.
5
Connect to the broader topic
Understand that in discussions of prophethood and miracles, distinguishing authentic from fabricated reports is essential.
This passage is a case study in critical evaluation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حديث الظبية فالحق أنه موضوع لا أصل له، ولفظه: كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في صحراء فنادته ظبية يا رسول الله، فقال: ما حاجتك؟ قالت: صادني هذا الأعرابي، ولي خشفان - بكسر الخاء وتسكين الشين؛ أي: ولدان في ذلك الجبل، فأطلقني حتى أذهب أرضعهما وأرجع فقال: وتفعلين؟ قالت: نعم، عذبني الله عذاب العشار إن لم أفعل، فأطلقها، فذهبت ورجعت فأوثقها فانتبه الأعرابي، وقال: يا رسول الله ألك حاجة؟ قال: تطلق هذه الظبية فأطلقها، فخرجت تعدو في الصحراء وتقول: أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله، وأنك رسول الله، لكن الحديث موضوع كما علمت.
As for the hadith of the deer, the truth is that it is fabricated and has no basis. Its wording is: 'The Prophet ﷺ was in a desert when a deer called out: O Messenger of God. He said: What is your need? It said: This Bedouin captured me, and I have two fawns - meaning two young ones in that mountain. So release me so I may go and nurse them and return. He said: And will you do that? It said: Yes, may God punish me with the punishment of the ten (months pregnant) if I do not. So he released it, it went and returned, and then he tied it up. The Bedouin woke up and said: O Messenger of God, do you need something? He said: Release this deer. So he released it, and it ran off in the desert saying: I bear witness that there is no god but God and that you are the Messenger of God. But the hadith is fabricated, as you have learned.'
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage addresses a purported miracle involving a speaking deer and clarifies that it is not authentic. The author states that the story is fabricated and has no authentic chain. He then quotes the fabricated wording: the deer asks the Prophet to be released to nurse her fawns, promises to return, and indeed returns, then declares faith. Despite its dramatic content, the author declares it subject (fabricated). This illustrates the importance of distinguishing authentic reports from forged ones in discussing prophetic miracles.

Key Terms
ظبية
حديث موضوع
فبركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think the deer story is a genuine miracle of the Prophet.
Correction: The passage clearly states that the hadith is fabricated and has no basis, so it cannot be considered an authentic miracle.

Checkpoint

A) It is authentic.
B) It is fabricated and has no basis.
C) It is weak but acceptable.
D) It is a valid miracle.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the deer is a fabricated story with no authentic basis, showing that not all reported miracles are reliable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you hear a miraculous tale, what specific steps will you personally take to verify its authenticity? Commit to one concrete action you will implement starting today.
?
The deer story is inspiring yet false. Are you willing to reject spiritual narratives that feel good but lack evidence? Examine your own desire for uplifting stories—does it sometimes override your commitment to truth?

Defining I'jaz and Its Minimum Amount
Defines i'jaz and discusses the minimum miraculous amount.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars define the miraculous nature of the Qur'an and their disagreement on the smallest portion that constitutes a miracle.

Core Idea
The Qur'an is miraculous in its entirety; the minimum is a short sura or three verses.

Before we explore what makes the Qur'an inimitable, we must first agree on its definition and scope. This passage from the commentator clarifies that the entire Qur'an is a miracle, but scholars differ on the minimum part that can be considered miraculous. We will examine the two main views and the preferred resolution.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Start by reading the Arabic definition of i'jaz and the supporting Quranic verse. Notice how the commentator explains that all creatures are incapable of opposing the Qur'an.
The verse from al-Isra' is the primary proof.
2
Understand the consensus
The commentator states consensus that the entire Qur'an is a miracle. This is a foundational point before the dispute on details.
3
Examine the two scholarly views
Identify the two positions: the majority says the shortest sura or three verses; Qadi 'Iyad says one long sura or a single long verse. Reflect on the reasoning behind each.
The commentator resolves the apparent contradiction.
4
Note the resolution
The commentator adopts the view that a long verse (like Ayat al-Kursi) is equivalent to three short verses. This resolves the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (مُعْجِزُ البَشَرُ ) أي : مصيرهم عاجزين عن معارضته، والإتيان بمثله، بل كل المخلوقات كذلك إجماعاً وقُل لَّئِنِ اجْتَمَعَتِ الإِنسُ وَالْجِنُّ عَلَى أَن يَأْتُوا بِمِثْلِ هَذَا الْقُرْآنِ لَا يَأْتُونَ بِمِثْلِهِ، وَلَوْ كَانَ بَعْضُهُمْ لِبَعْضِ ظَهِيرًا) [الإسراء: ۱۸۸؛ أي: مُعيناً، وخَصَّ الإنس والجن مع أن سائر المخلوقات كذلك ؛ لأنهما اللذان يتصوَّرُ منهما المعارضة، بخلاف غيرهما كالملائكة لعصمتهم واقتصار الناظم على البشر؛ لأنهم الذين تصدوا لذلك بالفعل والبشر) هم بنو آدم سُمُّوا بذلك لبدو بشرتهم التي هي ظاهر الجلد . ولا خلاف في أن القرآن بجملته معجز، وإنما الخلاف في أقل ما يقع به الإعجاز من أبعاضه واختار جمهور أهل التحقيق أن أقله أقصر سورة منه أو ثلاث آيات وقال القاضي عياض: إن أقله سورةُ إِنَّا أَعْطَيْنَاكَ الْكَوْثَرَ [الكوثر: 1] أو آية أو آيات في قدرها، وظاهر الأول أن الآية أو الآيتين ليس معجزاً وإن عادل الثلاثة أو السورة في الطول كآية الكرسي والدين والظاهر خلافه، فالمعتمد أن الآية الطويلة معجزة كالثلاثة . واختلف في وجه إعجازه فقيل : كون الله صرفهم عن الإتيان بمثله مع كونهم قادرين على ذلك، وهذا القول يُسمى قولَ الصَّرْفة ، والذي ذهب إليه الجمهور أن وجه إعجازه كونه في أعلى طبقات البلاغة والفصاحة مع اشتماله على الإخبار بالمغيبات ودقائق العلوم وأحوال المبدأ والمعاد، وغير ذلك ممَّا لا يُحصى، وهذا هو الصحيح في وجه الإعجاز.
His saying: ('Mu'jiz al-bashar') i.e., rendering them incapable of opposing it and producing its like, rather all creatures are likewise by consensus. And say: 'If mankind and jinn gathered to produce the like of this Qur'an, they would not produce its like, even if some of them were helpers to others' [al-Isra' 88]; i.e., assistants. And He specified mankind and jinn although all other creatures are likewise because they are the ones from whom opposition can be imagined, unlike others like angels due to their infallibility; and the poet's restriction to humans because they are the ones who actually undertook that. And 'al-bashar' are the sons of Adam, so called because of the appearance of their skin (bashara) which is the outer layer of skin. There is no dispute that the entire Qur'an is miraculous; rather the dispute is concerning the least part of it by which the miracle occurs. The majority of verifiers held that the least is the shortest sura of it or three verses. And Qadi 'Iyad said: The least is Surat Inna A'tayna al-Kawthar or one verse or verses of its length. And the apparent meaning of the first is that one or two verses are not miraculous even if they equal three or a sura in length, like Ayat al-Kursi and the verse of debt; but the apparent is contrary to that, so the relied-upon view is that a long verse is miraculous like three verses. And they differed concerning the aspect of its inimitability. It was said: It is that Allah turned them away from producing its like while they were capable of that, and this view is called the view of al-Sarfa. And the view adopted by the majority is that the aspect of its inimitability is that it is at the highest level of eloquence and rhetoric, along with its containing reports of the unseen, subtle sciences, states of the beginning and the return, and other things beyond count. And this is the correct view regarding the aspect of inimitability.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a definition and discussion of the miraculous nature of the Qur'an (i'jaz al-Qur'an). The commentator begins by explaining the phrase 'mu'jiz al-bashar' from the poem, meaning that the Qur'an renders people incapable of producing its like. He cites the Quranic verse from Surat al-Isra' (88) to support this. He notes that the verse specifically mentions humans and jinn because they are capable of opposition, unlike angels. The commentator then states the consensus that the entire Qur'an is miraculous, but scholars differ on the minimum portion that constitutes a miracle. The majority say it is the shortest sura or three verses, while Qadi 'Iyad says it could be a single long verse like Surat al-Kawthar or any verse of similar length. The commentator resolves the apparent contradiction by adopting the view that a long verse is equivalent to three short ones. Next, he presents two views on the nature of the miracle: the theory of sarfa (divine prevention), which holds that God prevented people from imitating the Qur'an despite their ability, and the majority view that the miracle lies in the unmatched eloquence and content (including prophecies and knowledge). The commentator declares the majority view as correct.

Key Terms
إعجاز
معجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the commentator state as the relied-upon view regarding the minimum miraculous portion of the Qur'an?
A) The entire Qur'an must be taken together.
B) The shortest sura or three verses.
C) One long verse like Ayat al-Kursi.
D) Only Surat al-Kawthar.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an is entirely miraculous, and the minimum part that is miraculous is a short sura or three verses, with a long verse being equivalent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the shortest sura of the Qur'an is beyond human ability to imitate, how does that expose your own pride in your intellectual abilities? In what area of your life are you acting as if you can produce something of comparable worth?
?
When you read a single verse like Ayat al-Kursi, do you feel its weight as a miracle? What would change in your recitation if you truly believed those words were impossible for any human to originate?
?
The scholars differed on the minimum miraculous amount, yet they all affirmed the Qur'an's inimitability. Is your belief in the Qur'an based on secondhand acceptance, or have you personally felt the impossibility of matching its language and depth? What would it take for you to move from intellectual assent to a heart-conviction?

The Two Views on the Nature of I'jaz
Presents and evaluates two views on the nature of Qur'anic inimitability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two major scholarly views on why the Qur'an is inimitable: the theory of sarfa (divine prevention) and the view of its unmatched eloquence and content.

Core Idea
The majority holds that i'jaz lies in eloquence, prophecies, and knowledge, not merely divine prevention.

After establishing that the Qur'an is a miracle, the commentator turns to the deeper question: what exactly makes it inimitable? Two classical theories emerged: one that God simply prevented people from imitating it, and another that its very content and style are beyond human capacity. Let us explore both positions and the preferred one.

Guided Path
1
Read the two views
The passage presents two views: al-sarfa and the majority view. Identify each one and note their key features.
Al-sarfa claims people were capable but prevented; the majority points to eloquence and unique content.
2
Understand al-sarfa
This view says that God turned people away from imitating the Qur'an even though they had the ability. Consider why some scholars might propose this.
It avoids attributing inherent superiority to the Qur'an's language.
3
Understand the majority view
The majority holds that the Qur'an itself is at the highest level of eloquence (balagha, fasaha) and contains prophecies, subtle sciences, and knowledge of the unseen. This makes it inherently inimitable.
4
Note the commentator's endorsement
The commentator explicitly states 'this is the correct view.' Reflect on why the majority view is preferred.
The evidence from the Qur'an's content supports this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (مُعْجِزُ البَشَرُ ) أي : مصيرهم عاجزين عن معارضته، والإتيان بمثله، بل كل المخلوقات كذلك إجماعاً وقُل لَّئِنِ اجْتَمَعَتِ الإِنسُ وَالْجِنُّ عَلَى أَن يَأْتُوا بِمِثْلِ هَذَا الْقُرْآنِ لَا يَأْتُونَ بِمِثْلِهِ، وَلَوْ كَانَ بَعْضُهُمْ لِبَعْضِ ظَهِيرًا) [الإسراء: ۱۸۸؛ أي: مُعيناً، وخَصَّ الإنس والجن مع أن سائر المخلوقات كذلك ؛ لأنهما اللذان يتصوَّرُ منهما المعارضة، بخلاف غيرهما كالملائكة لعصمتهم واقتصار الناظم على البشر؛ لأنهم الذين تصدوا لذلك بالفعل والبشر) هم بنو آدم سُمُّوا بذلك لبدو بشرتهم التي هي ظاهر الجلد . ولا خلاف في أن القرآن بجملته معجز، وإنما الخلاف في أقل ما يقع به الإعجاز من أبعاضه واختار جمهور أهل التحقيق أن أقله أقصر سورة منه أو ثلاث آيات وقال القاضي عياض: إن أقله سورةُ إِنَّا أَعْطَيْنَاكَ الْكَوْثَرَ [الكوثر: 1] أو آية أو آيات في قدرها، وظاهر الأول أن الآية أو الآيتين ليس معجزاً وإن عادل الثلاثة أو السورة في الطول كآية الكرسي والدين والظاهر خلافه، فالمعتمد أن الآية الطويلة معجزة كالثلاثة . واختلف في وجه إعجازه فقيل : كون الله صرفهم عن الإتيان بمثله مع كونهم قادرين على ذلك، وهذا القول يُسمى قولَ الصَّرْفة ، والذي ذهب إليه الجمهور أن وجه إعجازه كونه في أعلى طبقات البلاغة والفصاحة مع اشتماله على الإخبار بالمغيبات ودقائق العلوم وأحوال المبدأ والمعاد، وغير ذلك ممَّا لا يُحصى، وهذا هو الصحيح في وجه الإعجاز.
His saying: ('Mu'jiz al-bashar') i.e., rendering them incapable of opposing it and producing its like, rather all creatures are likewise by consensus. And say: 'If mankind and jinn gathered to produce the like of this Qur'an, they would not produce its like, even if some of them were helpers to others' [al-Isra' 88]; i.e., assistants. And He specified mankind and jinn although all other creatures are likewise because they are the ones from whom opposition can be imagined, unlike others like angels due to their infallibility; and the poet's restriction to humans because they are the ones who actually undertook that. And 'al-bashar' are the sons of Adam, so called because of the appearance of their skin (bashara) which is the outer layer of skin. There is no dispute that the entire Qur'an is miraculous; rather the dispute is concerning the least part of it by which the miracle occurs. The majority of verifiers held that the least is the shortest sura of it or three verses. And Qadi 'Iyad said: The least is Surat Inna A'tayna al-Kawthar or one verse or verses of its length. And the apparent meaning of the first is that one or two verses are not miraculous even if they equal three or a sura in length, like Ayat al-Kursi and the verse of debt; but the apparent is contrary to that, so the relied-upon view is that a long verse is miraculous like three verses. And they differed concerning the aspect of its inimitability. It was said: It is that Allah turned them away from producing its like while they were capable of that, and this view is called the view of al-Sarfa. And the view adopted by the majority is that the aspect of its inimitability is that it is at the highest level of eloquence and rhetoric, along with its containing reports of the unseen, subtle sciences, states of the beginning and the return, and other things beyond count. And this is the correct view regarding the aspect of inimitability.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a definition and discussion of the miraculous nature of the Qur'an (i'jaz al-Qur'an). The commentator begins by explaining the phrase 'mu'jiz al-bashar' from the poem, meaning that the Qur'an renders people incapable of producing its like. He cites the Quranic verse from Surat al-Isra' (88) to support this. He notes that the verse specifically mentions humans and jinn because they are capable of opposition, unlike angels. The commentator then states the consensus that the entire Qur'an is miraculous, but scholars differ on the minimum portion that constitutes a miracle. The majority say it is the shortest sura or three verses, while Qadi 'Iyad says it could be a single long verse like Surat al-Kawthar or any verse of similar length. The commentator resolves the apparent contradiction by adopting the view that a long verse is equivalent to three short ones. Next, he presents two views on the nature of the miracle: the theory of sarfa (divine prevention), which holds that God prevented people from imitating the Qur'an despite their ability, and the majority view that the miracle lies in the unmatched eloquence and content (including prophecies and knowledge). The commentator declares the majority view as correct.

Key Terms
الصَّرْفة
البلاغة
الفصاحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the i'jaz is only about eloquence and not about content.
Correction: The majority view includes both eloquence and content (prophecies, sciences, etc.).

Checkpoint
Which view does the commentator consider correct regarding the aspect of i'jaz?
A) Al-sarfa (divine prevention).
B) The majority view (eloquence and content).
C) Both views are correct.
D) Neither view.

Key Takeaway
The majority of scholars hold that the Qur'an is inimitable because of its supreme eloquence and its unique content, not because God prevented imitation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Qur'an, do you consciously experience its eloquence and depth, or do you rely on external proofs for its divine origin? What would change if you personally encountered its inimitability?
?
If you believed that the Qur'an’s inimitability was merely divine prevention (al-sarfa), how would that affect your conviction that it is truly the word of Allah? Are you willing to accept the majority view that the Qur'an itself is inherently miraculous?
?
The passage says the Qur'an contains 'reports of the unseen, subtle sciences, states of the beginning and the return.' Which of these aspects have you deeply reflected on? What is one unseen truth you must act upon today?

The Command to Believe in the Physical Mi'raj
The commentator explains the poem's command and defines the Mi'raj as a physical journey.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Mi'raj is a physical, wakeful journey of the Prophet, and why the poet only mentioned the Mi'raj despite covering both Isra' and Mi'raj.

Core Idea
The Mi'raj is a real physical ascent, not a metaphor.

Sanusi commands the student to have firm belief in the Prophet's Mi'raj, as reported by the reliable scholars. The commentator explains that the term 'Mi'raj' is often used inclusively for both the night journey and the ascension, so the poet sufficed with one. This lesson establishes the physical, wakeful nature of the journey as the orthodox position.

Guided Path
1
Read the poetic command and its explanation
Read the Arabic verse and the commentator's explanation of its wording and meaning.
Notice the lightened ya for metre.
2
Understand the scope of the term 'Mi'raj'
The commentator shows that 'Mi'raj' is used in a broad sense to include the Isra'. Recognize why the poet did not mention Isra' separately.
3
Identify the key details of the journey
Note the mention of al-Buraq, the angels, and the sequence from Masjid al-Haram to Masjid al-Aqsa to the heavens.
This reinforces the physical nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٧٤ - واجْزِمُ بِمِعْراجِ النَّبِيِّ كَمَا رَوَوا وَبَرِّئَنْ لِعَائِشَهُ مِمَّا رَمَوا قوله : واجْزِمْ بِمِعراج النَّبِي كَمَا رَوَوا بسكون الياء من النبي مخففة للوزن؛ أي: واعتقد اعتقاداً جازماً بعروج نبينا وصعوده إلى السماوات السبع إلى سدرة إلى حيث شاء الله بعد الإسراء به على البراق وجبريل عن يمينه وميكائيل عن يساره من المسجد الحرام إلى المسجد الأقصى حال كون العروج الذي جزمت به مثل الذي رواه أهل الحديث والتفسير والسير . المنتهى وكان على الناظم التعرضُ للإسراء أيضاً، لكن استغنى عن ذكره بذكر المعراج ؛ لشهرة إطلاق أحد الاسمين أعني الإسراء والمعراج على ما يعم مدلوليهما ، وهو سَيْرُهُ ليلاً إلى أمكنة مخصوصة على وجه خارق للعادة فهذا أمر كلي يشمل مدلوليهما . والحق أنه كان يَقَظَةٌ بالروح والجسد، كما أجمع عليه أهل القرن الثاني ومن بعده من الأمة، خلافاً لبعض القرن الأول، القائل بأنه كان مناماً، ولبعضه القائل بأنه كان بالروح فقط لكن يقظة، فالأقوال ثلاثة. أصلاً، فإن قيل: فما الفرق بين كونه مناماً وبين كونه بالروح؟ أجيب بأنه على كونه مناماً يكون في حالة النوم، وعلى كونه بالروح لا نوم بل الروح تذهب للأمكنة المخصوصة والجسم في هذه الحالة يكون كالغافل . والإسراء من المسجد الحرام إلى المسجد الأقصى ثابت بالكتاب والسنة وإجماع المسلمين، فمن أنكره كفر . والمعراج من المسجد الأقصى إلى السماوات السبع ثابت بالأحاديث المشهورة، ومنها إلى الجنة، ثم إلى المستوى أو العرش أو طرف العالم من فوق العرش، على (۱) سدرة المنتهى هي شجرة ينتهي إليها علم الملائكة، ولم يُجاوزها أحد إلا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، جاء : في وصفها ما أخرجه البخاري (۳۲۰٦) في حديث المعراج بقوله : ورفعت لي سدرة المنتهى، فإذا نبقها (حملها وثمارها كأنه قلال هجراء، وورقها كأنه آذان الفيول، في أصلها أربعة أنهار تهران باطنان و تهران ،ظاهران فسألتُ ،جبريل فقال: أما الباطنان ففي الجنة، وأما الظاهرانِ فالنيل والفرات».
74. And be certain of the Mi'raj of the Prophet as they narrated, and declare 'A'isha innocent of what they accused. His saying: 'And be certain of the Mi'raj of the Prophet as they narrated' with a sukun on the ya of al-nabi (the Prophet) lightened for the metre; meaning: And believe with firm belief in the ascent of our Prophet and his rising to the seven heavens, to the Sidra, to where Allah willed, after the Isra' on al-Buraq, with Jibril on his right and Mika'il on his left, from al-Masjid al-Haram to al-Masjid al-Aqsa, while the ascent which you affirmed is like what the people of hadith, tafsir, and sira narrated. (al-Muntaha) And it was incumbent upon the poet to also mention al-Isra', but he sufficed with mentioning al-Mi'raj because of the common usage of one of the two names, i.e., al-Isra' and al-Mi'raj, for what encompasses both significations, and it is his journey at night to specific places in a manner breaking the norm; thus this is a universal matter that includes both significations. And the truth is that it was in a state of wakefulness, with soul and body, as the people of the second century and those after them from the community have agreed upon, contrary to some of the first century who said it was a dream, and others who said it was only with the soul but while awake. So the views are three. Originally, if it is said: What is the difference between it being a dream and it being with the soul? The answer: That if it is a dream, it occurs in the state of sleep, and if it is with the soul, there is no sleep, but the soul goes to the specific places and the body in this state is like one who is heedless. And the Isra' from al-Masjid al-Haram to al-Masjid al-Aqsa is established by the Book, the Sunna, and the consensus of the Muslims; so whoever denies it becomes a disbeliever. And the Mi'raj from al-Masjid al-Aqsa to the seven heavens is established by well-known hadiths, and from them to Paradise, then to al-Mustawa or the Throne or the edge of the world above the Throne, upon (1) Sidrat al-Muntaha, which is a tree to which the knowledge of the angels extends, and no one has passed beyond it except the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. It is mentioned in its description what al-Bukhari (3206) narrated in the hadith of the Mi'raj: 'The Sidrat al-Muntaha was raised up for me, and behold, its fruits were like the pitchers of Hajar, and its leaves like the ears of elephants; at its base were four rivers: two hidden and two manifest. I asked Jibril, and he said: As for the two hidden, they are in Paradise, and as for the two manifest, they are the Nile and the Euphrates.'
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the Isra' and Mi'raj (the Night Journey and Ascension) of the Prophet Muhammad. The commentator begins by quoting the poem that commands certainty in the Mi'raj and declares 'A'isha innocent of slander. He explains the poem's wording, noting the lightened ya for metre. He defines the Mi'raj as the Prophet's ascent to the heavens and beyond, following the Isra' on al-Buraq with angels. He then explains why the poet mentioned only Mi'raj and not Isra': the term is often used inclusively. The commentator asserts the correct view that the journey was physical and wakeful, as agreed by the early generations. He lists three opinions: physical (correct), dream, and spiritual-only. He answers an objection distinguishing dream from spiritual journey: in a dream the person sleeps, while in a spiritual journey the soul goes while the body is heedless but awake. He then states that the Isra' is proven by Qur'an, Sunna, and consensus, and its denier becomes a disbeliever. The Mi'raj is proven by well-known hadiths. The footnote describes Sidrat al-Muntaha, the tree beyond which only the Prophet passed, with a hadith from al-Bukhari describing its fruits, leaves, and rivers.

Key Terms
معراج
إسراء
براق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the poet only mention the Mi'raj and not the Isra'?
A) Because the poet forgot the Isra'.
B) Because the Mi'raj is more important than the Isra'.
C) Because the term Mi'raj is often used broadly to include both.
D) Because the Isra' is not mentioned in the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
The Mi'raj is a physical journey of the Prophet, and the term is used inclusively for the entire night journey.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you profess belief in the Mi'raj, do you truly conceive of it as a physical, bodily journey through the heavens, or do you find yourself instinctively reducing it to a metaphor to avoid intellectual discomfort? Ask Allah for certainty today.
?
The poet commands 'be certain of the Mi'raj of the Prophet'. Examine your own heart: is your certainty in this event as firm as your certainty in the five daily prayers? If not, what steps will you take to strengthen it?
?
Imagine standing before Allah and being asked about your belief in the Mi'raj. Would you be able to say 'I believed it exactly as narrated, without doubt'? What does your current level of conviction reveal about your relationship with revelation?

The Three Opinions and the Proof of the Isra'
The commentator presents the three opinions and defends the physical Mi'raj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three opinions on the nature of the Mi'raj and understand why the orthodox position is that it was physical and wakeful.

Core Idea
The Mi'raj was bodily and wakeful, not a dream or a spiritual-only event.

After establishing the definition, the commentator addresses disagreements among early scholars about the nature of the Mi'raj. There were three views: dream, spiritual-only, and physical. He affirms the correct view as physical and wakeful, supported by consensus. He then answers an objection distinguishing dream from spiritual journey. Finally, he states that denying the Isra' leads to disbelief and describes the Sidrat al-Muntaha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opinions
Read the three views: dream, spiritual-only, and physical wakeful. Notice which one the commentator affirms.
The commentator sides with the third opinion.
2
Understand the objection and its answer
The commentator explains the difference between a dream journey and a spiritual journey: in a dream, sleep is present; in a spiritual journey, the body is heedless but awake.
This clarifies why the physical journey is unique.
3
Note the proofs and ruling
The Isra' is proven by Qur'an, Sunna, and consensus; denial is disbelief. The Mi'raj is proven by authentic hadiths.
4
Reflect on the Sidrat al-Muntaha
Read the description from al-Bukhari about the tree beyond which only the Prophet passed.
This highlights the Prophet's special status.

Do you truly believe that the Prophet ﷺ traveled physically to the heavens, or have you allowed secular doubts to creep in? Examine your heart: if you find any hesitation, will you actively seek to strengthen your conviction by studying the proofs from the Quran and Sunnah?
?
The denier of the Isra' is declared a disbeliever. Have you ever remained silent when someone mocked or questioned this miracle? Will you commit to defending the honor of the Prophet's journey with knowledge and courage, even among skeptical company?
?
The Prophet ﷺ alone passed beyond Sidrat al-Muntaha; no angel or human has reached that station. How does this exclusive honor affect your love and reverence for him? Will you make a firm intention to learn more about his unique virtues and let that transform your daily relationship with him?

The Reality of the Prophet's Ascension (Mi'raj)
Author explains the command to believe in the Mi'raj and clarifies its nature and the three opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the Prophet's Mi'raj, that it occurred in a waking state with body and soul, and how the term Mi'raj encompasses the Isra'.

Core Idea
The Mi'raj was a real, physical-spiritual journey, not a dream.

The poem commands us to be decisive about the Prophet's ascension as narrated. But what exactly is the Mi'raj? How does it relate to the Isra'? And was it a dream or a waking event? The author clarifies these points, affirming the orthodox position that it was a waking journey with body and soul, and explains why the poem only mentions Mi'raj.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the command and its explanation
Read the opening lines where the author explains the verse, noting that it commands a decisive belief in the ascension after the Night Journey.
2
Understand why only Mi'raj is mentioned
Notice how the author argues that 'Mi'raj' is used to cover both Isra' and Mi'raj because they are commonly understood together as the supernatural night journey.
3
Identify the three opinions on the nature of the journey
Find the three views: (1) a dream, (2) a spiritual journey while awake, (3) the correct view: a waking journey with body and soul. See how the author supports the third with consensus of the second generation.
4
Distinguish between dream and spiritual journey
Read the objection and answer, and understand the difference: a dream occurs in sleep, while a spiritual journey occurs without sleep, with the body in a daze.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : واجْزِمْ بِمِعراج النَّبِي كَمَا رَوَوا بسكون الياء من النبي مخففة للوزن؛ أي: واعتقد اعتقاداً جازماً بعروج نبينا وصعوده إلى السماوات السبع إلى سدرة إلى حيث شاء الله بعد الإسراء به على البراق وجبريل عن يمينه وميكائيل عن يساره من المسجد الحرام إلى المسجد الأقصى حال كون العروج الذي جزمت به مثل الذي رواه أهل الحديث والتفسير والسير . وكان على الناظم التعرضُ للإسراء أيضاً، لكن استغنى عن ذكره بذكر المعراج ؛ لشهرة إطلاق أحد الاسمين أعني الإسراء والمعراج على ما يعم مدلوليهما ، وهو سَيْرُهُ ليلاً إلى أمكنة مخصوصة على وجه خارق للعادة فهذا أمر كلي يشمل مدلوليهما . والحق أنه كان يَقَظَةٌ بالروح والجسد، كما أجمع عليه أهل القرن الثاني ومن بعده من الأمة، خلافاً لبعض القرن الأول، القائل بأنه كان مناماً، ولبعضه القائل بأنه كان بالروح فقط لكن يقظة، فالأقوال ثلاثة. فإن قيل: فما الفرق بين كونه مناماً وبين كونه بالروح؟ أجيب بأنه على كونه مناماً يكون في حالة النوم، وعلى كونه بالروح لا نوم بل الروح تذهب للأمكنة المخصوصة والجسم في هذه الحالة يكون كالغافل . والإسراء من المسجد الحرام إلى المسجد الأقصى ثابت بالكتاب والسنة وإجماع المسلمين، فمن أنكره كفر . والمعراج من المسجد الأقصى إلى السماوات السبع ثابت بالأحاديث المشهورة، ومنها إلى الجنة، ثم إلى المستوى أو العرش أو طرف العالم من فوق العرش، على الخلاف في ذلك، ثابت بخبر الواحد، فمن أنكره لا يكفر لكن يفسق، والتحقيق أنه لم يصل إلى العرش، كما نصوا عليه في مواد القصة
His statement: 'And be decisive about the Prophet's ascension as they narrated' — with the yaa of 'an-nabii' having sukoon for metrical lightness; i.e., hold a decisive belief in our Prophet's ascension and his rising to the seven heavens, to the Sidrat al-Muntaha, to wherever Allah willed, after the Night Journey (Isra') on al-Buraq, with Jibril on his right and Mika'il on his left, from the Sacred Mosque to the Farthest Mosque, while the ascension about which you are decisive is like what was narrated by the people of hadith, tafsir, and sirah. It was incumbent upon the poet to also mention the Isra', but he dispensed with mentioning it by mentioning the Mi'raj, due to the common usage of either name — namely al-Isra' and al-Mi'raj — to refer to what encompasses the meanings of both, which is his night travel to specific places in a supernatural manner, so this is a comprehensive matter that includes both of their meanings. The truth is that it was a waking state with spirit and body, as agreed upon by the people of the second century and after from the community, contrary to some of the first century who said it was a dream, and to some of them who said it was with the spirit only but while awake, so the opinions are three. If it is said: What is the difference between it being a dream and it being with the spirit? The answer is that on the basis of it being a dream, it occurs in the state of sleep, while on the basis of it being with the spirit, there is no sleep, rather the spirit goes to specific places while the body in this state is like one heedless. The Isra' from the Sacred Mosque to the Farthest Mosque is established by the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of Muslims; whoever denies it becomes a disbeliever. The Mi'raj from the Farthest Mosque to the seven heavens is established by well-known hadiths, and from there to Paradise, then to the Level (al-Mustawa) or the Throne or the edge of the world above the Throne, according to the difference of opinion on that; it is established by a solitary report (khabar al-wahid); so whoever denies it does not become a disbeliever but becomes a sinner (fasiq). The verified position is that he did not reach the Throne, as they stated in the accounts of the story.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the poem's verse that commands the believer to affirm the Prophet's Mi'raj (ascension) as narrated. The author begins by clarifying the meaning of the verse: it is a command to hold a firm belief in the Prophet's ascension through the heavens to the Sidrat al-Muntaha and beyond, after the Isra' (night journey) from Mecca to Jerusalem. He then addresses why the poem only mentions Mi'raj and not Isra' explicitly: because both terms are commonly used interchangeably to cover the whole miraculous night journey. The correct view, he states, is that the journey occurred in a wakeful state with both body and soul, as agreed upon by the scholars of the second generation and later, contrary to two minority opinions from the first generation: one that it was a dream, and another that it was a spiritual journey while awake. An objection is raised: what is the difference between a dream and a spiritual-only journey? The answer distinguishes the two: a dream happens during sleep, while a spiritual journey occurs without sleep, with the soul leaving the body which remains in a daze. The author then gives rulings: denying the Isra' (from Mecca to Jerusalem) is kufr because it is established by the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. Denying the details of the Mi'raj (from Jerusalem upward) is not kufr but fisq, because those details are based on ahad (single-narrator) reports. The verified position is that the Prophet did not reach the Throne, as stated in the accounts.

Key Terms
معراج
إسراء
براق
سدرة المنتهى
يقظة
منام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's Mi'raj was only a dream or a spiritual experience.
Correction: The orthodox position, as stated by the author, is that the Mi'raj occurred in a waking state with both body and soul, as agreed by the scholars of the second century onwards.

Checkpoint
According to the author, how many opinions are there regarding the nature of the Prophet's Mi'raj?
A) 2
B) 3
C) 4
D) 1

Key Takeaway
The Mi'raj was a real, waking journey of body and soul, and the term Mi'raj encompasses both the Isra' and the ascension.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you decisive (jāzim) in your belief about the Mi'raj, or do you entertain doubts? What would it mean for your faith if you wavered on this matter?
?
If the Mi'raj was a real physical-spiritual journey, what does that imply about the connection between body and soul in acts of worship? How does that affect your own spiritual practices?
?
The author says the true opinion is based on consensus. Do you submit to scholarly consensus even when individual opinions might seem more 'rational'? Why or why not?

The Ruling on Denying the Isra' and Mi'raj
Author explains the rulings on denying the Isra' and Mi'raj based on evidence levels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference in evidence between the Isra' and the Mi'raj, and why denial of the Isra' is disbelief while denial of the Mi'raj's details is only a sin.

Core Idea
Denial of the Isra' is disbelief; denial of the Mi'raj's details is sin—due to the strength of evidence.

Not all parts of the Prophet's night journey have the same level of proof. The Isra' from Mecca to Jerusalem is established by the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, while the details of the ascension rely on solitary reports. This difference has real consequences for belief and practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on rulings
Read the passage that discusses the evidentiary bases for the Isra' and the Mi'raj, and the consequences of denial.
2
Identify the two journeys
Note that the author distinguishes between the Isra' (Mecca to Jerusalem) and the Mi'raj (Jerusalem upward).
3
Understand the evidence levels
The Isra' is established by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus (definitive). The Mi'raj is established by well-known hadiths, but further details by solitary reports.
4
Learn the rulings
Denial of the Isra' leads to kufr (disbelief); denial of the details of the Mi'raj leads to fisq (sin).
5
Note the verified position on reaching the Throne
The author states that the Prophet did not reach the Throne, as the accounts indicate.

?

Will you now examine your heart for any reluctance to submit to the prophetic reports, even those with weaker chains?
?

This lesson asks you to repent from any intellectual arrogance.
?

Do you ever reflect on this miracle when you pray (the nightly journey) or when you read the Quran? Or is it just a story you accept without transformation? This lesson forces you to ask: what is the practical fruit of your belief in this event?

The Obligation to Believe in Aisha's Innocence
The author commands belief in Aisha's innocence and lists proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why affirming Aisha's complete innocence from the slander is an obligatory belief, and why doubting it constitutes disbelief.

Core Idea
Denying Aisha's innocence is not a sin—it is kufr.

Sanusi's poem commands the believer to hold the Mother of the Believers, Aisha, innocent from the false accusation of adultery. In this lesson, we explore the three definitive proofs for her innocence and the severe consequence of rejecting them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the poem uses poetic modifications like 'بَرِّتَنْ' for 'بَرِّئَنْ'.
2
Identify the three proofs
The passage lists three definitive proofs for Aisha's innocence. Find them and note how each is presented.
The proofs are: the Quran, the consensus of the Ummah, and authentic hadiths.
3
Understand the severity of the ruling
The author states that anyone who denies or doubts her innocence becomes a disbeliever. Reflect on why this ruling is so strong.
This is because her innocence is established by definitive evidence.
4
Connect to the story context
The passage begins the story of the slander. Read the opening of the story and anticipate how it continues.
The story is well-known; compare with the Quranic account in Surah an-Nur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَبَرِّتَنْ لِعَائِشَهُ مِمَّا رَمَوا) بزيادة اللام وسكون الهاء للوزن؛ أي: اعتقد وجوباً براءة أم المؤمنين عائشة بنت أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنها وعن أبويها ممَّا رماها به المنافقون من الإفك ؛ أي: أشدّ الكذب والذي تولى كبره ؛ أي: معظمه حيث ابتدأ الخوض فيه، وأشاعه عبد الله بن أبي بن سلول لعنه الله، وأبي : اسم أبيه، وسَلُول : اسم أمه، وقد جاء القرآن ببراءتها، وانعقد عليها إجماع الأمة، ووردت بها الأحاديث الصحيحة، فمن جحد براءتها أو شك فيها كفر . وحاصل قصتها أن النبي كان إذا أراد سفراً أقرع بين نسائه، فلما أراد صلى الله عليه وسلم التوجه لغزوة بني المصطلق وتسمى غزوة المُرَيسيع أقرع بينهن، فخرجت القرعة
His statement: 'And render innocence for Aisha from what they slandered' — with an extra lam and sukoon on the ha for meter; i.e., hold as obligatory the innocence of the Mother of the Believers Aisha bint Abi Bakr as-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with her and her parents, from what the hypocrites slandered her with of the lie (al-ifk); i.e., the worst falsehood, and he who undertook its main burden — i.e., its majority — where he initiated delving into it and spread it was Abdullah ibn Ubayy ibn Salul, may Allah curse him; Ubay is his father's name, and Salul is his mother's name. The Quran has come with her innocence, the consensus of the community has been concluded upon it, and authentic hadiths have been reported concerning it; so whoever denies her innocence or doubts it becomes a disbeliever. The summary of her story is that the Prophet, when he wanted to travel, would cast lots among his wives. When he intended to set out for the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq, also called Ghazwat al-Muraysi', he cast lots among them, and the lot came out (for Aisha).
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage explains the next verse of the poem, which commands the believer to affirm the innocence of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) from the slander (al-ifk) leveled against her. The author explains that the verse means to hold an obligatory belief in her complete innocence from the severe lie fabricated by the hypocrites, led by Abdullah ibn Ubayy ibn Salul. He then lists the definitive proofs: the Quran explicitly revealed her innocence (in Surah an-Nur), the consensus of the Muslim community, and the authentic hadiths. Consequently, anyone who denies her innocence or doubts it falls into disbelief (kufr). The author then provides a summary of the story: whenever the Prophet set out on a journey, he would cast lots among his wives. When he intended to go on the expedition against Banu al-Mustaliq (also known as Ghazwat al-Muraysi'), he cast lots, and the lot fell on Aisha. (The story continues on the next pages.)

Correction: The passage explicitly states that doubt or denial is kufr, which removes one from Islam.

Key Takeaway
Affirming Aisha's complete innocence is an obligatory belief; rejecting it nullifies faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author states that doubt in Aisha's innocence is disbelief. Ask yourself: is there any matter of this religion that you harbor intellectual reservations about? What would it cost you to fully submit to the definitive texts, without exception?
?
The Prophet cast lots among his wives to decide travel, showing reliance on Allah in even small decisions. Is there an area of your life where you rely more on your own planning than on Allah's guidance? How can you actively entrust that decision to Him today?
?
The slander was carried out by hypocrites—people who outwardly appeared Muslim but had evil in their hearts. Do you ever find yourself speaking about the honor of believers (especially the righteous predecessors) in a way that diminishes their dignity? What step will you take to purify your tongue from backbiting or slander?

The Lost Necklace and Safwan's Help
Narration of the beginning of the ifk incident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sequence of events that led to Aisha being left behind and how Safwan ibn al-Mu'attal assisted her.

Core Idea
A lost necklace set the stage for a slander that would be divinely refuted.

The story of the slander begins with a seemingly trivial incident—a broken necklace. This episode reveals the character of Aisha and Safwan, and sets the backdrop for the trial that would test the Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to understand the sequence.
Pay attention to the details about the necklace and Safwan's actions.
2
Identify the key events

This sets up the situation that led to accusations.
3
Reflect on Safwan's character
Notice how Safwan acted with propriety (turning his back, not looking at her). This shows his integrity.
4
Connect to the larger story
Understand that this innocent incident became the basis for slander by hypocrites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحاصل قصتها أن النبي كان إذا أراد سفراً أقرع بين نسائه، فلما أراد صلى الله عليه وسلم التوجه لغزوة بني المصطلق وتسمى غزوة المُرَيسيع أقرع بينهن، فخرجت القرعة على عائشة، فتوجهت معه، ففي رجوعهم منها ضاع عقدها، وكان من جزعِ أظفار - يفتح الجيم وسكون الزاي أو فتحها - أي : خرز منسوب لأظفار ؛ وهي بلدة في اليمن، فتخلفت في طلبه فحُمِلَ هودجها، وهو مركب من مراكب النساء كالقبة، ظنا أنها فيه ؛ لأنها كانت خفيفة كما أخبرت بذلك، وسار القوم ورجعت إليهم فلم تجدهم، فمكثت مكانها، فأخذها النوم، فمرَّ بها صفوان بن المعطل، وكان يعرفها قبل آية الحجاب، وكان يتخلف ليلتقط ما يسقط من المتاع أو لأنه كان ثقيل النوم فبرك ناقته، وولاها ظهره، وصار يسترجع جهراً حتى استيقظت وحملها على الناقة، ولم ينظر إليها، وقاد بها الناقة موليها ظهره حتى أدرك بها النبي ، فرَمَوْها به، وفشا ذلك بين المنافقين وضعفاء المسلمين فشق ذلك على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فجمع الصحابة، وقال: يا معشر المسلمين ؛ مَنْ يعذرني من رجل قد بلغني أذاه في أهل بيتي، فوالله ما علمت على أهلي إلا خيراً، ولقد ذكروا رجلاً ما علمت عليه إلا خيراً، فقال سعد بن سيد الأوس أنا أعذرك منه يا رسول الله ؛ إن كان من الأوس ضربت عنقه، وإن كان : من إخواننا من الخزرج أمرتنا ففعلنا أمرك . فقال سعد بن عبادة سيد الخزرج : كذبت لا تقدر على قتله، فَهم الأوس والخزرج بالقتال، فأمرهم النبي بالإعراض عن ذلك، فأنزل الله في براءتها إِنَّ الَّذِينَ جَاءُو بالإفكِ عُصْبَةٌ مِنكر [النور: ۱۱] العشر آيات ... إلى قوله تعالى: أُولَيكَ مُبَرَّءُونَ مِمَّا يَقُولُونَ لَهُم مَّغْفِرَةٌ وَرِزْقٌ كَرِيمٌ﴾ [النور: ٢٦] . فقال أبو بكر لعائشة : قومي فاشكري لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت : لا والله لا أشكرُ إلا الله الذي برأني ، لكن لم يكن ذلك لشيء كان في نفسها من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فإن مقامها يَجِلُّ عن ذلك، وإنما استغرقت في مقام الشهود، فلم تشهد إلا الله، وكان ممَّن تكلَّم في الإفك مِسْطح، وكان أبو بكر يُنفق عليه، فلما بلغه أنه تكلم في الإفك حلف لا ينفق عليه ، فأنزل الله: ﴿وَلَا يَأْتَلِ أُولُوا الْفَضْلِ مِنكُمْ وَالسَّعَةِ [النور: ۲۲] الآية، فأعاد أبو بكر النفقة كما كانت .
The summary of her story is that the Prophet, when he intended a journey, would cast lots among his wives. When he intended to set out for the expedition of Banu al-Mustaliq, also called the expedition of Muraysi', he cast lots among them, and the lot fell upon Aisha. So she set out with him. On their return, her necklace was lost. It was made of d̲j̲azʿ aẓfār (with d̲j̲im opened and zāy silent or opened) meaning: beads attributed to Aẓfār, which is a town in Yemen. So she fell behind to look for it, and her howdaj (a women's mount like a dome) was carried on the camel, thinking she was inside, because she was light as she reported. The people moved on, and she returned to them but did not find them. So she stayed in her place and was overcome by sleep. Safwan ibn al-Muʿaṭṭal passed by her. He had known her before the verse of hijab. He used to lag behind to pick up anything that fell of the baggage, or because he was a heavy sleeper. He made his camel kneel, turned his back to her, and began to recite the istirjāʿ aloud until she woke up. He mounted her on the camel without looking at her, led the camel with his back turned to her until he reached the Prophet with her. They accused her (of wrongdoing) because of that. This spread among the hypocrites and weak Muslims, and that distressed the Prophet. He gathered the Companions and said: 'O Muslims, who will excuse me concerning a man whose harm has reached my family? By Allah, I know nothing but good of my family, and they have mentioned a man of whom I know nothing but good.' Saʿd ibn Muʿādh, the leader of the Aws, said: 'O Messenger of Allah, I will excuse you concerning him. If he is from the Aws, I will strike his neck; if he is from our brothers of the Khazraj, command us and we will do your command.' Saʿd ibn ʿUbāda, the leader of the Khazraj, said: 'You lie! You cannot kill him.' The Aws and Khazraj nearly came to fighting, but the Prophet ordered them to ignore that. Then Allah revealed concerning her innocence: 'Indeed, those who came with the slander are a group among you' [an-Nur 24:11] ten verses ... up to His statement: 'Those are innocent of what they say. For them is forgiveness and a noble provision' [an-Nur 24:26]. Abu Bakr said to Aisha: 'Stand and thank the Messenger of Allah.' She said: 'No, by Allah, I will thank only Allah who declared me innocent.' But that was not due to anything in her heart towards the Messenger of Allah, for her station is above that; rather, she was absorbed in the station of witnessing, so she witnessed only Allah. Among those who spoke in the slander was Misṭaḥ, and Abu Bakr used to spend on him. When the news reached him that he had spoken in the slander, he swore not to spend on him. Then Allah revealed: 'And let not those among you who are blessed and have means swear' [an-Nur 24:22] the verse. So Abu Bakr resumed the expense as before.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage narrates the full story of the slander (ifk) against Aisha, the wife of the Prophet. It begins with the journey to the Muraysi' expedition, where Aisha's necklace was lost. She fell behind to look for it, and was left alone. Safwan ibn al-Muʿaṭṭal found her and brought her back. This incident was used by hypocrites to spread slander. The Prophet gathered the Companions and asked for advice. Saʿd ibn Muʿādh and Saʿd ibn ʿUbāda disagreed, nearly causing conflict between the Aws and Khazraj. Then Allah revealed ten verses from Surat an-Nur declaring Aisha's innocence. The account ends with Aisha's response to her father's request to thank the Prophet, and the incident of Misṭaḥ and Abu Bakr's oath, which was overruled by Quranic revelation. The story illustrates the divine vindication and the proper response of the believers.

Key Terms
عقْد
هودج
صفوان بن المعطل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Aisha fall behind the caravan?
A) She was sick.
B) She lost her necklace.
C) She wanted to pray.
D) She was tired.

Key Takeaway
A simple loss led to a situation where Aisha was alone, but Safwan acted honorably.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself in a situation where others might misunderstand your intentions (like Aisha and Safwan), do you act with the same level of caution and modesty to avoid even the appearance of wrongdoing? How can you apply their example to your daily interactions?
?
The Prophet's lot-casting shows that even his actions were subject to divine will. In your life, do you truly trust that Allah's choice for you, even in seemingly random events, is for the best? What might change if you lived with that certainty?
?
Aisha lost a valuable necklace and ended up in a vulnerable position. Are you more attached to material things than to your trust in Allah's plan? What 'lost necklace' in your life might be a test to see where your true loyalty lies?

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
The Slander and the Near Conflict
Narration of the spread of slander and the Prophet's response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the slander spread and how the Prophet handled the situation, including the near-conflict between the Aws and Khazraj.

Core Idea
The slander threatened to divide the community, but the Prophet's wisdom averted disaster.

When the slander reached the Prophet, he gathered the Companions to address it. The response of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh and Sa'd ibn 'Ubada reveals the tribal tensions and the Prophet's leadership.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the events.
Focus on the reactions of the Prophet and the two Sa'ds.
2
Analyze the Prophet's speech
Note how the Prophet defended his family and asked for help without directly accusing anyone.
His words show his wisdom and restraint.
3
Examine the exchange between Sa'ds
Understand the tribal dynamics: Sa'd ibn Mu'adh offered to kill if from the Aws; Sa'd ibn 'Ubada challenged him.
This nearly caused a fight between the Aws and Khazraj.
4
Observe the Prophet's resolution
The Prophet ordered them to ignore the matter and not fight.
This prevented internal conflict while awaiting divine guidance.

What did Sa'd ibn Mu'adh offer to do if the slanderer was from the Khazraj?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When your reputation or family honor is attacked, what is your first instinct—to defend aggressively or to seek a wise resolution? How can you emulate the Prophet's restraint in this passage?
?
The near fight between the Aws and Khazraj shows how quickly unity can be shattered. Is there a relationship or community tension in your life that you are fueling instead of calming? What would it cost you to 'ignore' a provocation for the sake of peace?
?
The Prophet asked 'who will excuse me?' but did not demand bloodshed. Have you ever sought support for a just cause but then wisely de-escalated when things went too far? How can you balance defending truth with preserving unity?

The Divine Vindication and Lessons
Narration of the revelation of innocence and subsequent events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah declared Aisha's innocence through revelation and the lessons from her response and Abu Bakr's incident.

Core Idea
Allah Himself defended Aisha, teaching believers to trust in divine justice.

The climax of the story is the revelation of ten verses from Surah an-Nur, clearing Aisha of all accusations. Her response to her father and the resolution with Mistah provide enduring lessons.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the revelation and reactions.
Note the exact verses mentioned.
2
Understand the Quranic declaration
Allah revealed ten verses declaring the slanderers guilty and Aisha innocent.
This is the central divine vindication.
3
Analyze Aisha's response
Aisha refused to thank the Prophet, saying she only thanks Allah. Understand the reason given: she was absorbed in witnessing Allah.
This shows her deep faith.
4
Examine the Mistah incident
Abu Bakr swore to stop supporting Mistah for his role in the slander, but a new revelation instructed him to forgive.
This teaches forgiveness and not swearing off charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحاصل قصتها أن النبي كان إذا أراد سفراً أقرع بين نسائه، فلما أراد صلى الله عليه وسلم التوجه لغزوة بني المصطلق وتسمى غزوة المُرَيسيع أقرع بينهن، فخرجت القرعة على عائشة، فتوجهت معه، ففي رجوعهم منها ضاع عقدها، وكان من جزعِ أظفار - يفتح الجيم وسكون الزاي أو فتحها - أي : خرز منسوب لأظفار ؛ وهي بلدة في اليمن، فتخلفت في طلبه فحُمِلَ هودجها، وهو مركب من مراكب النساء كالقبة، ظنا أنها فيه ؛ لأنها كانت خفيفة كما أخبرت بذلك، وسار القوم ورجعت إليهم فلم تجدهم، فمكثت مكانها، فأخذها النوم، فمرَّ بها صفوان بن المعطل، وكان يعرفها قبل آية الحجاب، وكان يتخلف ليلتقط ما يسقط من المتاع أو لأنه كان ثقيل النوم فبرك ناقته، وولاها ظهره، وصار يسترجع جهراً حتى استيقظت وحملها على الناقة، ولم ينظر إليها، وقاد بها الناقة موليها ظهره حتى أدرك بها النبي ، فرَمَوْها به، وفشا ذلك بين المنافقين وضعفاء المسلمين فشق ذلك على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فجمع الصحابة، وقال: يا معشر المسلمين ؛ مَنْ يعذرني من رجل قد بلغني أذاه في أهل بيتي، فوالله ما علمت على أهلي إلا خيراً، ولقد ذكروا رجلاً ما علمت عليه إلا خيراً، فقال سعد بن سيد الأوس أنا أعذرك منه يا رسول الله ؛ إن كان من الأوس ضربت عنقه، وإن كان : من إخواننا من الخزرج أمرتنا ففعلنا أمرك . فقال سعد بن عبادة سيد الخزرج : كذبت لا تقدر على قتله، فَهم الأوس والخزرج بالقتال، فأمرهم النبي بالإعراض عن ذلك، فأنزل الله في براءتها إِنَّ الَّذِينَ جَاءُو بالإفكِ عُصْبَةٌ مِنكر [النور: ۱۱] العشر آيات ... إلى قوله تعالى: أُولَيكَ مُبَرَّءُونَ مِمَّا يَقُولُونَ لَهُم مَّغْفِرَةٌ وَرِزْقٌ كَرِيمٌ﴾ [النور: ٢٦] . فقال أبو بكر لعائشة : قومي فاشكري لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت : لا والله لا أشكرُ إلا الله الذي برأني ، لكن لم يكن ذلك لشيء كان في نفسها من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فإن مقامها يَجِلُّ عن ذلك، وإنما استغرقت في مقام الشهود، فلم تشهد إلا الله، وكان ممَّن تكلَّم في الإفك مِسْطح، وكان أبو بكر يُنفق عليه، فلما بلغه أنه تكلم في الإفك حلف لا ينفق عليه ، فأنزل الله: ﴿وَلَا يَأْتَلِ أُولُوا الْفَضْلِ مِنكُمْ وَالسَّعَةِ [النور: ۲۲] الآية، فأعاد أبو بكر النفقة كما كانت .

He had known her before the verse of hijab. He used to lag behind to pick up anything that fell of the baggage, or because he was a heavy sleeper. He made his camel kneel, turned his back to her, and began to recite the istirjāʿ aloud until she woke up. He mounted her on the camel without looking at her, led the camel with his back turned to her until he reached the Prophet with her. They accused her (of wrongdoing) because of that. This spread among the hypocrites and weak Muslims, and that distressed the Prophet. He gathered the Companions and said: 'O Muslims, who will excuse me concerning a man whose harm has reached my family? By Allah, I know nothing but good of my family, and they have mentioned a man of whom I know nothing but good.' Saʿd ibn Muʿādh, the leader of the Aws, said: 'O Messenger of Allah, I will excuse you concerning him. If he is from the Aws, I will strike his neck; if he is from our brothers of the Khazraj, command us and we will do your command.' Saʿd ibn ʿUbāda, the leader of the Khazraj, said: 'You lie! You cannot kill him.' The Aws and Khazraj nearly came to fighting, but the Prophet ordered them to ignore that. Then Allah revealed concerning her innocence: 'Indeed, those who came with the slander are a group among you' [an-Nur 24:11] ten verses ... up to His statement: 'Those are innocent of what they say. For them is forgiveness and a noble provision' [an-Nur 24:26]. Abu Bakr said to Aisha: 'Stand and thank the Messenger of Allah.' She said: 'No, by Allah, I will thank only Allah who declared me innocent.' But that was not due to anything in her heart towards the Messenger of Allah, for her station is above that; rather, she was absorbed in the station of witnessing, so she witnessed only Allah. Among those who spoke in the slander was Misṭaḥ, and Abu Bakr used to spend on him. When the news reached him that he had spoken in the slander, he swore not to spend on him. Then Allah revealed: 'And let not those among you who are blessed and have means swear' [an-Nur 24:22] the verse. So Abu Bakr resumed the expense as before.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage narrates the full story of the slander (ifk) against Aisha, the wife of the Prophet. It begins with the journey to the Muraysi' expedition, where Aisha's necklace was lost. She fell behind to look for it, and was left alone. Safwan ibn al-Muʿaṭṭal found her and brought her back. This incident was used by hypocrites to spread slander. The Prophet gathered the Companions and asked for advice. Saʿd ibn Muʿādh and Saʿd ibn ʿUbāda disagreed, nearly causing conflict between the Aws and Khazraj. Then Allah revealed ten verses from Surat an-Nur declaring Aisha's innocence. The account ends with Aisha's response to her father's request to thank the Prophet, and the incident of Misṭaḥ and Abu Bakr's oath, which was overruled by Quranic revelation. The story illustrates the divine vindication and the proper response of the believers.

Key Terms
براءة
الإفك
مسطح
أبو بكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Aisha refused to thank the Prophet out of disrespect.
Correction: The passage explains that her station of witnessing Allah prevented her from focusing on anyone else; it was not a lack of respect.

Checkpoint
Why did Aisha refuse to thank the Prophet?
A) She was angry at him.
B) She was absorbed in witnessing Allah.
C) She did not believe the revelation.
D) She wanted to thank her father first.

Key Takeaway
Allah's revelation vindicated Aisha and taught lessons of forgiveness and trust in divine justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are wronged, do you immediately seek human vindication and approval, or do you, like Aisha, first turn to Allah alone? What would it take for you to be so absorbed in witnessing Allah's justice that the opinions of others become secondary?
?
Abu Bakr had every right to cut off support to Misṭaḥ, but Allah commanded him to forgive and continue generosity. Is there someone in your life whom you have cut off or withheld kindness from, believing you are justified? Will you let Allah's command override your hurt and restore that relationship?
?
Aisha thanked only Allah despite the Prophet's role in her vindication. Are there blessings in your life that you attribute to people while forgetting the ultimate Giver? How can you shift your thanks to be directed primarily to Allah, even when He uses others as means?

The Ten Companions Promised Paradise
The author explains the exclusive mention of ten companions as promised paradise and cites the hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the ten companions are specifically singled out as being promised Paradise, and the significance of the hadith that mentions them.

Core Idea
The ten are specified because they are listed together in a famous hadith; others are also promised Paradise.

In this passage, the author addresses a potential misunderstanding: why are only ten companions mentioned as being promised Paradise when many others, including Hasan, Husayn, and Fatima, are also certainly among the people of Paradise? The answer lies in a well-known hadith that gathers these ten together. This lesson explores that hadith and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to understand the author's point.
Notice the author acknowledges others are also promised Paradise.
2
Identify the hadith
The author cites a hadith from al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Hibban. List the ten names mentioned.
This hadith is the basis for the specification.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask: Why does the author clarify this? What misconception is being addressed?
The clarification shows that the specification does not exclude others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتخصيص هؤلاء العشرة بأنهم مبشرون بالجنة مع أن المبشرين بالجنة أكثر منهم، فإن الحسن والحسين وأمهما فاطمة من المبشرين بالجنة قطعاً؛ لأنَّ هؤلاء العشرة جمعوا في حديث مشهور ففي الترمذي وابن حبان من حديث عبد الرحمن بن عوف عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: «أبو بكر في الجنة، وعمرُ في الجنة، وعثمان في الجنة، وعلي في الجنة، وطلحة في الجنة والزبير في الجنة، وعبد الرحمن بن عوف في الجنة، وسعد بن أبي وقاص في الجنة، وأبو عبيدة بن الجراح في الجنة، وسعيد بن زيد في الجنة»
And the specification of these ten as being given glad tidings of Paradise, while those given glad tidings of Paradise are more than them, for al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and their mother Fatima are from those given glad tidings of Paradise definitively; because these ten are gathered in a well-known hadith, in al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Hibban from the hadith of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Abu Bakr is in Paradise, and Umar is in Paradise, and Uthman is in Paradise, and Ali is in Paradise, and Talha is in Paradise, and al-Zubayr is in Paradise, and Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf is in Paradise, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas is in Paradise, and Abu Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah is in Paradise, and Sa'id ibn Zayd is in Paradise.'
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory note on why the ten companions are specifically singled out as those promised Paradise, despite there being many others (like al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Fatima) who are also certainly among the people of Paradise. The author explains that the reason is that these ten are gathered together in a well-known hadith narrated by Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, which the author then quotes. The hadith lists each of the ten by name, affirming that each will be in Paradise. The passage thus serves to clarify that the special mention of the ten does not negate the status of other companions; rather, it highlights a specific textual tradition.

Key Takeaway
The ten companions are specifically mentioned as promised Paradise because they are listed together in a well-known hadith, but many other companions are also promised Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
This hadith reminds us that Allah's mercy is vast and that Paradise is promised to many. But are you living with the certainty that you will be among them? What are you doing today that demonstrates that certainty?
