The Rank of the People of Badr
Defines the rank of the people of Badr and provides details on their number and resources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the lofty rank of all participants of Badr, their number, and the significance of the name.

Core Idea
Every warrior of Badr, alive or martyred, shares an exalted rank.

The poem honors the people of Badr. This lesson unpacks who they were, why their rank is second only to the six from the ten, and clarifies that all participants—not just martyrs—share that honor. We'll also look at the number of warriors and the etymology of 'Badr'.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening explanation
Read the Arabic passage from 'فَأَهْلُ بَدْرٍ العَظِيمِ الشَّانِ' to 'بين من لم يُستشهد فيها'. Understand that the rank of Ahl Badr is just below the six from the ten.
The six from the ten likely refer to the first six Caliphs among the ten promised Paradise.
2
Understand the rank equality
Notice that the author explicitly says there is no difference between martyred and surviving participants—all have the same rank.
3
Learn the etymology and count
Review the derivation of 'Badr' and the differing counts (317 vs 313), and the significance of the number 313 matching Talut's companions.
The Prophet rejoiced at the count.
4
Note the army composition
The Muslims had only two horsemen and seventy camels, highlighting their modest resources.

وقال: عِدَّة أصحاب طالوت (۲)، وكان معهم فرسان فقط، إحداهما للمقداد بن الأسود، والثاني للزبير بن العوام، وفي عبارة بعضهم ثلاثة أفراس، وكان أيضاً سبعون بعيراً، وكان المشركون ألفاً ومعهم منة فرس وسبع مئة بعير، وسبق المشركون إلى ماء بدر، فأحرزوه، ولم يصل إليه المسلمون، فعَطشوا وأصبح غالبهم جنباً، فوسوس الشيطان لبعضهم، وقال تزعمون أنكم على الحق، وفيكم نبي الله، وأنكم أولياء الله وقد غلبكم المشركون على الماء، وأنتم عطاش، وتصلون محدثين معهم مجنبين، وما ينتظر أعداؤكم إلا أن يقطع العطش رقابكم، ويُذهب قواكم، فيتحكمون فيكم كيف شاؤوا فأرسل الله عليهم مطراً وسال منه الوادي، فاغتسلوا وتوضؤوا وشربوا وشربت دوابهم ومَلؤوا الأسقية، وثَبَّتَ المطرُ رمل الأرض، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي تحت شجرة حتى أصبح، وصنعوا عريشاً له، فكان فيه هو وأبو بكر، وقام سعد بن معاذ على بابه مُتوشّحاً بالسيف، ومشى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في موضع المعركة، وجعل يشير بيده: هذا مَصْرَعُ فلانٍ وهذا مَصْرَعُ فلان إن شاء الله تعالى، فما تعدَّى أحدٌ منهم موضع إشارته، وسَوَّى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الصفوف، وخطب خُطبةً يحثهم فيها على الثبات، وابتهل في الدعاء، حتى قال: اللهمَّ إِنْ تُهْلِكُ هذه العصابة اليوم لا تُعْبَدُ في الأرض، اللهم إني أُنشدك عهدك ووعدك، اللهم إن ظهروا على هذه العصابة ظهر الشرك، ولا يقومُ لك دين» (١)، وركع ركعتين، وكان كثيراً ما يقول في سجوده إذ ذاك: يا حي يا قيوم يكرِّرُها مُدَّةً، وهو ساجد حتى سقط رداؤه من كثرة ما ابتهل فألقاه عليه أبو بكر، وقال: يا نبي الله؛ كفاك تناشد ربَّك فإنه سينجز لك ما وعدك، ثم قاتل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بنفسه قتالاً شديداً، وحرّض المسلمين على القتال، فقال: قوموا إلى جنة عرضها السماوات والأرض، وكانوا إذا اشتدَّ البأس اتقوا برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فكان أقربهم للمشركين، فأخذ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كفا من حصى فرمی به المشركين وقال شاهتِ الوجوه (۲)؛ أي: قُبِّحَتْ، اللهم أرعب قلوبهم، وزلزل أقدامهم، فأصاب أعين جميعهم وانهزموا ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: سَيُهزم الجَمْعُ وَيُولُونَ الدُّبُرَ) [القمر: 45]، وأُسِرَ منهم سبعون، وقتل من أشرافهم سبعون، كأبي جهل وأمية بن خلف، وكان مع المسلمين سبعون من الجن وثلاثة آلاف من الملائكة مردفين، يتبع خلف وعتبة بن ربيعة.
So the people of Badr of great importance, and the people of Uhud, and the pledge of Ridwan. His statement: ('So the people of Badr') with the nunation moved for meter; meaning: the people of the Battle of Badr; so in the speech there is an omitted genitive construction, and their rank follows the rank of the six of the ten, and there is no difference between those who were martyred in it, and they are fourteen men: six from the Emigrants and eight from the Helpers, and those who were not martyred in it. And 'Badr' is a name for the valley or for a well built by a man in the Jahiliyya, called Badr, and in 'al-Sira al-Shamiyya': Badr is a famous village about four stages from Medina. The people of the Battle of Badr were three hundred and seventeen men, and in a narration: and thirteen men, and this narration is supported by the fact that he ordered them [to be counted] and informed that they were three hundred and thirteen, so he rejoiced at that, and said: 'The number of the companions of Talut' (2), and with them were only two horsemen, one of them belonging to Miqdad ibn al-Aswad, and the second to al-Zubayr ibn al-Awwam, and in the expression of some of them there were three horses, and there were also seventy camels, and the polytheists were a thousand, with them a hundred horses and seven hundred camels, and the polytheists preceded [the Muslims] to the water of Badr, so they secured it, and the Muslims did not reach it, so they became thirsty and most of them became junub, so Satan whispered to some of them, saying: 'You claim that you are upon the truth, and among you is the Prophet of Allah, and that you are the allies of Allah, yet the polytheists have overcome you over the water, and you are thirsty, and you pray while in a state of minor impurity and major impurity, and your enemies await only that thirst may cut your necks and take away your strength, so they may control you as they wish.' So Allah sent rain upon them, and the valley flowed from it, so they washed themselves and performed wudu and drank and their animals drank and filled the water skins, and the rain solidified the sand of the ground, and the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, prayed under a tree until morning, and they made an arbor for him, so he and Abu Bakr were in it, and Sa'd ibn Mu'adh stood at his door girded with a sword, and the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, walked in the place of the battle and began to point with his hand: 'This is the place of death of so-and-so, and this is the place of death of so-and-so, if Allah wills.' So not one of them exceeded the place he indicated. And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, straightened the ranks and gave a sermon urging them to steadfastness, and he prayed earnestly until he said: 'O Allah, if You destroy this group today, You will not be worshipped on the earth. O Allah, I implore You by Your covenant and Your promise. O Allah, if they overcome this group, polytheism will appear, and Your religion will not stand' (1). And he bowed two rak'ahs, and he often said in his prostration at that time: 'O Living, O Self-Subsistent,' repeating it for a while, prostrating until his cloak fell from the abundance of his supplication, so Abu Bakr threw it over him and said: 'O Prophet of Allah, enough of your imploring your Lord, for He will fulfill what He promised you.' Then the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, fought himself a severe fight, and urged the Muslims to fight, saying: 'Rise to a Garden whose width is the heavens and the earth.' And when the battle became intense, they sought protection behind the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, so he was the closest of them to the polytheists. Then the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, took a handful of pebbles and threw them at the polytheists, saying: 'May their faces be disfigured' (2); i.e., may they be ugly. 'O Allah, terrify their hearts and shake their feet.' So it hit the eyes of all of them, and they were defeated while the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'The multitude will be defeated and they will turn their backs' [Al-Qamar: 45]. And seventy of them were taken captive, and seventy of their nobles were killed, such as Abu Jahl and Umayya ibn Khalaf, and with the Muslims there were seventy jinn and three thousand angels following, behind Khalid? and Utba ibn Rabi'a.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the poetic line about the people of Badr. It begins by explaining that the phrase 'the people of Badr' refers to the participants in the Battle of Badr, and their rank follows that of the six from the ten (i.e., the first six Caliphs? Actually the six from the ten refers to the ten promised paradise, but specifically the first six? The text says 'the six from the ten' – likely meaning the six who were Caliphs? It needs careful reading. The author then states that there is no difference between those martyred in Badr and those who survived; all have the same rank. He then gives the etymology of 'Badr' and notes the number of participants: 317 or 313, citing that the Prophet rejoiced at the number 313 as it matches the number of Talut's companions. He then gives details about the horses and camels. The narrative then shifts to the battle itself: the polytheists seized the water, the Muslims became thirsty and junub, Satan whispered doubts, but Allah sent rain, allowing them to purify and drink. The Prophet prayed, made an arbor, pinpointed the locations of the enemy's deaths, straightened ranks, gave a sermon, prayed earnestly, and even fought personally. The climax is the Prophet throwing pebbles at the polytheists, causing them to be defeated. The passage ends with the number of captives and slain, and notes the presence of jinn and angels. The entire account serves to illustrate the honor of the people of Badr and the miraculous aid given to the Prophet in this battle.

Correction: All participants of Badr, whether martyred or not, share the same elevated rank according to the author.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Is there a person in your life whom you consider more blessed because they died in a noble cause, while you secretly think of those still alive as lesser? How can you realign your heart to honor both equally, as Allah does?

The Battle of Badr and Miraculous Aid
Narrates the Battle of Badr, highlighting divine aid and miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sequence of events at Badr and the miracles that ensured Muslim victory.

Core Idea
Allah sent rain, angels, and the Prophet's throw to secure victory at Badr.

The Battle of Badr was a decisive moment for the early Muslim community. This lesson follows the narrative from the polytheists' seizure of water to the miraculous defeat. You'll see how the Prophet's prayers, divine intervention, and the support of angels and jinn turned the tide.

Guided Path
1
Read the battle narrative
Read from 'وكان المشركون ألفاً' to the end. Notice the sequence: water conflict, rain, Prophet's actions before battle.
The narrative is vivid and detailed.
2
Identify the miracles
Look for the rain miracle, the Prophet's accurate predictions of death locations, and the pebble throw that blinded the enemy.
These are signs of prophethood.
3
Note the divine support
See the mention of seventy jinn and three thousand angels aiding the Muslims.

بدر قرية مشهورة على نحو أربع مراحل من المدينة. وكان أهل غزوة بدر ثلاث مئة وسبعة عشر رجلاً، وفي رواية: وثلاثة عشر رجلاً»، ويُؤيد هذه الرواية أنه هو أمر بعدهم فأخبر بأنهم ثلاث مئة وثلاثة عشر ففرح بذلك، وقال: عِدَّة أصحاب طالوت (۲)، وكان معهم فرسان فقط، إحداهما للمقداد بن الأسود، والثاني للزبير بن العوام، وفي عبارة بعضهم ثلاثة أفراس، وكان أيضاً سبعون بعيراً، وكان المشركون ألفاً ومعهم منة فرس وسبع مئة بعير، وسبق المشركون إلى ماء بدر، فأحرزوه، ولم يصل إليه المسلمون، فعَطشوا وأصبح غالبهم جنباً، فوسوس الشيطان لبعضهم، وقال تزعمون أنكم على الحق، وفيكم نبي الله، وأنكم أولياء الله وقد غلبكم المشركون على الماء، وأنتم عطاش، وتصلون محدثين معهم مجنبين، وما ينتظر أعداؤكم إلا أن يقطع العطش رقابكم، ويُذهب قواكم، فيتحكمون فيكم كيف شاؤوا فأرسل الله عليهم مطراً وسال منه الوادي، فاغتسلوا وتوضؤوا وشربوا وشربت دوابهم ومَلؤوا الأسقية، وثَبَّتَ المطرُ رمل الأرض، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي تحت شجرة حتى أصبح، وصنعوا عريشاً له، فكان فيه هو وأبو بكر، وقام سعد بن معاذ على بابه مُتوشّحاً بالسيف، ومشى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في موضع المعركة، وجعل يشير بيده: هذا مَصْرَعُ فلانٍ وهذا مَصْرَعُ فلان إن شاء الله تعالى، فما تعدَّى أحدٌ منهم موضع إشارته، وسَوَّى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الصفوف، وخطب خُطبةً يحثهم فيها على الثبات، وابتهل في الدعاء، حتى قال: اللهمَّ إِنْ تُهْلِكُ هذه العصابة اليوم لا تُعْبَدُ في الأرض، اللهم إني أُنشدك عهدك ووعدك، اللهم إن ظهروا على هذه العصابة ظهر الشرك، ولا يقومُ لك دين» (١)، وركع ركعتين، وكان كثيراً ما يقول في سجوده إذ ذاك: يا حي يا قيوم يكرِّرُها مُدَّةً، وهو ساجد حتى سقط رداؤه من كثرة ما ابتهل فألقاه عليه أبو بكر، وقال: يا نبي الله؛ كفاك تناشد ربَّك فإنه سينجز لك ما وعدك، ثم قاتل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بنفسه قتالاً شديداً، وحرّض المسلمين على القتال، فقال: قوموا إلى جنة عرضها السماوات والأرض، وكانوا إذا اشتدَّ البأس اتقوا برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فكان أقربهم للمشركين، فأخذ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كفا من حصى فرمی به المشركين وقال شاهتِ الوجوه (۲)؛ أي: قُبِّحَتْ، اللهم أرعب قلوبهم، وزلزل أقدامهم، فأصاب أعين جميعهم وانهزموا ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: سَيُهزم الجَمْعُ وَيُولُونَ الدُّبُرَ) [القمر: 45]، وأُسِرَ منهم سبعون، وقتل من أشرافهم سبعون، كأبي جهل وأمية بن خلف، وكان مع المسلمين سبعون من الجن وثلاثة آلاف من الملائكة مردفين، يتبع خلف وعتبة بن ربيعة.
So the people of Badr of great importance, and the people of Uhud, and the pledge of Ridwan. His statement: ('So the people of Badr') with the nunation moved for meter; meaning: the people of the Battle of Badr; so in the speech there is an omitted genitive construction, and their rank follows the rank of the six of the ten, and there is no difference between those who were martyred in it, and they are fourteen men: six from the Emigrants and eight from the Helpers, and those who were not martyred in it. And 'Badr' is a name for the valley or for a well built by a man in the Jahiliyya, called Badr, and in 'al-Sira al-Shamiyya': Badr is a famous village about four stages from Medina. The people of the Battle of Badr were three hundred and seventeen men, and in a narration: and thirteen men, and this narration is supported by the fact that he ordered them [to be counted] and informed that they were three hundred and thirteen, so he rejoiced at that, and said: 'The number of the companions of Talut' (2), and with them were only two horsemen, one of them belonging to Miqdad ibn al-Aswad, and the second to al-Zubayr ibn al-Awwam, and in the expression of some of them there were three horses, and there were also seventy camels, and the polytheists were a thousand, with them a hundred horses and seven hundred camels, and the polytheists preceded [the Muslims] to the water of Badr, so they secured it, and the Muslims did not reach it, so they became thirsty and most of them became junub, so Satan whispered to some of them, saying: 'You claim that you are upon the truth, and among you is the Prophet of Allah, and that you are the allies of Allah, yet the polytheists have overcome you over the water, and you are thirsty, and you pray while in a state of minor impurity and major impurity, and your enemies await only that thirst may cut your necks and take away your strength, so they may control you as they wish.' So Allah sent rain upon them, and the valley flowed from it, so they washed themselves and performed wudu and drank and their animals drank and filled the water skins, and the rain solidified the sand of the ground, and the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, prayed under a tree until morning, and they made an arbor for him, so he and Abu Bakr were in it, and Sa'd ibn Mu'adh stood at his door girded with a sword, and the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, walked in the place of the battle and began to point with his hand: 'This is the place of death of so-and-so, and this is the place of death of so-and-so, if Allah wills.' So not one of them exceeded the place he indicated. And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, straightened the ranks and gave a sermon urging them to steadfastness, and he prayed earnestly until he said: 'O Allah, if You destroy this group today, You will not be worshipped on the earth. O Allah, I implore You by Your covenant and Your promise. O Allah, if they overcome this group, polytheism will appear, and Your religion will not stand' (1). And he bowed two rak'ahs, and he often said in his prostration at that time: 'O Living, O Self-Subsistent,' repeating it for a while, prostrating until his cloak fell from the abundance of his supplication, so Abu Bakr threw it over him and said: 'O Prophet of Allah, enough of your imploring your Lord, for He will fulfill what He promised you.' Then the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, fought himself a severe fight, and urged the Muslims to fight, saying: 'Rise to a Garden whose width is the heavens and the earth.' And when the battle became intense, they sought protection behind the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, so he was the closest of them to the polytheists. Then the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, took a handful of pebbles and threw them at the polytheists, saying: 'May their faces be disfigured' (2); i.e., may they be ugly. 'O Allah, terrify their hearts and shake their feet.' So it hit the eyes of all of them, and they were defeated while the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'The multitude will be defeated and they will turn their backs' [Al-Qamar: 45]. And seventy of them were taken captive, and seventy of their nobles were killed, such as Abu Jahl and Umayya ibn Khalaf, and with the Muslims there were seventy jinn and three thousand angels following, behind Khalid? and Utba ibn Rabi'a.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the poetic line about the people of Badr. It begins by explaining that the phrase 'the people of Badr' refers to the participants in the Battle of Badr, and their rank follows that of the six from the ten (i.e., the first six Caliphs? Actually the six from the ten refers to the ten promised paradise, but specifically the first six? The text says 'the six from the ten' – likely meaning the six who were Caliphs? It needs careful reading. The author then states that there is no difference between those martyred in Badr and those who survived; all have the same rank. He then gives the etymology of 'Badr' and notes the number of participants: 317 or 313, citing that the Prophet rejoiced at the number 313 as it matches the number of Talut's companions. He then gives details about the horses and camels. The narrative then shifts to the battle itself: the polytheists seized the water, the Muslims became thirsty and junub, Satan whispered doubts, but Allah sent rain, allowing them to purify and drink. The Prophet prayed, made an arbor, pinpointed the locations of the enemy's deaths, straightened ranks, gave a sermon, prayed earnestly, and even fought personally. The climax is the Prophet throwing pebbles at the polytheists, causing them to be defeated. The passage ends with the number of captives and slain, and notes the presence of jinn and angels. The entire account serves to illustrate the honor of the people of Badr and the miraculous aid given to the Prophet in this battle.

Checkpoint
What was Satan's argument to the Muslims before the rain?
A) They were outnumbered and should flee.
B) They claimed truth yet were defeated over water and unable to pray properly.
C) The polytheists were stronger due to better weapons.
D) The Prophet had abandoned them.

Key Takeaway
The Battle of Badr was won through divine aid, including rain, the Prophet's accurate predictions, and angelic assistance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a seemingly impossible situation, do you, like the Prophet, turn to Allah with urgent, repeated supplication until your cloak falls? Or do you rely on your own planning?
?
The Muslims at Badr were outnumbered, thirsty, and spiritually impure. Yet Allah sent rain and angels. What 'dry' trial are you enduring right now where you need to trust that Allah's help will come at the perfect moment?
?
The Prophet's accurate predictions required complete trust in Allah's promise. Is there a promise from Allah in the Quran that you are struggling to believe will be fulfilled in your life? What step will you take today to strengthen that trust?

Prophethood
beginner
5 min
The Miracle of Rain at Badr
Describes the miracle of rain during the Battle of Badr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the rain at Badr was a direct divine miracle supporting the Muslims and affirming prophethood.

Core Idea
Allah sent rain as a direct answer to need, stabilizing and purifying.

The Battle of Badr began with severe thirst threatening the Muslims. In a desperate situation, Allah sent rain that not only quenched their thirst but also strengthened their position. This event is presented as a clear sign of divine intervention.

Guided Path
1
Read the rain miracle passage
Read the Arabic passage describing the thirst and the rain. Notice the detailed effects: washing, drinking, and stabilizing the sand.
The rain is described as coming from Allah in response to the situation.
2
Identify the miraculous elements
List the specific benefits of the rain: it provided water for ablution, drinking, and animals, and it solidified the ground. Consider why each detail matters.
The rain was not ordinary—it came at a critical moment.
3
Connect to prophethood evidence
Reflect on how this miracle serves as evidence for the Prophet's truthfulness. The rain was a direct answer to the Muslims' need, showing Allah's support.
This event is part of the broader argument for prophethood.

O Allah, I implore You by Your covenant and promise. O Allah, if they prevail over this group, polytheism will appear, and Your religion will not stand.' When the battle became severe, they sought protection with the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, so he was the closest of them to the polytheists. 'O Allah, terrify their hearts and shake their feet.' [continuation of the narrative including details about angels, Iblis, etc.]
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative of the Battle of Badr, intended to illustrate divine assistance and angelic support as signs of prophethood. The author describes the Muslims' severe thirst and the miraculous rain that provided water and stabilized the terrain. The Prophet's supplication is highlighted, especially his desperate plea to Allah that if the believers were destroyed, He would not be worshipped. Abu Bakr comforts him. The Prophet then personally fought and encouraged the Muslims. He threw pebbles at the polytheists, causing them to be defeated, fulfilling the Quranic prophecy. The narrative continues with details of the angels: initially 3,000, then 5,000, appearing as white-clad riders. The wounds of the slain polytheists had a distinctive burn-like mark. Iblis, disguised as Suraqa, initially encouraged the polytheists but fled when he saw the angels. The Prophet smiled during prayer because he saw the Archangel Michael returning from pursuit. Jibril later came to the Prophet and asked if he was satisfied, to which the Prophet replied yes. The author explains the wisdom of having multiple angels fight alongside the Muslims, rather than a single angel annihilating the enemy: it preserves the normal order of causes and supports the Muslim army in a customary manner. Ibn Abbas is quoted saying that angels fought only at Badr but attend other battles to increase the Muslim numbers. The entire account serves to reinforce the truth of prophethood through manifest miracles and divine intervention.

What did the rain help the Muslims do, according to the passage?
A) Only drink
B) Perform ablution, drink, and fill waterskins
C) Strengthen weapons
D) Build shelters

Key Takeaway
The rain at Badr was a clear divine miracle that met every need of the Muslim army, affirming Allah's support for the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a seemingly impossible situation, do you truly believe that Allah can send relief in unexpected ways, just as He sent rain at Badr? What is one area of your life right now where you are waiting for Allah’s help? Will you commit to turning to Him in prayer tonight, as the Prophet prayed under the tree?
?
The rain at Badr benefited every aspect: physical, spiritual, and practical. Are you making dua for comprehensive help from Allah, or only for one thing? Write down three specific needs you have and ask Allah for a complete blessing — not just partial relief.
?
The Prophet was praying when the rain came. How consistent is your salah during crises? When are you most likely to abandon prayer? Will you promise to use prayer as your first resort, not your last, especially in your most desperate moments?

Prophethood
beginner
5 min
The Prophet's Supplication and Divine Assurance
Describes the Prophet's intense supplication and Abu Bakr's reassurance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the intensity of the Prophet's supplication at Badr and how it reflects complete reliance on Allah.

Core Idea
The Prophet's desperate prayer shows that victory comes only from Allah.

Before the battle, the Prophet urgently pleaded with Allah, stating that if the believers were destroyed, He would not be worshipped. Abu Bakr comforted him, expressing confidence in Allah's promise. This scene underscores the human aspect of prophethood and the importance of supplication.

Guided Path
1
Read the supplication passage
Read the Arabic text describing the Prophet's du'a and Abu Bakr's response. Notice the emotional intensity.
The Prophet raised his hands and even his cloak fell off.
2
Analyze the content of the du'a
Identify the key phrases: 'If You destroy this group, You will not be worshipped.' What does this indicate about the Prophet's concern?
His primary concern was the worship of Allah, not personal victory.
3
Understand Abu Bakr's role
Abu Bakr reassures the Prophet. What does this show about the relationship between the Prophet and his companion?
Abu Bakr's faith in Allah's promise was strong.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تحفة المريد على جوهرة التوحيد
مجنبين، وما ينتظر أعداؤكم إلا أن يقطع العطش رقابكم، ويُذهب قواكم، فيتحكمون فيكم كيف شاؤوا فأرسل الله عليهم مطراً وسال منه الوادي، فاغتسلوا وتوضؤوا وشربوا وشربت دوابهم ومَلؤوا الأسقية، وثَبَّتَ المطرُ رمل الأرض، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي تحت شجرة حتى أصبح ، وصنعوا عريشاً له ، فكان فيه هو وأبو بكر، وقام سعد بن معاذ على بابه مُتوشّحاً بالسيف، ومشى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في موضع المعركة، وجعل يشير بيده : هذا مَصْرَعُ فلانٍ وهذا مَصْرَعُ فلان إن شاء الله تعالى، فما تعدَّى أحدٌ منهم موضع إشارته ، وسَوَّى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الصفوف، وخطب خُطبةٌ يحثهم فيها على الثبات، وابتهل في الدعاء، حتى قال: اللهمَّ إِنْ تُهْلِكُ هذه العصابة اليوم لا تُعْبَدُ في الأرض ، اللهم إني أُنشدك عهدك ووعدك، اللهم إن ظهروا على هذه العصابة ظهر الشرك، ولا يقومُ لك دين» (١) ، وركع ركعتين، وكان كثيراً ما يقول في سجوده إذ ذاك : يا حي يا قيوم يكرِّرُها مُدَّةٌ، وهو ساجد حتى سقط رداؤه من كثرة ما ابتهل فألقاه عليه أبو بكر ، وقال : يا نبي الله ؛ كفاك تناشد ربَّك فإنه سينجز لك ما وعدك، ثم قاتل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بنفسه قتالاً شديداً، وحرّض المسلمين على القتال، فقال : قوموا إلى جنة عرضها السماوات والأرض، وكانوا إذا اشتدَّ البأس اتقوا برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فكان أقربهم للمشركين، فأخذ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كفا من حصى فرمی به المشركين وقال شاهتِ الوجوه (۲) ؛ أي: قُبِّحَتْ، اللهم أرعب قلوبهم، وزلزل أقدامهم، فأصاب أعين جميعهم وانهزموا ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : سَيُهزم الجَمْعُ وَيُولُونَ الدُّبُرَ) [القمر: ٤٥] ، وأُسِرَ منهم سبعون، وقتل من أشرافهم سبعون، كأبي جهل وأمية بـ وكان مع المسلمين سبعون من الجن وثلاثة آلاف من الملائكة مردفين، يتبع
خلف وعتبة بن ربيعة .
(1) أخرجه مسلم بنحوه (١٧٦٣).
(۲) روى الطبراني في المعجم الكبير ) (۳۱۲۸) عن حكيم بن حزام قال : لما كان يوم بدر، أمر رسول الله فأخذ كفا من الحصى فاستقبلنا به فرمی بها وقال: شاهت الوجوه، فأنزل الله عز وجل : وَمَا رَمَيْتَ إِذْ رَمَيْتَ وَلَكِن اللهَ رَمَى [الأنفال : ١٧ ] . وفي رواية: «قال لعلي ناولني كفا من حصى فناوله فرمی به وجوه القوم، فما بقي أحد من القوم إلا امتلأت عيناه من الحصى .

النبوات
بعضهم
بعضاً، ثم كملت خمسة آلاف فتمثلوا برجال بيض على خيل بُلْقٍ (۱) ، عمائمهم بيضُ قد أرخوا أطرافها بين أكتافهم وقيل : سُود، وقيل: صُفْر، وقيل: حُمْر ، وقيل خُضْر، فكأنهم أنواع وكان قتيلهم يُعرف بأثر السواد في الأعناق والبنان؛ أي: المفصل، مثل حَرْقِ النار (٢).
(۲)
وكان إبليس مع المشركين مُتصوّراً بصورة سراقة بن مالك، وكان معه راية، وقال : لا غالب لكم اليوم من الناس، وإني جارٌ لكم ؛ أي معين لكم فلما أقبل جبريل والملائكة نَكَصَ على عقبيه وقال : إني بريء منكم إني أرى ما لا ترون وصار يقول : اللهم إني أنشدك أني من المنظرين
·
(۳)
وتبسَّمَ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في صلاته، فسألوه عن ذلك بعد انقضائها، فقال: «مَرَّ ميكائيل وعلى جناحيه أثر الغبارِ ، وهو راجع من طلب القوم، فضحكَ إِليَّ فتبسمْتُ بي إليه (4)، وجاءه جبريل بعد القتال على فرس أحمر عليه درعه ومعه رمحه، فقال: یا محمد ؛ إن الله بعثني إليك وأمرني ألا أفارقك حتى ترضى، هل رضيت؟ قال: نعم. والحكمة في قتال الملائكة وحضورهم مع المسلمين مع أن الملك الواحد كجبريل يقدر على رفع الكفار، بل على اقتلاع الأرض أن تكون الملائكة عدداً و مدداً لجيش المسلمين على عادة مدد الجيوش؛ رعاية لصورة الأسباب التي أجراها الله بين عباده.
قال ابن عباس (٥) : (ولم تقاتل الملائكة إلا يوم بدر، ولكنها تحضر في كل قتال من قتال الكفار إلى يوم القيامة لتكثير سواد المسلمين).
(۱) (البلق) سواد وبياض.
(۲) انظر الروض الأنف» (۸۱) ، و (تاريخ الخميس في أحوال أنفس النفيس، (٣٨٣/١).
(۳) روى الطبراني في المعجم الكبير ) (٤٥٥٠) عن رفاعة بن رافع الأنصاري، قال: لما رأى إبليس ما تفعل الملائكة بالمشركين أشفق أن يخلص القتل إليه، فتشبث به الحارث بن هشام، وهو يظن مالك، فوكز في صدر الحارث فألقاه ، ثم خرج هارباً حتى ألقى نفسه في البحر،
أنه سراقة بن فرفع يديه فقال : اللهم إني أسألك نظرتك إياي
(٤) أخرجه أبو يعلى في مسنده (٢٠٦٠).
(ه) في (أ) (ابن عبد السلام).
Tuhfat al-Mureed on Jawharat al-Tawhid. ... (they were) avoiding (thirst), and your enemies are only waiting for thirst to cut your throats and take away your strength, so they control you as they wish. So Allah sent rain upon them and the valley flowed from it, so they washed and performed ablution and drank and their animals drank and filled the waterskins, and the rain stabilized the sand of the earth, while the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was praying under a tree until morning. They made a canopy for him, so he and Abu Bakr were in it, and Sa'd ibn Mu'adh stood at its door girded with a sword. The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, walked in the place of the battle and began to point with his hand: 'This is the fall of so-and-so, and this is the fall of so-and-so, if Allah wills.' So none of them exceeded the place of his indication. The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, arranged the ranks and gave a sermon urging them to steadfastness, and he implored in supplication until he said: 'O Allah, if You destroy this group today, You will not be worshipped on earth. O Allah, I implore You by Your covenant and promise. O Allah, if they prevail over this group, polytheism will appear, and Your religion will not stand.' (1) And he performed two rak'ahs, and he often said in his prostration at that time: 'O Living, O Self-Subsisting,' repeating it for a while while prostrating, until his cloak fell off due to the intensity of his supplication, so Abu Bakr threw it over him and said: 'O Prophet of Allah, enough of your imploring your Lord, for He will fulfill what He promised you.' Then the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, fought intensely himself and urged the Muslims to fight, saying: 'Rise to a Garden whose width is the heavens and the earth.' When the battle became severe, they sought protection with the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, so he was the closest of them to the polytheists. The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, took a handful of pebbles and threw them at the polytheists, saying: 'May the faces be disfigured' (2); that is, 'may they be ugly.' 'O Allah, terrify their hearts and shake their feet.' So it struck the eyes of all of them, and they were defeated, and the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was saying: 'The multitude will be defeated, and they will turn their backs' [Quran 54:45]. Seventy of them were captured, and seventy of their nobles were killed, such as Abu Jahl and Umayyah ibn Khalaf, and with the Muslims were seventy jinn and three thousand angels riding in succession... [continuation of the narrative including details about angels, Iblis, etc.]
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative of the Battle of Badr, intended to illustrate divine assistance and angelic support as signs of prophethood. The author describes the Muslims' severe thirst and the miraculous rain that provided water and stabilized the terrain. The Prophet's supplication is highlighted, especially his desperate plea to Allah that if the believers were destroyed, He would not be worshipped. Abu Bakr comforts him. The Prophet then personally fought and encouraged the Muslims. He threw pebbles at the polytheists, causing them to be defeated, fulfilling the Quranic prophecy. The narrative continues with details of the angels: initially 3,000, then 5,000, appearing as white-clad riders. The wounds of the slain polytheists had a distinctive burn-like mark. Iblis, disguised as Suraqa, initially encouraged the polytheists but fled when he saw the angels. The Prophet smiled during prayer because he saw the Archangel Michael returning from pursuit. Jibril later came to the Prophet and asked if he was satisfied, to which the Prophet replied yes. The author explains the wisdom of having multiple angels fight alongside the Muslims, rather than a single angel annihilating the enemy: it preserves the normal order of causes and supports the Muslim army in a customary manner. Ibn Abbas is quoted saying that angels fought only at Badr but attend other battles to increase the Muslim numbers. The entire account serves to reinforce the truth of prophethood through manifest miracles and divine intervention.

Key Terms
الدعاء
ابتهل
تناشد
عهد
وعد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Prophet was in despair or doubted Allah's promise.
Correction: The Prophet's intense supplication demonstrates his complete reliance on Allah and his deep concern for the faith, not lack of faith.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say in his supplication about the destruction of the believers?
A) They would be martyrs
B) Allah would not be worshipped on earth
C) The polytheists would convert
D) The battle would be lost

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's desperate du'a at Badr shows that victory comes only from Allah, and the believers must turn to Him in complete humility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a seemingly impossible situation, does your du'a reflect the same urgency as the Prophet's, or do you rely on your own efforts? What does your du'a reveal about what truly matters to you?
?
The Prophet feared that if the believers were destroyed, Allah would not be worshipped. Do you live your daily life with that same concern for Allah's worship? In what moments do you prioritize your own comfort over the cause of Allah?
?
Abu Bakr had complete confidence in Allah's promise. Are there promises of Allah that you struggle to trust in your own life? What specific promise from the Qur'an or Sunnah do you need to hold onto today? How will you act on that trust this week?

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
Angels at Badr and the Flight of Iblis
Describes angelic assistance and Iblis's flight at Badr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of angels in the Battle of Badr and the wisdom of their visible intervention.

Core Idea
Angels fought at Badr as a visible sign of divine support, while Iblis fled in fear.

The narrative continues with details of angelic assistance: initially 3,000 angels, then 5,000, appearing as riders. Iblis, disguised as Suraqa, encouraged the polytheists but fled when he saw the angels. The author explains why multiple angels were sent rather than a single one: to preserve the normal cause-and-effect order and to support the Muslim army in a customary manner.

Guided Path
1
Read the angel and Iblis passages
Read the Arabic text about the angels and Iblis. Note the numbers and descriptions.
The angels are described with specific colors and attire.
2
Understand the role of angels
The angels fought alongside the Muslims. Why did they appear in such numbers? Consider the author's explanation: 'rعاية لصورة الأسباب' (preserving the appearance of causes).
This shows that Allah works through ordinary means even in miracles.
3
Analyze Iblis's reaction
Iblis initially promised support but fled when he saw Jibril and the angels. What does this teach about the power of Allah?
Even the devil cannot withstand divine forces.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تحفة المريد على جوهرة التوحيد
مجنبين، وما ينتظر أعداؤكم إلا أن يقطع العطش رقابكم، ويُذهب قواكم، فيتحكمون فيكم كيف شاؤوا فأرسل الله عليهم مطراً وسال منه الوادي، فاغتسلوا وتوضؤوا وشربوا وشربت دوابهم ومَلؤوا الأسقية، وثَبَّتَ المطرُ رمل الأرض، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي تحت شجرة حتى أصبح ، وصنعوا عريشاً له ، فكان فيه هو وأبو بكر، وقام سعد بن معاذ على بابه مُتوشّحاً بالسيف، ومشى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في موضع المعركة، وجعل يشير بيده : هذا مَصْرَعُ فلانٍ وهذا مَصْرَعُ فلان إن شاء الله تعالى، فما تعدَّى أحدٌ منهم موضع إشارته ، وسَوَّى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الصفوف، وخطب خُطبةٌ يحثهم فيها على الثبات، وابتهل في الدعاء، حتى قال: اللهمَّ إِنْ تُهْلِكُ هذه العصابة اليوم لا تُعْبَدُ في الأرض ، اللهم إني أُنشدك عهدك ووعدك، اللهم إن ظهروا على هذه العصابة ظهر الشرك، ولا يقومُ لك دين» (١) ، وركع ركعتين، وكان كثيراً ما يقول في سجوده إذ ذاك : يا حي يا قيوم يكرِّرُها مُدَّةٌ، وهو ساجد حتى سقط رداؤه من كثرة ما ابتهل فألقاه عليه أبو بكر ، وقال : يا نبي الله ؛ كفاك تناشد ربَّك فإنه سينجز لك ما وعدك، ثم قاتل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بنفسه قتالاً شديداً، وحرّض المسلمين على القتال، فقال : قوموا إلى جنة عرضها السماوات والأرض، وكانوا إذا اشتدَّ البأس اتقوا برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فكان أقربهم للمشركين، فأخذ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كفا من حصى فرمی به المشركين وقال شاهتِ الوجوه (۲) ؛ أي: قُبِّحَتْ، اللهم أرعب قلوبهم، وزلزل أقدامهم، فأصاب أعين جميعهم وانهزموا ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : سَيُهزم الجَمْعُ وَيُولُونَ الدُّبُرَ) [القمر: ٤٥] ، وأُسِرَ منهم سبعون، وقتل من أشرافهم سبعون، كأبي جهل وأمية بـ وكان مع المسلمين سبعون من الجن وثلاثة آلاف من الملائكة مردفين، يتبع
خلف وعتبة بن ربيعة .
(1) أخرجه مسلم بنحوه (١٧٦٣).

(they were) avoiding (thirst), and your enemies are only waiting for thirst to cut your throats and take away your strength, so they control you as they wish. So Allah sent rain upon them and the valley flowed from it, so they washed and performed ablution and drank and their animals drank and filled the waterskins, and the rain stabilized the sand of the earth, while the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was praying under a tree until morning. The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, walked in the place of the battle and began to point with his hand: 'This is the fall of so-and-so, and this is the fall of so-and-so, if Allah wills.' So none of them exceeded the place of his indication. The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, arranged the ranks and gave a sermon urging them to steadfastness, and he implored in supplication until he said: 'O Allah, if You destroy this group today, You will not be worshipped on earth. O Allah, I implore You by Your covenant and promise. O Allah, if they prevail over this group, polytheism will appear, and Your religion will not stand.' (1) And he performed two rak'ahs, and he often said in his prostration at that time: 'O Living, O Self-Subsisting,' repeating it for a while while prostrating, until his cloak fell off due to the intensity of his supplication, so Abu Bakr threw it over him and said: 'O Prophet of Allah, enough of your imploring your Lord, for He will fulfill what He promised you.' Then the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, fought intensely himself and urged the Muslims to fight, saying: 'Rise to a Garden whose width is the heavens and the earth.' When the battle became severe, they sought protection with the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, so he was the closest of them to the polytheists. The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, took a handful of pebbles and threw them at the polytheists, saying: 'May the faces be disfigured' (2); that is, 'may they be ugly.' 'O Allah, terrify their hearts and shake their feet.' So it struck the eyes of all of them, and they were defeated, and the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was saying: 'The multitude will be defeated, and they will turn their backs' [Quran 54:45]. Seventy of them were captured, and seventy of their nobles were killed, such as Abu Jahl and Umayyah ibn Khalaf, and with the Muslims were seventy jinn and three thousand angels riding in succession... [continuation of the narrative including details about angels, Iblis, etc.]
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative of the Battle of Badr, intended to illustrate divine assistance and angelic support as signs of prophethood. The author describes the Muslims' severe thirst and the miraculous rain that provided water and stabilized the terrain. The Prophet's supplication is highlighted, especially his desperate plea to Allah that if the believers were destroyed, He would not be worshipped. Abu Bakr comforts him. The Prophet then personally fought and encouraged the Muslims. He threw pebbles at the polytheists, causing them to be defeated, fulfilling the Quranic prophecy. The narrative continues with details of the angels: initially 3,000, then 5,000, appearing as white-clad riders. The wounds of the slain polytheists had a distinctive burn-like mark. Iblis, disguised as Suraqa, initially encouraged the polytheists but fled when he saw the angels. The Prophet smiled during prayer because he saw the Archangel Michael returning from pursuit. Jibril later came to the Prophet and asked if he was satisfied, to which the Prophet replied yes. The author explains the wisdom of having multiple angels fight alongside the Muslims, rather than a single angel annihilating the enemy: it preserves the normal order of causes and supports the Muslim army in a customary manner. Ibn Abbas is quoted saying that angels fought only at Badr but attend other battles to increase the Muslim numbers. The entire account serves to reinforce the truth of prophethood through manifest miracles and divine intervention.

Key Terms
الملائكة
جبريل
ميكائيل
إبليس
سراقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that angels always directly fight alongside Muslims in every battle.
Correction: Ibn Abbas states that angels fought only at Badr, but they attend other battles to increase numbers, not necessarily to fight.

Checkpoint
Why did Allah send multiple angels to Badr instead of a single powerful angel?
A) Because a single angel was not enough
B) To preserve the appearance of customary causes and support the army in a usual way
C) To test the faith of the Muslims
D) To allow Iblis to escape

Key Takeaway
The angels at Badr were a visible divine reinforcement, and the manner of their involvement preserves the principle of customary causes, teaching that Allah often works through means.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face an overwhelming challenge, do you truly believe that Allah can send unseen reinforcements, or do you rely only on what you see? Have you ever experienced a sudden shift that you now recognize as divine help? How does the account of Badr change your expectation of Allah's involvement in your life?
?
Iblis, despite his knowledge and arrogance, fled when he saw the angels. What are the 'angels' in your life—the signs of Allah's power that you sometimes avoid until you are forced to confront them? Are you fleeing from truth or running towards it?
?
The Prophet smiled upon learning of Mika'il's pursuit of the polytheists. What is your heart's response when you hear of Allah's victory for His cause? Do you rejoice in the success of Islam even in small ways, or are you indifferent or even uncomfortable?

The Rank of the People of Uhud
The commentator explains the phrase 'the people of Uhud' and their rank.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rank of the people of Uhud in relation to the people of Badr and the meaning of the poet's phrase.

Core Idea
The people of Uhud hold the second highest rank after the people of Badr.

In this passage, the commentator explains a line from the poem that mentions the people of Uhud. He clarifies the pronunciation, identifies Uhud as a mountain near Medina, and establishes that their rank follows that of the people of Badr. The lesson clarifies who is included in 'the people of Uhud'—all those who witnessed the battle, whether martyred or not.

Guided Path
1
Parse the poet's phrase
Understand the pronunciation and meaning of 'فَأَهْلُ احد'. Note that 'احد' is pronounced with hamza and silent dal for meter.
2
Recognize Uhud's location
Uhud is a well-known mountain in Medina. This sets the geographical context.
3
Grasp the rank
The people of Uhud are second in rank after Badr. This is a key point in the poem's hierarchy.
4
Define the group
The term includes all Muslims who witnessed the battle, regardless of martyrdom. So the seventy martyrs are included, but also survivors.
This inclusiveness is important for understanding the poem's reference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فَأَهْلُ احد ) : بدرج همزة (أحد)، وتسكين داله للوزن، و(أحد) جبل معروف بالمدينة؛ أي: فأهل غزوة أحد فرتبتهم تلي رتبة أهل غزوة بدر، والمراد من شهدها من المسلمين سواء استشهد بها كالسبعين أم لا .
وكان أهلها ألفاً، منهم ثلاث مئة من المنافقين الذين رجع بهم عبد الله بن أبي بن سلول، وكان المشركون ثلاثة آلاف رجل، واصطف المسلمون بأصل أُحُدٍ والمشركون بالسبخة، وجعل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عبد الله بن جبير أميراً على الرماة بالنبل وهم خمسون، وقال: «احْمُوا ظهورنا واثبتوا مكانكم (۲) ، فلمَّا التحمّ الحرب شرع المسلمون في أخذ ) الغنائم، فقال الرماة: غلب أصحابكم فما تنتظرون؟ فقال أميرهم : أنسيتم قول
(1) يُسمِّي ابن هشام في سيرته ) (۲۳۸/۲) هذه الغزوة بغزوة سفوان: وهي أن كرز بن جابر الفهري أغار على إبل المدينة ، وغنمها ، فخرج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في طلبه، حتى بلغ وادياً يقال له : سفوان في ناحية بدر، فلم يُدركه فعاد عليه الصلاة والسلام.
ثم إن جابر بن كرز أسلم وحَسُن إسلامه .
(٢) أخرجه البخاري بنحوه (٤٠٤٣).
His statement: 'And the people of Uhud' — by inserting the hamza of 'Ahad' and making its dal silent for the meter. And 'Ahad' is a well-known mountain in Medina. So: the people of the Battle of Uhud, their rank follows the rank of the people of the Battle of Badr. And what is meant is those who witnessed it from among the Muslims, whether they were martyred there like the seventy or not. 
And its people were one thousand, among them three hundred hypocrites whom Abdullah ibn Ubayy ibn Salul took back. And the polytheists were three thousand men. The Muslims lined up at the foot of Uhud and the polytheists at the sabkha (salt flat). The Prophet, peace be upon him, appointed Abdullah ibn Jubayr as commander of the archers with arrows, and they were fifty, and he said: 'Protect our backs and stay in your place' (2). When the battle became fierce, the Muslims began taking spoils. The archers said: 'Your companions have prevailed, so why are you waiting?' Their commander said: 'Have you forgotten the saying...' 
(1) Ibn Hisham in his Sirah (2/238) calls this battle the battle of Safwan: it is that Kurz ibn Jabir al-Fihri raided the camels of Medina and took them as booty, so the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, went out in pursuit of him until he reached a valley called Safwan in the region of Badr, but he did not catch him, so he returned, peace be upon him. Then Jabir ibn Kurz accepted Islam and his Islam was good. 
(2) Al-Bukhari recorded it similarly (4043).
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage explains the rank and details of the Battle of Uhud. It begins by parsing the poet's phrase 'and the people of Uhud', noting the correct pronunciation and that Uhud is a mountain near Medina. The fighters of Uhud hold the next rank after those of Badr. The commentator then provides historical numbers: the Muslim army was one thousand, but three hundred hypocrites withdrew under Abdullah ibn Ubayy. The polytheists numbered three thousand. The Muslims positioned at the base of Uhud, the polytheists on a salt flat. The Prophet appointed Abdullah ibn Jubayr as leader of fifty archers with clear orders to protect the rear and remain in place. When the battle turned and Muslims began gathering spoils, the archers wanted to join, but their commander reminded them of the Prophet's command. The text cuts off there, but the incident is well known: most archers disobeyed, leading to a counterattack. The footnote clarifies that the first three battles of Badr include the 'Battle of Safwan' mentioned earlier, where Kurz ibn Jabir raided and then later accepted Islam.

Key Terms
أحد
أهل أحد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the commentator say about the rank of the people of Uhud?
A) They are equal to the people of Badr.
B) Their rank follows the rank of the people of Badr.
C) They are the highest rank after the Prophets.
D) Their rank is unspecified.

Key Takeaway
The people of Uhud are second in rank after the people of Badr, and the term includes all Muslims who were present at the battle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The people of Uhud hold the second highest rank after Badr. Do you honor them accordingly in your heart, or do you neglect their sacrifice as you go about your daily life? Pause right now and silently thank Allah for their example, then commit to learning more about their stories.
?
The commentator insists that 'the people of Uhud' includes every Muslim present, not just the seventy martyrs. Isn't it easy to envy those who died as martyrs, thinking you missed such a rank? But you are still alive—what trial is Allah testing you with today? Will you stand firm like the survivors of Uhud, or will you waver? Decide now to stay steadfast in one specific obedience this week.

The Archer Incident at Uhud
The commentator recounts the military setup and the archers' command at Uhud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key events of the archer incident at Uhud, including the numbers, the prophet's orders, and the archers' initial disobedience.

Core Idea
Disobeying the Prophet's command led to a turning point at the Battle of Uhud.

This passage provides historical details of the Battle of Uhud: the number of Muslims and polytheists, the positions of the armies, and the appointment of Abdullah ibn Jubayr as commander of the archers. The Prophet's explicit command to protect the rear and stay put was challenged by the archers when they saw their companions gathering spoils, leading to a pivotal moment of disobedience.

Guided Path
1
Understand the numbers and positions
Note the Muslim army of 1,000 (including 300 hypocrites who deserted) vs. the polytheist army of 3,000. The Muslims were at the base of Uhud, the polytheists at a salt flat.
2
Learn the archers' role
The Prophet appointed Abdullah ibn Jubayr as commander of 50 archers with a clear command to protect the rear and stay in place.
3
Observe the archers' temptation
When the battle turned, the Muslims began taking spoils. The archers wanted to join, but their commander reminded them of the Prophet's command.
4
Reflect on the consequence
The passage cuts off, but the well-known outcome was that most archers disobeyed, leading to a counterattack. This highlights the importance of obedience.

?

?
Abdullah ibn Jubayr reminded the archers of the Prophet's command even when others pressed him. When you find yourself in a situation where others are compromising, do you have the courage to speak up and hold firm to what you know is right? How can you strengthen that resolve?
?
The archers thought they knew better than the Prophet's order because the battle seemed won. Reflect on a time you assumed you understood the wisdom behind a divine command better than Allah. What was the result, and what did you learn about trusting Allah's wisdom over your own perception?

The Three Battles of Badr
Defines the three battles of Badr and identifies the middle one as the great one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the phrase 'العظيم الشان' in reference to Badr specifically denotes the middle battle, which is distinguished by the presence of angels and jinn.

Core Idea
Only the middle battle of Badr is the great one.

When the commentator describes Badr as 'العظيم الشان' (great in status), he is not speaking generally. He clarifies that there were actually three military encounters at the location of Badr. The first and third were minor; the middle one is the famous great battle. This lesson unpacks that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic text carefully, then its literal translation. Notice how the commentator distinguishes the three battles.
The passage contains a footnote about the first expedition.
2
Identify the three battles
From the passage, list the three battles of Badr: the first (no fighting), the third (unfulfilled promise), and the middle (the great one).
3
Understand why the middle one is great
The passage states the middle battle is great because angels and jinn fought alongside humans. Reflect on the significance of this supernatural involvement.
4
Address the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that 'great Badr' refers to all battles at Badr. The passage corrects this by specifying the middle one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (العَظِيمِ الشَّانِ): صفةٌ لبدر من حيث غزوتها، واحترز بذلك عن غزوتيها الأخيرتين، فإن غزواتها ثلاثة : الأولى : لم يقع فيها قتال، بل كانت لطلب إنسان أغار على مواشي المدينة، وخرجوا في طلبه فلم يجدوه (1) والثالثة : قد تواعد لها أبو سفيان مع النبي ، وتخلف أبو سفيان خوفاً . والوسطى هي العظمى ؛ لحضور الملائكة والجن فيها مع الإنس. (1) يُسمِّي ابن هشام في سيرته (۲۳۸/۲) هذه الغزوة بغزوة سفوان: وهي أن كرز بن جابر الفهري أغار على إبل المدينة ، وغنمها، فخرج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في طلبه، حتى بلغ وادياً يقال له : سفوان في ناحية بدر، فلم يُدركه فعاد عليه الصلاة والسلام. ثم إن جابر بن كرز أسلم وحَسُن إسلامه .
His saying: (العَظِيمِ الشَّانِ): an attribute of Badr in respect to its battle, and he thereby excluded its other two battles. Indeed, its battles are three: The first: no fighting occurred in it, rather it was for seeking a person who raided the livestock of Madinah, and they went out in pursuit of him but did not find him (1). The third: Abu Sufyan had promised to meet the Prophet (pbuh) for it, but Abu Sufyan stayed behind out of fear. And the middle one is the great one, due to the presence of the angels and jinn in it along with humans. (1) Ibn Hisham calls this expedition in his Sirah the expedition of Safwan: it is that Kharzah bin Jabir al-Fihri raided the camels of Madinah and seized them, so the Messenger of Allah (pbuh) went out in pursuit of him until he reached a valley called Safwan in the region of Badr, but he did not catch him, so he (pbuh) returned. Then Kharzah bin Jabir accepted Islam and his Islam was good.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'al-'azim al-shaan' (the great in status) as an attribute of the Battle of Badr, warning that not all battles fought at Badr are the famous one. The commentator explains that there were three battles at the location Badr: the first (Safwan) involved no combat; it was merely a pursuit of a raider. The third was a planned encounter with Abu Sufyan that did not happen. The middle one is the great Badr, distinguished by the presence of angels and jinn fighting alongside the Muslims. The footnote provides details on the first expedition.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the descriptor 'great' applies to all battles fought at Badr.
Correction: The passage shows that only the middle battle is called great, due to the miraculous presence of angels and jinn.

Checkpoint

B) Because it involved the presence of angels and jinn
C) Because it was the only one with casualties

Key Takeaway
The middle battle of Badr is the great one because of the presence of angels and jinn, marking it as a miraculous event.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah sent angels to support the believers at Badr? If so, how does that certainty affect your trust in Allah's help when you face overwhelming odds? What would you do differently today if you expected unseen aid?
?
The first and third battles of Badr had no fighting yet are recorded. Does your faith value effort and intention even when results are not visible? Where in your life are you seeking immediate outcomes instead of trusting Allah's wisdom in hidden successes?
?
The middle battle is great because of the presence of angels and jinn. In your daily struggles, do you rely more on visible means or do you actively seek Allah's unseen support through dua and tawakkul? What practical step can you take this week to strengthen that reliance?

The Rank of the People of Uhud
Definition and rank of Ahl Uhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the people of the Battle of Uhud, which includes all Muslim participants, hold a rank second only to the people of Badr.

Core Idea
The people of Uhud are second in rank only to the people of Badr.

After discussing the people of Badr, the commentator now turns to the participants of the Battle of Uhud. He clarifies their status: every Muslim who was present at Uhud, whether he was martyred or not, has a special rank. This lesson establishes that definition and sets the stage for understanding the battle's significance in Islamic history.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
Notice the linguistic note about the word 'Ahad'.
2
Identify the rank given
Find the phrase that states the rank of the people of Uhud compared to Badr.
The phrase 'فرتبتهم تلي رتبة أهل غزوة بدر' is key.
3
Understand who is included
The passage says 'المراد من شهدها من المسلمين سواء استشهد بها كالسبعين أم لا'. This means all Muslims who witnessed the battle are included, not just the martyrs.
This is important to counter a misconception.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this rank matters for the study of the companions' virtues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فَأَهْلُ احد ) : بدرج همزة (أحد)، وتسكين داله للوزن، و(أحد) جبل معروف بالمدينة؛ أي: فأهل غزوة أحد فرتبتهم تلي رتبة أهل غزوة بدر، والمراد من شهدها من المسلمين سواء استشهد بها كالسبعين أم لا . وكان أهلها ألفاً، منهم ثلاث مئة من المنافقين الذين رجع بهم عبد الله بن أبي بن سلول، وكان المشركون ثلاثة آلاف رجل، واصطف المسلمون بأصل أُحُدٍ والمشركون بالسبخة، وجعل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عبد الله بن جبير أميراً على الرماة بالنبل وهم خمسون، وقال: «احْمُوا ظهورنا واثبتوا مكانكم (۲) ، فلمَّا التحمّ الحرب شرع المسلمون في أخذ ( الغنائم، فقال الرماة: غلب أصحابكم فما تنتظرون؟ فقال أميرهم : أنسيتم قول رسول الله الله فقالوا : والله لنأتين الناس ونصيب من الغنيمة (١)، وحملوا كلامه على أن المراد ما دام الحرب قائماً، فلما أتوهم رجع الكفار عليهم ووقع القتال، وأشاع إبليس في ذلك الوقت أن محمداً قتل، فقُتل من المسلمين سبعون، ومن الكفار نيف (۲) وعشرون ، وقيل : سبعون أيضاً منهم أبي بن خلف قتله المصطفى بيده أُبَيُّ الكريمة (۳)، ولم يقتل بيده الشريفة غيره، وكان لابساً درعين، فأراد أن ينهض وهما عليه ليصعد صخرةً هنالك فبرك طلحة فصعد على ظهره واستوى عليها، وقد أصيب طلحة حينئذ ببضع وسبعين ما بین طعنة بالرمح وضربة بالسيف ورمية بالسهم وقطعت أصابعه، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقولُ : قد أوجب طلحة (4)، أي: الجنة، وفيها استشهد حمزة قتله ،وحشي، وشُجَّ وجه رسول الله ، ورماه عتبة بن أبي وقاص لعنه الله بحجر فكسر ،رباعيته، فلم يُولد من نسله ولدٌ إلا أَهْتَمُ أَبْخَرُ (٥)، ودخل حلقتان المِغْفَر في وجنته الله فأخرجهما أبو عبيدة بأسنانه فسقطت ثنيتاه، فكان أحسن من الناس هَماً .
His saying: (فَأَهْلُ أُحُدٍ): with the hamza of 'Ahad' pronounced, and its dal made silent for meter, and 'Ahad' is a well-known mountain in Madinah. Meaning: So the people of the battle of Uhud—their rank follows the rank of the people of the battle of Badr, and what is intended are those who witnessed it from among the Muslims, whether martyred there like the seventy or not. Its people numbered a thousand, among them three hundred hypocrites whom Abdullah ibn Ubayy ibn Salul brought back. The polytheists numbered three thousand men. The Muslims lined up at the base of Uhud and the polytheists at the Sabkhah (marshy ground). The Prophet (pbuh) made Abdullah ibn Jubayr commander over the archers with arrows, and they were fifty, and he said: 'Protect our backs and remain in your places.' When the war engaged, the Muslims began taking spoils. The archers said: 'Your companions have prevailed, so what are you waiting for?' Their commander said: 'Have you forgotten the statement of the Messenger of Allah?' They said: 'By Allah, we will surely go to the people and take a share of the spoils' (1), interpreting his words to mean as long as the war was ongoing. When they arrived, the disbelievers turned back on them and fighting occurred. Iblis spread at that time that Muhammad had been killed. Seventy Muslims were killed, and from the disbelievers a little over twenty (2) were killed, and it is said also seventy, among them Ubayy ibn Khalaf whom the Chosen One killed with his own hand—his noble hand (3)—and he killed no one else with his hand. He (Ubayy) was wearing two coats of mail, and he wanted to rise while wearing them to climb a rock there, so Talhah knelt down and he (the Prophet) climbed onto his back and stood upon it. Talhah was struck at that time with some seventy-odd wounds between a spear thrust, a sword blow, an arrow shot, and his fingers were cut. The Messenger of Allah (pbuh) said: 'Talhah is obligated' (4), meaning Paradise. In it Hamzah was martyred, killed by Wahshi. The face of the Messenger of Allah was wounded, and 'Utbah ibn Abi Waqqas (may Allah curse him) threw a stone at him and broke his lateral incisor, so no child was born from his lineage except with a broken front tooth and halitosis (5). Two ringlets of the helmet entered his cheek (noble), so Abu 'Ubaydah extracted them with his teeth, and his two front teeth fell out, so he became the most beautiful of people in gap in front teeth? (hamman).
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage defines 'Ahl Uhud' (the people of the Battle of Uhud) and gives their rank as immediately below the rank of the people of Badr. It specifies that all Muslims who attended the battle, whether martyred or not, are included. The commentator then provides a detailed narrative of the battle: the total numbers (1000 Muslims including 300 hypocrites who left, 3000 polytheists), the initial strategy (archers on the mountain), the archers' disobedience after seeing the spoils, the resulting reversal, the rumor of Muhammad's death, the casualties (70 Muslims, about 22-70 polytheists), Ubayy ibn Khalaf's killing by the Prophet, Talhah's bravery and wounds, the martyrdom of Hamzah, the Prophet's facial wounds including broken tooth and cheek injury, and Abu 'Ubaydah's extraction of the helmet rings at the cost of his own teeth. Footnotes provide minor clarifications but do not alter the main doctrinal point.

Key Terms
أهل أحد
أحد
غزوة أحد
السبعين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the rank of the people of Uhud according to the passage?
A) They have the same rank as the people of Badr
B) Their rank is above the people of Badr
C) Their rank follows that of the people of Badr
D) Their rank is below that of the people of Badr but above others

Key Takeaway
The people of Uhud hold the second highest honor among the companions in terms of battle participation, and all attendees share in that honor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the people of Uhud are second only to Badr, do you feel a longing to have been among them, or are you content with your current level of devotion? What is one thing you will do today to increase your zeal for Allah's cause, even if no one notices?
?
The lesson includes all attendees of Uhud—martyrs and survivors—in the same honor. Does your service to Allah depend on recognition or results? Are you willing to persevere even if your efforts seem invisible or unsuccessful?
?
The seventy martyrs gave their lives. What is the greatest sacrifice you have made for Allah recently, and if you cannot think of any, what is holding you back from giving something truly costly?

The Battle of Uhud: Key Events and Lessons
Narrative of the Battle of Uhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the major events of the Battle of Uhud as recounted in this passage, including the archers' disobedience, the casualties, and the injuries suffered by the Prophet and his companions.

Core Idea
Disobedience to the Prophet's command led to disaster, but the companions showed extraordinary courage.

The commentator now narrates the Battle of Uhud in detail. He describes the initial setup, the critical mistake of the archers, the ensuing reversal, and the heroic acts of companions like Talhah and Hamzah, as well as the Prophet's own injuries. This narrative serves as a powerful lesson on obedience, sacrifice, and the resilience of the early Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Read the battle narrative
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the events.
This passage is longer; take your time.
2
Identify the archers' role and mistake
Notice the Prophet's instruction to the archers and how they disobeyed when they saw spoils.
Their disobedience turned the tide of battle.
3
Note the casualties and key figures
The passage mentions seventy Muslim martyrs, including Hamzah, and the killing of Ubayy ibn Khalaf by the Prophet.
Also note Talhah's bravery and wounds.
4
Reflect on the Prophet's injuries
The Prophet was wounded in the face, his tooth was broken, and his cheek was injured. Abu 'Ubaydah extracted helmet rings with his teeth.
This shows the extent of the suffering.
5
Consider the lessons
Think about the importance of obedience, the reality of sacrifice, and the high status of those who suffered for Islam.

?

?

?

The People of Bay‘at al-Riḍwān and Their Rank
Defines Bay‘at al-Riḍwān and places its participants after Uhud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the identity of the participants of Bay‘at al-Riḍwān, their rank after the people of Uhud, and the significance of the pledge as recorded in the Qur'an.

Core Idea
Bay‘at al-Riḍwān participants rank just below Uhud's martyrs, honored by Allah's pleasure.

This passage from the commentary defines Bay‘at al-Riḍwān (the Pledge of Good Pleasure) and situates its participants in the hierarchy of the Companions. It explains the name's origin from the Qur'anic verse of divine pleasure and provides historical details about the event, which took place in the sixth year of the Hijrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rank
Read the passage to find where the participants of Bay‘at al-Riḍwān stand relative to the people of Uhud.
The phrase 'تلي رتبة أهل غزوة أحد' is key.
2
Understand the name
Notice how the commentator explains the grammatical construction of 'بيعة الرضوان' and why it is called that.
The term 'رضوان' is the cause for the pledge's naming.
3
Review the Qur'anic basis
The passage quotes Surah al-Fatḥ verse 18. Reflect on the significance of Allah's pleasure being mentioned.
4
Learn the historical details
Note the number of participants (1400 or 1500) and the year (6 AH). Consider the context of the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah.
The passage ends mid-sentence, but the purpose was to visit the Ka'bah.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فَبَيْعَةُ الرِّضْوانِ) أي : فأهلُ بيعة الرضوان فرتبتهم تلي رتبة أهل غزوة أحد، والإضافة في بيعة الرضوان من إضافة السبب للمسبب، وسميت بذلك لقوله تعالى: ﴿لَقَدْ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنِ الْمُؤْمِنِين . . [الفتح: (۱۸) الآية، وكان أهل بيعة الرضوان ﴾ ألفاً وأربع مئةٍ ، وقيل : وخمس مئة وخرج بهم النبي العام ست من الهجرة لزيارة
His saying: (فَبَيْعَةُ الرِّضْوانِ) meaning: So the people of the Pledge of Good Pleasure—their rank follows the rank of the people of the battle of Uhud. The genitive construction in 'Bay‘at al-Riḍwān' is a causative attribution. It was named thus because of the verse: 'Certainly Allah was pleased with the believers...' [Surah al-Fatḥ (48):18]. And the people of Bay‘at al-Riḍwān were one thousand four hundred, and it is said one thousand five hundred, and the Prophet went out with them in the sixth year of the Hijrah to visit
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage defines 'Bay‘at al-Riḍwān' (the Pledge of Good Pleasure) and states that its participants rank after those of Uhud. The commentator explains the grammatical construction: the word 'Riḍwān' (pleasure) is the cause for the pledge being named so, because Allah expressed His pleasure with them in the Qur'an (48:18). The number of participants is given as 1400 or 1500. The Prophet led them in the year 6 AH to visit (the Ka'bah), which was the event leading to the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah. The passage ends mid-sentence at the page break.

The Battle of Uhud: Sacrifice and Devotion of the Companions
Commentary narrates events of the Battle of Uhud and praises the Companions' sacrifices.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key events of the Battle of Uhud and the extraordinary sacrifices made by the Prophet's Companions, reinforcing their lofty status in Islam.

Core Idea
The Companions' sacrifices at Uhud prove their unwavering love for the Prophet.

The Battle of Uhud was a severe test for the early Muslim community. This passage from the commentary recounts specific moments of heroism and suffering, showing how the Companions put the Prophet's safety above their own lives. As you read, notice the physical costs borne by Talha, Hamza, and Abu Ubaydah, and the Prophet's own injuries—a reminder of his humanity and the trials he endured for the sake of the message.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then the full literal translation. Let the narrative flow without analysis first.
2
Identify the Companions mentioned
List the Companions named: Talha, Hamza, Abu Ubaydah, and note what each sacrificed.
Talha: allowed Prophet to climb on his back, received 70+ wounds. Hamza: martyred. Abu Ubaydah: lost incisors extracting arrowheads.
3
Notice the Prophet's injuries
Observe how the commentator describes the Prophet's broken tooth and cheek wounds, and the curse on Utbah ibn Abi Waqqas.
This highlights the Prophet's humanity and the severity of the battle.
4
Reflect on the lesson for faith
Ask yourself: Why are these details preserved? They show the Companions' extreme love and the Prophet's endurance, strengthening our appreciation of their sacrifices.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النبوات
رسول الله الله فقالوا : والله لنأتين الناس ونصيب من الغنيمة (١)، وحملوا كلامه على أن المراد ما دام الحرب قائماً، فلما أتوهم رجع الكفار عليهم ووقع القتال، وأشاع إبليس في ذلك الوقت أن محمداً قتل، فقُتل من المسلمين سبعون، ومن الكفار نيف (۲) وعشرون ، وقيل : سبعون أيضاً منهم أبي بن خلف قتله المصطفى بيده أُبَيُّ الكريمة (۳)، ولم يقتل بيده الشريفة غيره، وكان لابساً درعين، فأراد أن ينهض وهما عليه ليصعد صخرةً هنالك فبرك طلحة فصعد على ظهره واستوى عليها، وقد أصيب طلحة حينئذ ببضع وسبعين ما بین طعنة بالرمح وضربة بالسيف ورمية بالسهم وقطعت أصابعه، ورسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقولُ : قد أوجب طلحة (4)، أي: الجنة، وفيها استشهد حمزة قتله ،وحشي، وشُجَّ وجه رسول الله ، ورماه عتبة بن أبي وقاص لعنه الله بحجر فكسر ،رباعيته، فلم يُولد من نسله ولدٌ إلا أَهْتَمُ أَبْخَرُ (٥)، ودخل حلقتان المِغْفَر في وجنته الله فأخرجهما أبو عبيدة بأسنانه فسقطت ثنيتاه، فكان أحسن من الناس هَماً .
The prophecies. The Messenger of God, God said: 'By God, we will go to the people and take from the spoils (1),' and they interpreted his words to mean as long as the war was ongoing. When they came to them, the disbelievers returned against them and fighting occurred, and Iblis at that time spread the word that Muhammad was killed. So seventy of the Muslims were killed, and of the disbelievers twenty-odd (2), and it was said: seventy as well, among them Ubayy ibn Khalaf, whom the Chosen One killed with his own hand, Ubayy al-Karimah (3), and he killed no other with his blessed hand. He was wearing two coats of mail, and he wanted to rise up with them on him to climb a rock there, so Talha knelt, and he climbed on his back and stood upon it. Talha was then wounded with seventy-some wounds, between a spear thrust, a sword blow, an arrow shot, and his fingers were cut off. The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Talha has become obligated (4),' i.e., Paradise. In it Hamza was martyred, killed by Wahshi. The face of the Messenger of God was wounded, and Utbah ibn Abi Waqqas, may God curse him, threw a stone at him and broke his incisor, so no child was born from his descendants except one with broken front teeth and foul breath (5). Two rings of the mail-coif entered his cheek, and Abu Ubaydah extracted them with his teeth, losing his two incisors. So he became the most handsome of people in mouth.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative recounting events from the Battle of Uhud. It begins with a misinterpretation of the Prophet's words about spoils, leading to a battle where many Muslims were killed. The commentator highlights the bravery of Talha, who helped the Prophet climb a rock and was severely wounded, and the martyrdom of Hamza. It also describes the Prophet's injuries, including a broken tooth from a stone thrown by Utbah ibn Abi Waqqas, which had a lasting curse on his descendants. The passage concludes with Abu Ubaydah extracting arrowheads from the Prophet's cheek, losing his own teeth in the process. The narrative emphasizes the physical sacrifices of the Companions and the Prophet's own suffering.

Key Terms
أحد
حمزة
طلحة
أبو عبيدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Battle of Uhud was a defeat that shows the Prophet was not protected by God.
Correction: The passage shows that despite the Prophet's injuries and the martyrdom of many Companions, the battle's events are recorded to highlight the Companions' devotion and the Prophet's perseverance. The Prophet's survival and the mention of curses on his enemies affirm divine support.

Checkpoint
How many wounds did Talha receive according to the passage?
A) Fifty
B) Seventy
C) Bada and seventy (73+)
D) Twenty

Key Takeaway
The Battle of Uhud exemplifies the Companions' extraordinary devotion, with Talha, Hamza, and Abu Ubaydah sacrificing their bodies to protect and aid the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Talha received over seventy wounds and lost fingers just to help the Prophet climb a rock. What are you willing to sacrifice—your comfort, time, reputation, or even your body—for the sake of Allah and His Messenger? Name one specific thing you will give up this week.
?
The Prophet only killed one enemy with his own hand, yet the Companions gave their lives. How much of your devotion is mere talk, and how much is proven by your actions? Write down a concrete action you will take today to show your love for the Prophet.
?
Abu Ubaydah lost his teeth to extract the rings from the Prophet's cheek, and his reward is being among the most handsome in mouth. When you are faced with a painful task for Allah's sake, do you shy away or do you step forward? What is holding you back from embracing hardship for His pleasure?

The Pledge of Ridwan: Rank and Event
Commentator explains rank, naming, and event of the Pledge of Ridwan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the Pledge of Ridwan, the rank of its participants, and the events that led to it.

Core Idea
Loyalty to the Prophet was pledged even when it seemed costly.

This lesson explores the Pledge of Ridwan, a moment when the Prophet called for a pledge of allegiance under a tree, and nearly fourteen hundred Companions responded with unwavering loyalty. The commentator explains the rank of these Companions, the reason for the pledge's name, and the dramatic rumor that sparked it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the Pledge of Ridwan
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the first part: from the beginning to 'thumma tabayyanat hayatu Uthman'.
This section covers the rank of the people of the pledge, the story of Uthman, and the pledge itself.
2
Understand the rank and naming
Notice that the commentator places the people of the Pledge of Ridwan after the people of Uhud in rank, and explains the name comes from God's pleasure in Surah al-Fath.
The term 'Pledge of Ridwan' combines cause and effect.
3
Analyze the narrative
Follow the sequence: the expedition for Umrah, the prevention by Quraysh, the rumor of Uthman's death, and the Prophet's response. See how this led to the pledge.
The pledge was for steadfastness, not flight, and was made under a tree.
4
Reflect on the one who held back
Note the mention of al-Jadd ibn Qays, who hid under his camel. Consider why such details are recorded and what they teach about human nature.
His later repentance is also noted.

Source Text
