ه. أهلُ بيعة الرضوان]
قوله : (فَبَيْعَةُ الرِّضْوانِ) أي : فأهلُ بيعة الرضوان فرتبتهم تلي رتبة أهل غزوة أحد، والإضافة في بيعة الرضوان من إضافة السبب للمسبب، وسميت بذلك لقوله تعالى: ﴿لَقَدْ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنِ الْمُؤْمِنِين . . [الفتح: (۱۸) الآية، وكان أهل بيعة الرضوان ﴾ ألفاً وأربع مئةٍ ، وقيل : وخمس مئة وخرج بهم النبي العام ست من الهجرة لزيارة البيت الحرام والاعتمار به ولم يكن معهم سلاح إلا السيوف، فنزلوا (۱) بأقصى الحديبية محل معروف فصدَّه المشركون عن دخول مكة، فأرسل إليهم عثمان بكتاب لأشراف قريش يعلمهم أنه إنما قَدِمَ مُعتمراً لا مُقاتلاً، فقالوا : لا يدخل مكة هذا العام، فشاع أنهم قتلوا عثمان أشاع ذلك إبليس ورفع صوته به، فقال عليه الصلاة والسلام عند ذلك : لا نبرح حتى نناجزهم الحرب (۳) ، ودعا الناس عند الشجرة للبيعة على الموت، أو على ألا يفروا، بل يصبرون على الحرب، فبايعوه على ذلك، ووضع شماله في يمينه وقال هذه عن يَدِ عثمان أي على تقدير حياته، أو نظراً (۳) للحقيقة، ولم يتخلف عنها إلا الجد بن قيس (4) ـ بفتح الجيم ـ اختبأ تحت بطن ،ناقته، وكان منافقاً، ويقال : إنه تاب وحَسُنَ إسلامه، ثم تبينت حياة عثمان .
فصالحهم النبي على شروط وهي :
(٤)
أن يوضع الحرب بينه وبينهم عشر سنين، وأن يؤمن بعضهم بعضاً، وأن يرجع في هذا العام ويأتي للعمرة في العام القابل، وأن من جاء ممن تبعه لا يردُّوه، ومن حاء من قريش مؤمناً يردُّه، وكَرِهَ المسلمون ذلك، وقالوا: يا رسول الله ؛ إنا نرد ولا يردون، قال: «نعم، من ذهب إليهم فأبعده الله، ومن جاء منهم فسيجعل الله له مخرجاً (٥) ، حتى أسلم أبو جندل وجماعة وانحازوا بجبل يقطعون الطريق على ،قريش، فأرسلوا له بإسقاط الشروط، وأن يأخذهم عنده.
وقد كتب عليّ : هذا ما صالح عليه محمد رسول الله ، فقالوا : لو سلمنا أنك
(1) في (ب) و(ج): (حتى نزلوا).
(٢) أخرجه البيهقي في دلائل النبوة» (١٣٥/٤).
(۳) في (أ) و(ب) و(ج): (نظر هنا).
(٤) جَد بن قيس بن صخر بن خنساء بن سنان بن عبيد بن غنم بن كعب بن سلمة الأنصاري، أبو عبد الله، روى الطبراني وابن منده من طريق معاوية بن عمار الدهني، عن أبيه، عن أبي الزبير، عن جابر، قال: حملني خالي جد بن قيس وما أقدر أن أرمي بحجر في السبعين راكباً من الأنصار الذين وفدوا على رسول الله ، فذكر الحديث في بيعة العقبة، ويقال: إن الجد بن قيس كان منافقاً. الإصابة» (٥٧٥/١).
(5) أخرجه مسلم (١٧٨٤).
H. The people of the Pledge of Ridwan. His saying: 'And the Pledge of Ridwan' means: the people of the Pledge of Ridwan, their rank comes after the rank of the people of the Battle of Uhud. The construct in 'Pledge of Ridwan' is a causal construct, and it was named thus due to His saying, exalted: 'Indeed, God was pleased with the believers' [Surah al-Fath: 18]. The people of the Pledge of Ridwan were one thousand four hundred, and it was said: one thousand five hundred. The Prophet went out with them in the sixth year of the Hijra to visit the Sacred House and perform Umrah, and they had no weapons except swords. They camped at the far end of al-Hudaybiyyah, a known place, and the polytheists prevented him from entering Mecca. So he sent Uthman with a letter to the nobles of Quraysh informing them that he had come as a pilgrim, not a fighter. They said: 'He will not enter Mecca this year.' Then it spread that they had killed Uthman – Iblis spread that and raised his voice with it. Upon that, he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'We will not leave until we engage them in battle (3).' He called the people at the tree to pledge allegiance to death, or not to flee, but to be patient in war. So they pledged allegiance to him on that. He placed his left hand in his right and said: 'This is on behalf of the hand of Uthman,' meaning on the assumption of his life, or considering the reality. None held back from it except al-Jadd ibn Qays (4) – with a fatha on the jim – who hid under the belly of his she-camel, and he was a hypocrite. It is said that he repented and his Islam became good. Then the life of Uthman became clear. So the Prophet made a treaty with them on conditions, which are: (4) That war be laid aside between him and them for ten years, and that they give security to each other, and that he return this year and come for Umrah the following year, and that whoever comes from those who follow him they will not send back, but whoever comes from Quraysh as a believer they will send back. The Muslims disliked that, and said: 'O Messenger of God, we send back but they do not send back.' He said: 'Yes. Whoever goes to them, God will distance him; and whoever comes from them, God will provide a way out for him (5).' Then Abu Jandal and a group became Muslim and gathered on a mountain, cutting off the road against Quraysh, so they sent to him to drop the conditions and take them with him. And Ali wrote: 'This is what Muhammad the Messenger of God agreed upon.' They said: 'If we admit that you...'
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the Pledge of Ridwan (Bay'at al-Ridwan) and the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah. It begins by stating the rank of those who participated, placing them after the people of Uhud in merit. The name 'Ridwan' comes from God's pleasure expressed in the Quran. The commentator then narrates the events: the Prophet's expedition for Umrah in 6 AH, the prevention by Quraysh, the rumor of Uthman's death, the Prophet's call to pledge allegiance under a tree, and the pledge itself. Only one hypocrite, al-Jadd ibn Qays, held back. Then the peace treaty terms are listed: a ten-year truce, mutual security, postponement of Umrah, and a clause about returning refugees. The Muslims were initially displeased with the one-sided nature of the refugee clause, but the Prophet assured them. The passage ends with the later nullification of the conditions after some Muslims (Abu Jandal) became Muslim and caused trouble, leading Quraysh to request dropping the conditions. The commentary emphasizes the wisdom of the Prophet and the virtue of the Companions who participated.

Key Terms
بيعة الرضوان
الحديبية
عثمان
الجد بن قيس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Pledge of Ridwan was a military oath for aggressive war.
Correction: It was a pledge for steadfastness in self-defense, as the Muslims were prevented from peaceful pilgrimage and were threatened.

Checkpoint
What event triggered the Prophet to call for the Pledge of Ridwan?
A) The Quraysh attacked the Muslim camp
B) The rumor that Uthman had been killed
C) The Muslims were starving
D) The Prophet received a revelation

Key Takeaway
The Pledge of Ridwan demonstrated the Companions' unwavering loyalty, earning God's pleasure as promised in the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Companions pledged to fight to the death or never flee. If you were in that situation, would your fear of death or comfort outweigh your loyalty to Allah and His Messenger? What would you need to change in your heart today to be ready for such a test?
?
Al-Jadd ibn Qays hid out of fear and hypocrisy. Are there areas in your life where you hide your faith, avoid standing up for Islam, or prioritize your safety over obedience? Will you make a sincere intention to step forward the next time?
?
The Prophet used his left hand to represent Uthman's hand. He included the absent as if they were present. Do you feel included in every act of obedience of the Ummah, or do you isolate yourself? What concrete step will you take this week to strengthen your bond with the community of believers?

The Treaty of Hudaybiyyah: Terms and Wisdom
Commentator lists treaty conditions, Muslim reaction, and subsequent events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the terms of the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah, the initial Muslim reaction, and how it ultimately benefited Islam.

Core Idea
A treaty that seemed unfair was actually a strategic victory.

After the pledge, the Prophet negotiated a treaty with Quraysh. The terms seemed one-sided, and many Muslims were disappointed. However, the Prophet's wisdom and trust in Allah turned this apparent defeat into a great success. This lesson explains the conditions and the later developments that proved the treaty's benefit.

Guided Path
1
Read the treaty conditions
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'fasalahum al-Nabiyyu' and its translation. List the conditions mentioned.
There are four main conditions: ten-year truce, mutual safety, postponement of Umrah, and the refugee clause.
2
Understand the Muslim objection
Notice the Muslims' complaint: they have to return any Muslim from Quraysh, but Quraysh does not return Muslims who go to them. The Prophet's response shows his trust in Allah's plan.
The Prophet said: 'Whoever goes to them, Allah will distance him; whoever comes from them, Allah will provide a way out.'
3
See the later nullification
Read the event of Abu Jandal and how Quraysh eventually asked to drop the conditions because the treaty was harming them.
This shows the treaty was not a permanent setback but a strategic move.
4
Reflect on the writing of the treaty
Notice the objection about writing 'Muhammad Rasul Allah', which Quraysh disputed. This highlights the Prophet's flexibility for overall benefit.
The passage ends with this incident.

?

Miracles vs. Charisms and the Frequency of Karamat
Refutation and explanation on miracles vs. charisms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key difference between a miracle and a charism, and why charisms became more frequent in later Islamic history.

Core Idea
Charisms are extraordinary but never become ordinary, no matter how frequent.

The commentator addresses a common confusion: how do we distinguish a prophet's miracle from a saint's charism? He also tackles a historical observation about the increase of charisms in later times, offering a profound reason rooted in the strength of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the two main topics: the definitional distinction and the explanation for frequency.
2
Identify the core distinction
Find where the commentator states the difference between a miracle and a charism. Note the role of the claim to prophethood.
3
Analyze the refutation
Understand the objection about frequency making charisms ordinary. See how the commentator refutes it by clarifying that continuity of breaking custom does not create a new custom.
4
Examine the question and answer
Read the question about why charisms increased. Notice the answer links to the weakness of conviction in later believers.
This is a historical and spiritual explanation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في وقوعها التباسُ النبي بغيره للفرق بين المعجزة والكرامة، بدعوى النبوة في الأولى وعدمها في الثانية، ورُدَّ الثاني بأنا لا نُسلّم أنها تخرج بكثرتها عن كونها خارقة للعادة، بل غاية الأمر استمرار خرق العادة وذلك لا يوجب كونه عادة . وسئل بعضهم : لأي شيءٍ كثرت الكرامات في الزمان المتأخر عن الزمان المتقدم؟ فأجاب بأن ذلك لضعف اعتقاد المتأخرين، فاحتيج لتأليفهم بالكرامات ليعتقدوا في الصالحين، وأما المتقدمون فاعتقادهم تابع لميزان الشرع .
In its occurrence there is confusion of the prophet with others due to the difference between the miracle (mu'jiza) and the charism (karama), by the claim of prophethood in the first and its absence in the second. And the second objection was refuted by [saying]: we do not concede that they exit, by their frequency, from being extraordinary; rather the utmost is the continuation of breaking the custom, and that does not necessitate its being customary. And some of them were asked: for what reason did charisms increase in the later time over the earlier time? He answered: because of the weakness of the conviction of the later ones, so there was need to attract them with charisms so that they would believe in the righteous. As for the earlier ones, their conviction was subject to the scale of the Law.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and explanation regarding the distinction between miracles (mu'jizat) and charisms (karamat). The commentator begins by stating that confusion arises between a prophet and a non-prophet when trying to differentiate the two types of extraordinary events. The distinction lies in the claim of prophethood: miracles are associated with a claim of prophethood, while charisms are not. The commentator then addresses an objection: someone might argue that if charisms occur frequently, they cease to be extraordinary and become customary. The refutation is that we do not concede that frequency removes the extraordinary nature; the only change is the continuation of the breaking of custom, which does not establish a new custom. Then a question is raised about why charisms are more numerous in later times compared to earlier times. The answer given is that later generations have weaker conviction, so they need to be drawn by charisms to believe in the saints (awliya). The earlier generations, however, had strong conviction directly from the Law (Sharia).

Key Terms
معجزة
كرامة
النبوة
خارقة للعادة
خرق العادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If charisms occur very frequently, they cease to be extraordinary and become ordinary events.
Correction: The commentator argues that frequency does not remove the extraordinary nature; the continuity of breaking custom does not make it a custom.

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between a miracle (mu'jiza) and a charism (karama) according to the passage?
A) Miracles are more extraordinary than charisms.
B) Miracles are associated with a claim of prophethood, while charisms are not.
C) Charisms are more frequent than miracles.
D) Miracles are performed by prophets and charisms by angels.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between miracles and charisms is the claim to prophethood, and charisms remain extraordinary regardless of frequency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you find yourself needing extraordinary signs to believe in the sincerity of righteous people, or does the scale of the Sharia suffice? What does your answer reveal about the strength of your conviction?
?
When you witness a remarkable event attributed to a pious person, do you automatically assume it is a sign of their high rank, or do you check if it leads to a claim of prophethood? How can you train yourself to apply this distinction?
?
The passage says earlier believers had conviction subject to the scale of the Law. Is your faith anchored in the Sharia and its proofs, or are you swayed by visible wonders? Commit to one concrete step this week to strengthen your reliance on the revealed guidance.

Prophethood

The Obligation of Belief in the Prophet's Intercession: Definition and Three Aspects
Defines shafāʿa and enumerates three obligatory aspects of the Prophet's intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and technical meaning of shafāʿa and the three obligatory aspects of the Prophet's intercession: that he is an intercessor, his intercession is accepted, and he is foremost among all creation.

Core Idea
Belief in the Prophet's intercession requires affirming three things: he intercedes, he is accepted, and he is foremost.

The passage begins by establishing that belief in the Prophet's intercession is obligatory according to revealed law. It first gives a precise definition of the term shafāʿa, then extracts from the author's speech three essential aspects that every Muslim must believe about the Prophet's intercession. These aspects form the foundation of the Sunni doctrine on this topic.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of shafāʿa
Read the Arabic and translation of the definition carefully. Note the linguistic meaning (wasīla and ṭalab) and the technical meaning (asking for good from another for another).
Also note the distinction between mushaffaʿ and mushaffiʿ.
2
Understand the distinction between the Prophet's intercession and Allah's 'intercession'
The passage mentions the shafāʿa of the Lord, which is actually His forgiveness. This clarifies that when we speak of the Prophet's intercession, we mean a specific type that is granted by Allah.
3
Identify the three obligatory aspects
Look for the three matters indicated by the author: the Prophet being a shāfiʿ (intercessor), being mushaffaʿ (accepted), and being muqaddam (foremost). Reflect on why each is essential.
The third aspect is supported by the hadith 'I am the first intercessor and the first whose intercession is accepted.'
4
Consider the implications
Think about why the Prophet must be foremost. How does this relate to the concept of al-maqām al-maḥmūd? This sets the stage for the Great Intercession.
This aspect will be elaborated in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوبُ الإيمان بشفاعة النبي
قوله : (وَوَاجِبٌ شَفَاعَةُ المُشَفّع) أي : وواجب سمعاً عند أهل الحق)، شفاعة المشفّع، بفتح الفاء؛ وهو الذي تُقبل شفاعته وأما بكسرها فهو الذي يقبلُ شفاعة غيره .
والشفاعة لغةٌ : الوسيلة والطلب. وعرفاً سؤال الخير من الغير للغير. وشفاعةُ المولى (۲) : عبارةٌ عن عفوه ؛ فإنه تعالى يشفع فيمن قال : لا إله إلا الله، وأثبت الرسالة للرسول الذي أُرسل إليه، ولم يعمل خيراً قط، فيتفضل الله تعالى عليه بعدم دخوله النار بلا شفاعة أحدٍ .
(۲) قوله (وشفاعة المولى محلّ هذه العبارة عند قول المصنف : وغيره من مرتضى الأخيار فإن الشارح عبد السلام ذكر أن الغير يشمل المولى سبحانه وتعالى، وفسرت هناك شفاعة المولى بعفوه، وأما الشفاعة المذكورة هنا فهي شفاعة النبي . انتهى أجهوري.
وقوله : (مُحَمَّدٍ) بدل من المشفّع، دفع به إبهامه .
وقوله : (مُقَدَّماً) أي: حال كونه مقدَّماً على غيره من الأنبياء والمرسلين والملائكة المقربين، فهو الذي يفتح باب الشفاعة لغيره، كما قاله ابن العربي، وفي الصحيحين: «أنا أوَّلُ شافع، وأوَّلُ مُشفّع».
وفي كلام المصنف إشارة إلى واجبات ثلاثة :
فالأول : كونه شافعاً .
والثاني : كونه مُشفّعاً ؛ أي: مقبول الشفاعة.
والثالث: كونه مُقدَّماً على غيره ؛ فإنه حين يشتد الهول، ويتمنى الناس الانصراف ولو للنار، يُلهمون أن الأنبياء هم الواسطة بين الله وخلقه، فيذهبون إلى آدم، فيقولون له : أنت أبو البشر اشفع لنا ، فيقول : لستُ لها لستُ لها، نفسي نفسي، لا أسألُ اليوم غيرها، ويعتذر بالأكل من الشجرة، فيذهبون إلى نوح، ويسألونه الشفاعةَ، فيعتذر لهم ؛ وهكذا ، وبين كل نبي ونبي ألف سنة؛ فلما يذهبون إلى سيدنا محمد ويسألونه الشفاعة، يقول: أنا لها أمتي أمتي ؛ فيسجد تحت العرش، فيُنادى من قبل الله : يا محمد ارفع رأسك، واشفع تشفع؛ فيرفع رأسه ويشفع في فصل القضاء؛ وحينئذ ينفتح باب الشفاعة لغيره؛ وهذه هي الشفاعة العظمى، وهي مختصة به قطعاً، وهي أول المقام المحمود المذكور في قوله تعالى : وعَسَى أَن يَبْعَثَكَ رَبُّكَ مَقَامًا مَّحْمُودًا [الإسراء: ۷۹] ؛ أي: يحمدك فيه الأوّلون والآخرون، وآخره استقرار أهل الجنة في الجنة وأهل النار في النار.
أنواع الشَّفاعات
وله صلى الله عليه وسلم شفاعاتٌ أُخَرُ :
منها شفاعته في إدخال قوم الجنة بغير حساب .
ومنها شفاعته في عدم دخول النار لقوم استحقوا دخولها .
(1) أخرجه الترمذي (٣٦١٦) ، وابن ماجه (٤٣٠٨ ) . والذي في الصحيحين ما أتى به المصنف رحمه الله بعد أسطر .
The obligation of belief in the intercession of the Prophet. He said: 'And obligatory is the intercession of the one whose intercession is accepted.' That is: It is obligatory by revealed law (samʿan) according to Ahl al-Haqq, the intercession of the mushaffaʿ (with fatḥa on the fā'), meaning the one whose intercession is accepted. And if with kasra, it means the one who accepts the intercession of another. Al-Shafāʿa linguistically is the means and request. Technically, it is asking for good from another for another. And the shafāʿa of the Lord (mawlā) is an expression of His forgiveness; for He, exalted, intercedes for whoever says 'There is no god but Allah' and affirms the message of the messenger sent to him, and has not done any good at all, so Allah bestows upon him by not entering the Fire without anyone's intercession. (2) His saying (and the shafāʿa of the Lord) the place of this expression is at the saying of the author: 'and other than Him from the approved righteous.' For the commentator ʿAbd al-Salām mentioned that 'other' includes the Lord, exalted, and there the shafāʿa of the Lord was interpreted as His forgiveness. And as for the shafāʿa mentioned here, it is the intercession of the Prophet. End of Ajhūrī. And his saying: 'Muḥammad' is a substitution for al-mushaffaʿ, to remove its ambiguity. And his saying: 'muqaddaman' meaning: in a state of being foremost over other prophets, messengers, and the closest angels. Thus he is the one who opens the door of intercession for others, as Ibn al-ʿArabī said, and in the Two Ṣaḥīḥs: 'I am the first intercessor and the first whose intercession is accepted.' And in the author's speech is an indication of three obligatory matters: The first: his being an intercessor. The second: his being mushaffaʿ, i.e., accepted intercession. The third: his being foremost over others; for when the terror intensifies, and people wish to depart even to the Fire, they are inspired that the prophets are the intermediaries between Allah and His creation. So they go to Adam and say: You are the father of mankind, intercede for us. He says: I am not for that, I am not for that, myself, myself, I ask nothing today except for myself, and he apologizes with eating from the tree. Then they go to Noah and ask him intercession, and he apologizes to them; and so on, and between each prophet and a prophet is a thousand years. When they go to our master Muḥammad and ask him intercession, he says: I am for that, my nation, my nation. Then he prostrates under the Throne, and it is called from Allah: O Muḥammad, raise your head, intercede and you will be interceded for. So he raises his head and intercedes concerning the judgment of separation (faṣl al-qaḍāʾ). Then the door of intercession opens for others. This is the great intercession (al-shafāʿa al-ʿuẓmā), which is exclusively his definitively, and it is the first part of the praiseworthy station (al-maqām al-maḥmūd) mentioned in His saying: 'And it may be that your Lord will raise you to a praiseworthy station,' meaning: in which the first and last will praise you, and its end is the settling of the people of Paradise in Paradise and the people of the Fire in the Fire. Types of Intercessions. And he, peace and blessings be upon him, has other intercessions: Among them is his intercession for admitting a people to Paradise without account. Among them is his intercession for preventing a people from entering the Fire who deserved to enter it. (1) Recorded by al-Tirmidhī (3616) and Ibn Mājah (4308). And what is in the Two Ṣaḥīḥs is what the author, may Allah have mercy on him, brought after a few lines.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage covers the obligation of believing in the Prophet's intercession. It begins by stating that the intercession of the one whose intercession is accepted (al-mushaffaʿ) is obligatory by revealed law according to Ahl al-Sunna. A linguistic and technical definition of shafāʿa is given: linguistically 'means and request', technically 'asking for good from another for another'. The passage then distinguishes the shafāʿa of the Lord (which is His forgiveness) from the intercession of the Prophet. After clarifying that 'Muḥammad' is a substitution for al-mushaffaʿ and that 'muqaddaman' means foremost over all other prophets and angels, the author extracts three obligatory matters from the verse: (1) the Prophet is an intercessor (shāfiʿ), (2) his intercession is accepted (mushaffaʿ), and (3) he is foremost (muqaddam) over others. The third point is then illustrated by the well-known narration of the great intercession on the Day of Judgment. People go from prophet to prophet seeking intercession, but each declines until they reach Prophet Muḥammad, who accepts and prostrates, then intercedes for the judgment of separation. This is the great intercession (al-shafāʿa al-ʿuẓmā), uniquely his, and it is the first part of the praiseworthy station (al-maqām al-maḥmūd). Finally, other types of his intercessions are listed: intercession for admitting some to Paradise without account, and intercession for preventing some who deserved the Fire from entering it.

Key Terms
شفاعة
المشفع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that intercession means the Prophet can intercede for anyone regardless of faith.
Correction: The passage shows intercession is only for those who affirm tawḥīd and accept the messenger, and it is by Allah's permission.

Checkpoint
What are the three obligatory aspects of the Prophet's intercession indicated in the author's speech?
A) He is a shāfiʿ, mushaffaʿ, and muqaddam.
B) He is a shāfiʿ, he is loved, he is first.
C) He intercedes for all, he is accepted, he is last.
D) He intercedes for prophets, he is accepted, he is foremost.

Key Takeaway
The three obligatory beliefs about the Prophet's intercession are that he intercedes, his intercession is accepted, and he is foremost among all creation in intercession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You say you believe in the Prophet's intercession, but do you live as if it is your only hope, or do you secretly trust in your own deeds?
?
The Prophet is the foremost intercessor—yet how many times today did you send ṣalawāt upon him or ask for his intercession in your duʿā'?
?
If the Prophet's intercession is only for those who affirm 'lā ilāha illā Allāh' with sincerity, what evidence in your daily choices proves that your faith is more than a claim?

Prophethood

The Great Intercession and Other Types of Intercession
Narrates the Great Intercession and lists other types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the narrative of the Great Intercession (al-shafāʿa al-ʿuẓmā) on the Day of Judgment and the other types of intercession granted to the Prophet.

Core Idea
The Prophet's Great Intercession is unique to him, opening the door for all others, and he also intercedes for admission to Paradise and prevention from the Fire.

After establishing the three obligatory aspects, the passage now provides a vivid narration of the Great Intercession on the Day of Judgment, illustrating how the Prophet is the foremost intercessor. It then briefly lists other types of intercession that are part of his honor. This lesson brings the doctrine to life.

Guided Path
1
Read the Great Intercession narrative
Read the Arabic and translation of the story from when the terror intensifies to the Prophet's intercession for final judgment. Notice how each prophet declines until Muhammad accepts.
This story is from authentic hadith (Bukhari and Muslim).
2
Identify what makes it the 'great' intercession
The passage calls it al-shafāʿa al-ʿuẓmā and says it is unique to him. It is the first part of al-maqām al-maḥmūd (the Praiseworthy Station).
3
List the other types of intercession
The passage mentions two other types: intercession for admitting some to Paradise without account, and intercession for preventing some from entering the Fire.
These are mentioned briefly but are part of the Prophet's honors.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why the Prophet is given this unique role and how it relates to his status as the most honored creation.
This reinforces the third aspect of being muqaddam.

The obligation of belief in the intercession of the Prophet. He said: 'And obligatory is the intercession of the one whose intercession is accepted.' That is: It is obligatory by revealed law (samʿan) according to Ahl al-Haqq, the intercession of the mushaffaʿ (with fatḥa on the fā'), meaning the one whose intercession is accepted. And if with kasra, it means the one who accepts the intercession of another. Al-Shafāʿa linguistically is the means and request. Technically, it is asking for good from another for another. The third: his being foremost over others; for when the terror intensifies, and people wish to depart even to the Fire, they are inspired that the prophets are the intermediaries between Allah and His creation. So they go to Adam and say: You are the father of mankind, intercede for us. He says: I am not for that, I am not for that, myself, myself, I ask nothing today except for myself, and he apologizes with eating from the tree. Then they go to Noah and ask him intercession, and he apologizes to them; and so on, and between each prophet and a prophet is a thousand years. When they go to our master Muḥammad and ask him intercession, he says: I am for that, my nation, my nation. Then he prostrates under the Throne, and it is called from Allah: O Muḥammad, raise your head, intercede and you will be interceded for. So he raises his head and intercedes concerning the judgment of separation (faṣl al-qaḍāʾ). Then the door of intercession opens for others. This is the great intercession (al-shafāʿa al-ʿuẓmā), which is exclusively his definitively, and it is the first part of the praiseworthy station (al-maqām al-maḥmūd) mentioned in His saying: 'And it may be that your Lord will raise you to a praiseworthy station,' meaning: in which the first and last will praise you, and its end is the settling of the people of Paradise in Paradise and the people of the Fire in the Fire. Types of Intercessions. And he, peace and blessings be upon him, has other intercessions: Among them is his intercession for admitting a people to Paradise without account. Among them is his intercession for preventing a people from entering the Fire who deserved to enter it. (1) Recorded by al-Tirmidhī (3616) and Ibn Mājah (4308). And what is in the Two Ṣaḥīḥs is what the author, may Allah have mercy on him, brought after a few lines.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage covers the obligation of believing in the Prophet's intercession. It begins by stating that the intercession of the one whose intercession is accepted (al-mushaffaʿ) is obligatory by revealed law according to Ahl al-Sunna. A linguistic and technical definition of shafāʿa is given: linguistically 'means and request', technically 'asking for good from another for another'. The passage then distinguishes the shafāʿa of the Lord (which is His forgiveness) from the intercession of the Prophet. After clarifying that 'Muḥammad' is a substitution for al-mushaffaʿ and that 'muqaddaman' means foremost over all other prophets and angels, the author extracts three obligatory matters from the verse: (1) the Prophet is an intercessor (shāfiʿ), (2) his intercession is accepted (mushaffaʿ), and (3) he is foremost (muqaddam) over others. The third point is then illustrated by the well-known narration of the great intercession on the Day of Judgment. People go from prophet to prophet seeking intercession, but each declines until they reach Prophet Muḥammad, who accepts and prostrates, then intercedes for the judgment of separation. This is the great intercession (al-shafāʿa al-ʿuẓmā), uniquely his, and it is the first part of the praiseworthy station (al-maqām al-maḥmūd). Finally, other types of his intercessions are listed: intercession for admitting some to Paradise without account, and intercession for preventing some who deserved the Fire from entering it.

Key Terms
الشفاعة العظمى
المقام المحمود
شفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Prophet only has one intercession.
Correction: He has multiple: the Great Intercession for judgment, and others for specific groups.

Checkpoint
What is the first part of the Praiseworthy Station (al-maqām al-maḥmūd)?
A) The Great Intercession
B) Intercession for entry to Paradise
C) Intercession for prevention from Fire
D) The Prophet's birth

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's Great Intercession for the final judgment is unique to him and is the first part of the Praiseworthy Station; he also intercedes for admission to Paradise and prevention from the Fire.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet, in his greatest moment, cried out 'my nation, my nation.' Does your daily life reflect that you are truly part of that nation, or do you live as if his concern is not for you?
?
If you were standing on the Day of Judgment, hoping for intercession, would you be among those who know his words and deeds, or would you be a stranger to what he taught?
?
The great intercession is exclusively his; yet do you live with the assumption that you deserve it without effort, or are you actively seeking to be worthy of his plea?

The Three Obligatory Matters of the Prophet's Intercession
The commentator enumerates three obligatory matters of intercession and narrates the great intercession tradition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three obligatory matters related to the Prophet's intercession and the narrative of the great intercession on the Day of Judgment.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession has three dimensions: he intercedes, his intercession is accepted, and he is foremost in interceding.

This lesson unpacks a dense passage from Tuhfat al-Mureed that identifies three essential aspects of the Prophet's intercession (shafa'ah). The commentator also narrates the well-known story of the great intercession, showing how the Prophet ﷺ is the first to intercede and opens the door for others. Understanding these points clarifies the Prophet's unique rank and the nature of intercession in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic text and its English translation carefully. Notice the grammatical clarification and the enumeration of three matters.
The passage begins with a substitution (badal) to remove ambiguity.
2
Identify the three obligatory matters
Find where the commentator lists the three wajibat: being an intercessor (shafi'), having his intercession accepted (mushaffa'), and being foremost (muqaddam). Understand the distinction.
These three are derived from the wording of the matn.
3
Follow the narrative of intercession
Read the story from Adam to the Prophet ﷺ. Notice how each prophet excuses themselves except Muhammad ﷺ, who says 'I am for it.' Reflect on why he is the one to open the door.
The narrative emphasizes his unique role.
4
Connect to the Praiseworthy Station
Understand that this great intercession is the first part of al-maqam al-mahmud mentioned in the Quran. How does this elevate the Prophet's status?
The station ends with the final settlement in Paradise and Hell.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : (مُحَمَّدٍ) بدل من المشفّع، دفع به إبهامه .
وقوله : (مُقَدَّماً) أي: حال كونه مقدَّماً على غيره من الأنبياء والمرسلين والملائكة المقربين، فهو الذي يفتح باب الشفاعة لغيره، كما قاله ابن العربي، وفي الصحيحين: «أنا أوَّلُ شافع، وأوَّلُ مُشفّع (١) .
وفي كلام المصنف إشارة إلى واجبات ثلاثة :
فالأول : كونه شافعاً .
والثاني : كونه مُشفّعاً ؛ أي: مقبول الشفاعة.
والثالث: كونه مُقدَّماً على غيره ؛ فإنه حين يشتد الهول، ويتمنى الناس الانصراف ولو للنار، يُلهمون أن الأنبياء هم الواسطة بين الله وخلقه، فيذهبون إلى آدم، فيقولون له : أنت أبو البشر اشفع لنا ، فيقول : لستُ لها لستُ لها، نفسي نفسي، لا أسألُ اليوم غيرها، ويعتذر بالأكل من الشجرة، فيذهبون إلى نوح، ويسألونه الشفاعةَ، فيعتذر لهم ؛ وهكذا ، وبين كل نبي ونبي ألف سنة؛ فلما يذهبون إلى سيدنا محمد ويسألونه الشفاعة، يقول: أنا لها أمتي أمتي ؛ فيسجد تحت العرش، فيُنادي من قبل الله : يا محمد ارفع رأسك، واشفع تشفع (۲) ؛ فيرفع رأسه ويشفع في فصل : القضاء ؛ وحينئذ ينفتح باب الشفاعة لغيره ؛ وهذه هي به قطعاً، وهي أول المقام المحمود المذكور في قوله تعالى : وعَسَى أَن يَبْعَثَكَ رَبُّكَ مَقَامًا مَّحْمُودًا [الإسراء: ۷۹] ؛ أي: يحمدك فيه الأوّلون والآخرون، وآخره استقرار أهل الجنة في الجنة وأهل النار في النار.
(1) أخرجه الترمذي (٣٦١٦) ، وابن ماجه (٤٣٠٨ ) . والذي في الصحيحين ما أتى به المصنف رحمه الله بعد أسطر .
(۲) أخرجه البخاري (٤٧١٢)، ومسلم (١٩٤).
And His saying: 'Muhammad' is a substitute for 'the intercessor,' he repelled by it (i.e., the substitution) its ambiguity.
And His saying: 'foremost' meaning: in the state of him being foremost over other prophets, messengers, and the near-station angels, for he is the one who opens the door of intercession for others, as Ibn al-'Arabi said, and in the two Sahihs: 'I am the first intercessor, and the first whose intercession is accepted.'
In the author's words is an indication of three obligatory matters:
The first: his being an intercessor.
The second: his being one whose intercession is accepted; i.e., accepted of intercession.
The third: his being foremost over others; for when the terror intensifies, and people wish to depart even to the Fire, they are inspired that the prophets are the intermediaries between Allah and His creation, so they go to Adam, and they say to him: 'You are the father of mankind, intercede for us,' so he says: 'I am not for that, I am not for that, myself, myself, I ask not today except for myself,' and he excuses himself by eating from the tree, then they go to Noah, and ask him for intercession, and he excuses himself; and so on, and between each prophet and a prophet is a thousand years; then when they go to our master Muhammad and ask him for intercession, he says: 'I am for it, my ummah, my ummah,' so he prostrates under the Throne, and it is called out from Allah: 'O Muhammad, raise your head, and intercede, and you will be granted intercession'; so he raises his head and intercedes concerning the judgment; and at that moment the door of intercession opens for others; and this is the great intercession, exclusively for him, and it is the first of the Praiseworthy Station mentioned in the saying of the Exalted: 'And perhaps your Lord will raise you to a Praiseworthy Station' [al-Isra:79]; meaning: the first and the last will praise you in it, and its end is the settling of the people of Paradise in Paradise and the people of Hell in Hell.
(1) Narrated by al-Tirmidhi (3616) and Ibn Majah (4308). And what is in the two Sahihs is what the author (may Allah have mercy on him) brought after a few lines.
(2) Narrated by al-Bukhari (4712) and Muslim (194).
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the matn's mention of the Prophet's intercession. The commentator first clarifies grammatical points: the word 'Muhammad' is a substitute for 'al-mushaffa'' (the one whose intercession is accepted), removing ambiguity. Then he explains 'muqaddaman' (foremost) meaning he is ahead of all other prophets and angels in opening the door of intercession, citing Ibn al-'Arabi and a hadith from the Sahihayn. He then points out that the author's words imply three obligatory matters (wajibat): (1) being a shafi' (intercessor), (2) being mushaffa' (accepted intercessor), (3) being muqaddam (foremost). He elaborates on the third by recounting the well-known tradition of intercession on the Day of Judgment: people go to Adam, Noah, etc., each excusing themselves, until they come to the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ, who says 'I am for it, my ummah,' prostrates under the Throne, and is commanded to intercede. At that point he intercedes for judgment, and the door of intercession opens for others. This is the great intercession (al-shafa'ah al-'uzma) exclusively for him, and it is the first part of the Praiseworthy Station (al-maqam al-mahmud) mentioned in Surah al-Isra'. The end of that station is the settlement of the peoples in their eternal abodes.

Key Terms
شفاعة
شافع
مشفّع
مقدَّم
المقام المحمود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's intercession is a single simple act; he only intercedes once.
Correction: The passage shows three distinct aspects: being an intercessor, having his intercession accepted, and being foremost. Additionally, the narrative reveals that his intercession for judgment is the first, opening the door for others.

Checkpoint

A) شافع، مشفع، مقدم
B) شافع، مقبول الشفاعة، مقدم
C) شفاعة عظمى، شفاعة في أهل الكبائر، شفاعة في زيادة الدرجات
D) إدخال قوم الجنة، عدم دخول النار، إخراج الموحدين

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad ﷺ is uniquely the first intercessor, his intercession is accepted, and he is foremost in opening the door of intercession for others, which constitutes the first part of the Praiseworthy Station.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet ﷺ said, 'I am for it, my ummah, my ummah.' Have you ever sincerely asked yourself: Am I truly part of his ummah in a way that he would recognize? What proof is there in your daily life that you belong to him, not just by name, but by obedience and love?
?
When you think of the terror of that Day, and how even the prophets were preoccupied with their own selves ('myself, myself'), where does your hope for salvation actually lie? Is it in your own deeds, or do you genuinely rely on the intercession that only the Prophet ﷺ can initiate? Be honest: does your heart feel that reliance or is it just a belief you hold?
?
The other prophets excused themselves from interceding because of their sins. If you were in their position, would you have any excuse? This teaches that intercession is not a right, but a gift. What does that tell you about your own accountability? Are you living as if you deserve intercession, or as if you are utterly in need of Allah's mercy through His Prophet?

Types of the Prophet's Minor Intercessions
Enumeration of the Prophet's minor intercessions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the types of intercession specific to the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ beyond the great intercession.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession comes in multiple forms, each for a different purpose.

This passage from the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid lists the various intercessions that are unique to the Prophet ﷺ. After affirming that the great intercession (al-shafa'ah al-'uzma) is exclusively his, it goes on to enumerate other intercessions, each with a distinct purpose. As you read, note how these intercessions cover different aspects of salvation and elevation in the Hereafter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the meaning. Notice the numbered list structure.
The passage begins by restating the special status of the great intercession.
2
Identify each type of intercession
Locate the five categories mentioned: entry without account, exemption from Fire, removal from Fire, increase in ranks, and other unspecified intercessions.
Each type is introduced with 'ومنها' meaning 'among them'.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why multiple intercessions are needed. What does this tell us about the Prophet's mercy and the diversity of people's states in the Hereafter?
This shows the comprehensiveness of the Prophet's role as an intercessor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشفاعة العظمي، وهي مختصة به قطعاً
أنواع الشَّفاعات
وله صلى الله عليه وسلم شفاعاتٌ أَخَرُ :
منها شفاعته في إدخال قوم الجنة بغير حساب .
ومنها شفاعته في عدم دخول النار لقومِ استحقُوا دخولها .
ومنها شفاعته في إخراج الموحدين من النار.
ومنها شفاعته في زيادة الدرجات في الجنة لأهلها
ومنها غير ذلك كما ذكره السيوطي وغيره.
The great intercession, and it is exclusively for him definitively.
Types of intercessions:
And for him, peace be upon him, other intercessions:
Among them: his intercession in admitting a people to Paradise without account.
And among them: his intercession in non-entry into the Fire for a people who deserved entry into it.
And among them: his intercession in removing the monotheists from the Fire.
And among them: his intercession in increasing ranks in Paradise for its people.
And among them: other than that, as mentioned by al-Suyuti and others.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage classifies the types of intercessions of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ. It first reaffirms that the great intercession (al-shafa'ah al-'uzma) is exclusively for him, unequivocally. Then it enumerates other intercessions specific to him: (1) intercession for a group to enter Paradise without being called to account, (2) intercession for a group who deserved entry into the Fire to not enter it, (3) intercession for monotheists (muwahhidun) to be removed from the Fire, (4) intercession for increasing ranks in Paradise for its inhabitants, and (5) other intercessions not detailed, citing al-Suyuti and others.

Key Terms

إدخال الجنة بغير حساب
عدم دخول النار
إخراج الموحدين
زيادة الدرجات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's intercession is only the great intercession.
Correction: This passage shows that the Prophet has multiple intercessions beyond the great intercession, including for entry without account, exemption from Fire, removal from Fire, and increase of ranks.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What specific sins or attachments might prevent you from receiving that mercy, and how will you turn away from them starting today?
?
The Prophet ﷺ has intercessions to remove monotheists from the Fire. Yet, do you rely on this hope to be careless with your major sins? Be honest: is there a sin you keep committing because you think ‘I’m a believer, so eventually the Prophet will save me’? What step will you take this week to repent from it sincerely?
?
Among the intercessions is an increase in ranks in Paradise. But growth in rank requires deeds. Are you content with your current level of faith? If you were to die tonight, what single change could you make tomorrow that would raise your rank, not out of arrogance, but out of love for His mercy?

Intercession of Other Righteous Beings
Commentary on intercession by approved righteous beings and angelic order.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that intercession is not exclusive to the Prophet but includes other approved righteous beings according to their ranks, with a specific order for angels.

Core Idea
Many righteous beings intercede for major sinners by Allah's permission, each according to their rank.

This passage expands the concept of intercession beyond the Prophet, listing various categories of righteous beings who intercede for people of major sins. It also specifies the sequential intercession of angels, from Jibril to the nineteen guardians of Hell. This understanding is grounded in textual evidence and Sunni consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the poetic meter reference (sukun on 'ayn for weight).
2
Identify the categories of intercessors
The passage lists several categories: prophets, messengers, angels, Companions, martyrs, acting scholars, and saints. List them and note that they intercede for people of major sins.
The term 'murtaḍā al-akhyār' refers to those Allah has approved.
3
Understand the angelic intercession order
The passage states that angels intercede sequentially: first Jibril, last the nineteen angels over the Fire. Reflect on why this order matters.
The nineteen angels are mentioned in Quran 74:30.
4
Grasp the condition and evidence
Note that intercession occurs only after the punishment period ends, and that this is established by texts and Sunni consensus.
This clarifies that intercession does not prevent punishment entirely but ends it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وغَيْرُهُ مِنْ مُرْتَضَى الأَخْيَارِ يَشْفَعْ بسكون العين للوزن؛ أي: وغيره ممن ارتضاه الله تعالى من الأخيار ؛ كالأنبياء والمرسلين والملائكة والصحابة والشهداء والعلماء العاملين والأولياء يشفعُ في أرباب الكبائر على قدر مقامه عند الله تعالى وشفاعة الملائكة على الترتيب ؛ فأولهم في الشفاعة جبريلُ، وآخرهم فيها التسعة عشر التي على النار .
وقوله : كَمَا قَدْ جاءَ في الأَخْبَارِ) أي : للنص الذي قد جاء في الأخبار الدالَّةِ على ذلك، كما أجمع عليه أهل السنة، ولا يشفع أحد ممن ذُكر إلا بعد انتهاء مُدَّة المؤاخذة.
His saying: 'And other than him from the approved righteous ones will intercede' — with sukun on the 'ayn for meter; i.e., and other than him from those whom Allah the Exalted has approved from the righteous, such as the prophets, messengers, angels, Companions, martyrs, acting scholars, and saints, they intercede for the people of major sins according to their rank with Allah the Exalted. And the intercession of the angels is sequential; so the first of them in intercession is Jibril, and the last of them are the nineteen (angels) who are over the Fire.
And His saying: 'as has come in the reports' — i.e., according to the text that has come in the reports indicating that, as the Ahl al-Sunnah have agreed upon, and none of those mentioned intercedes except after the completion of the period of punishment.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage explains that intercession is not limited to the Prophet; other approved righteous individuals (murtaḍā al-akhyār) also intercede. The commentator lists categories: prophets, messengers, angels, Companions, martyrs, active scholars, and saints. They intercede for people of major sins (arbāb al-kabā'ir) according to their rank with Allah. The angels intercede in a specific order: first Jibril, and last the nineteen angels assigned over the Fire (mentioned in Qur'an 74:30). The passage emphasizes that this is established by texts and agreed upon by Ahl al-Sunnah, and that no intercession occurs from these except after the period of punishment (muddat al-mu'ākhadhah) has ended.

Key Terms
مرتضى الأخيار
أرباب الكبائر
الملائكة التسعة عشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) can intercede on the Day of Judgment.
Correction: According to this passage, many other righteous beings such as prophets, angels, Companions, martyrs, scholars, and saints also intercede, each according to their rank, and this is supported by texts and Sunni consensus.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Intercession on Judgment Day is not exclusive to the Prophet; many righteous beings intercede for major sinners, with angels interceding in a specific sequence, all by Allah's permission and after the punishment period ends.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that intercession only comes after punishment has begun, how does this change your view of your own major sins? Are you relying on someone else's intercession to escape punishment entirely, or are you actively seeking Allah's forgiveness now?

The Prophet ﷺ and other righteous beings will intercede for the people of major sins. Has this lesson made you complacent about sinning, or has it increased your urgency to repent before that Day? Be honest with yourself.
